Murahiq's Tahlil: Hanafi Position and Maliki Dispute
Hanafi ruling with proof and Maliki opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a murahiq performing tahlil, explain the Hanafi proof, and compare it with the Maliki position to identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A murahiq capable of intercourse can perform tahlil — penetration, not ejaculation, is the key.

This passage tackles a disputed point: can a boy on the verge of puberty (murahiq) serve as the second husband to make a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband? The Hanafi school says yes, based on the condition of penetration alone. Imam Malik disagrees, requiring ejaculation. Let's follow the Hanafi proof and the response to the Maliki objection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
A murahiq (boy near puberty who can engage in intercourse) can perform tahlil if he has valid marriage and penetration. He is treated like an adult for this purpose.
The condition is dukhul, not puberty in itself.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Malik holds that tahlil requires ejaculation (inzal), which a murahiq cannot produce. Hence, his tahlil is invalid.
Maliki school: dukhul alone is insufficient.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Quranic condition is 'until she marries another husband' and hadith specify dukhul. There is no textual requirement for inzal. A murahiq capable of intercourse fulfills dukhul.
Proof is purely textual (dalil naqli).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the condition is the meeting of circumcised parts, which triggers ghusl for the woman. This shows dukhul is sufficient. Inzal is not mentioned in the primary texts.
Ghusl obligation on the woman without inzal confirms the point.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In Hanafi school, the woman becomes lawful for her first husband after murahiq's tahlil. In Maliki, she remains unlawful, so she cannot remarry her first husband.
This directly affects the woman's marital status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وہ بچہ قریب البلوغ ہو وہ حلالہ کرنے میں بالغ کی طرح ہے۔ نکاح صحیح میں دخول کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور یہی شرط ہے نص حدیث سے اور مراہق کے مسئلہ میں امام مالک ہمارے مخالف ہیں اور ان کے خلاف حجت وہی دلیل ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں مراہق کی تفسیر کی اور کہا کہ لڑکا جو بالغ نہیں ہوا حالانکہ ایسا لڑکا جماع کر سکتا ہے۔ اس نے کسی عورت سے جماع کیا تو اس عورت پر غسل واجب ہوگا اور اس عورت کو پہلے شوہر پر حلال کر دیا اور (امام محمد کے ) اس کلام کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کا عضو تناسل حرکت کرتا اور خواہش کرتا ہو اور عورت ہی پر غسل واجب ہوا دونوں ختان کے مل جانے کی وجہ سے اور یہی عورت کی منی اترنے کا سبب ہے اور (غسل) واجب کرنے کی ضرورت صرف عورت کے حق میں ہے لیکن ( مراہق ) لڑکے پر غسل (واجب) نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کو عادت ڈالنے کے لئے حکم دیا جائے گا۔
A boy who is near puberty is like an adult in performing tahlil. Because penetration occurs in a valid marriage, and this is the condition from the text of hadith. In the issue of the murahiq, Imam Malik is opposed to us, and against him the proof is the same proof we have mentioned. Imam Muhammad explained in al-Jami' al-Saghir the definition of murahiq: a boy who has not reached puberty, yet such a boy can engage in intercourse. If he has intercourse with a woman, ghusl becomes obligatory upon that woman, and she becomes lawful for the first husband. The meaning of his words are: his penis moves and desires, and ghusl is obligatory only upon the woman due to the meeting of the two circumcised parts, and this is the cause of the descent of the woman's fluid. The need for ghusl is only regarding the woman. As for the murahiq, ghusl is not obligatory upon him, although he may be commanded to do it to form a habit.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. It states that a murahiq (a boy on the verge of puberty) can serve as the second husband (muhallil) who makes a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband, just like an adult. The condition is penetration (dukhul) in a valid marriage, as derived from the Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' and the hadith. Imam Malik disagrees, requiring ejaculation, which a murahiq cannot produce. The Hanafi response maintains that the condition is penetration alone, relying on the same evidence. Imam Muhammad's definition in al-Jami' al-Saghir specifies that the murahiq must be capable of intercourse, with his organ moving and desiring. The ruling about ghusl: if such a boy has intercourse, the woman must perform ghusl due to the meeting of circumcised parts, but the boy is not obligated because he is not yet legally responsible (mukallaf). However, he may be instructed to perform ghusl for training.

Key Terms
مراہق (murahiq): A boy who has not reached puberty but is capable of intercourse, with his organ moving and desiring.
حلالہ (tahlil): The act of marrying a thrice-divorced woman and consummating the marriage so she becomes lawful for her first husband.
دخول (dukhul): Penetration, i.e., the meeting of circumcised parts (i.e., intercourse).
انزال (inzal): Ejaculation (emission of seminal fluid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for a murahiq's tahlil to be valid?
A) He must have reached puberty.
B) He must be capable of ejaculation.
C) He must perform penetration in a valid marriage.
D) He must be ordered by a guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a murahiq's tahlil based on the condition of penetration, rejecting the Maliki requirement of ejaculation.

Master's Intercourse with Slave Girl and the Tahlil Condition Dispute
Ruling that master's intercourse does not enable tahlil, followed by intra-Hanafi dispute on tahlil condition marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on a marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for each.

Core Idea
Marriage with the condition of tahlil is valid but disliked; three Hanafi imams differ on whether tahlil is effective.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, with commentary from Al-Hidayah, presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins with a related but distinct ruling: a master's intercourse with his own slave girl does not make her lawful for her former husband because the Quran requires marriage to a 'husband' (zawj), and a master is not a husband. The core issue then shifts to a more controversial scenario: a man marries a woman explicitly conditioning that he will make her lawful (tahlil) for her first husband. All imams agree the condition makes the marriage disliked, but they split on its validity and effect. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi usul handles conditions that contradict the contract's purpose.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial ruling
Identify why a master's intercourse with his slave girl does not enable tahlil. The key is that the Quran requires marriage to a 'zawj' (husband), and a master is not a husband.
This sets the stage for the main dispute by highlighting the importance of the marriage contract.
2
Identify the disputed scenario
The passage now discusses a woman who marries a man with the explicit condition that he will divorce her so she can remarry her first husband. This is the tahlil condition.
All Hanafi imams agree this marriage is disliked (makruh) due to the hadith cursing muhallil.
3
Learn the three positions
Three opinions: Abu Hanifa holds the marriage is valid (sahih) and tahlil effective. Abu Yusuf holds the marriage is invalid (fasid). Muhammad holds the marriage is valid but tahlil ineffective as punishment.
Focus on the reasoning behind each: Abu Hanifa: condition does not invalidate; Abu Yusuf: resembles mut'ah; Muhammad: analogy to killing the testator.
4
Examine the proofs
The hadith of cursing is the primary dalil. Each imam interprets it differently: Abu Hanifa sees it as affecting sin, not validity; Abu Yusuf sees it as invalidating; Muhammad sees it as a penalty.
Also note the qiyas used by Muhammad (killer of testator) and Abu Yusuf (temporary marriage).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical outcome
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the marriage is valid and tahlil effective. Therefore, if the husband consummates and divorces, the woman becomes lawful for her first husband. The condition itself is sinful but does not affect validity.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدری نے فرمایا کہ مولیٰ کا اپنی باندی سے وطی کرنا اس کو حلال نہیں کرے گا، کیونکہ غایت نکاح زوج ہے اور اگر کسی عورت کو تحلیل کی شرط کے ساتھ نکاح میں لیا تو ( یہ ) نکاح مکروہ ہے۔ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے فرمان لعن اللہ الحدیث کی وجہ سے یعنی اللہ لعنت کرے حلالہ کرنے والے کو اور جس کے لئے حلالہ کیا گیا اور یہی اس حدیث کا عمل ہے۔ پھر اگر اس نے وطی کے بعد اس عورت کو. طلاق دیدی تو اول شوہر کے واسطے حلال ہو جائے گی کیونکہ دخول کرنا نکاح صحیح میں پایا گیا اس لئے کہ شرط سے نکاح باطل نہیں ہوتا اور ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ نکاح فاسد ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ نکاح موقت کے معنی میں ہے اور اس کو حلال نہیں کرے گا اول پر نکاح کے فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ نکاح تو صحیح ہو جائے گا اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور زوج اول پر اس کو حلال نہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ شریعت نے جس چیز کو موخر کیا تھا اس نے اس کو جلدی کر لیا پس اس کو بدلہ دیا جائے گا اس کے مقصود کو روک کر ، جیسا کہ مورث کو قتل کرنے میں ۔
Al-Quduri said: The master's intercourse with his slave girl will not make her lawful, because the goal (of the verse) is marriage to a husband. And if a woman is married with the condition of tahlil, then this marriage is disliked due to the Prophet's saying: 'Allah curses the one who performs tahlil and the one for whom tahlil is performed.' This is the application of the hadith. Then if he divorces her after intercourse, she becomes lawful for the first husband because penetration occurred in a valid marriage, for a condition does not invalidate a marriage. It is reported from Abu Yusuf that the marriage becomes invalid (fasid) because it is like a temporary marriage, and it does not make her lawful for the first due to its invalidity. It is reported from Muhammad that the marriage is valid for the reason we mentioned, but it does not make her lawful for the first husband because he hastened what the Law delayed, so he is punished by denial of his objective, as in the case of killing the testator.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of a marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil. It first states the general ruling: a master's intercourse with his own slave girl does not make her lawful for her previous husband, because the Quranic condition (nikah zawj) requires marriage, and a master is not considered a husband. Then it discusses a different scenario: if a man marries a woman explicitly conditioning that he will make her lawful for her first husband, the marriage is disliked (makruh) according to all, due to the hadith cursing the muhallil and the muhallal lahu. However, there are three opinions on its validity and effect: 1) Abu Hanifa (the matn author): The marriage is sahih despite the condition; the condition does not invalidate it. Therefore, if he consummates and divorces, she becomes lawful for the first husband because a valid nikah with dukhul occurred. 2) Abu Yusuf: The marriage is fasid (invalid) because the condition makes it resemble a temporary marriage (mut'ah). Hence, it does not make her lawful. 3) Muhammad: The marriage itself is sahih because it contains all essential elements, but it does not make her lawful for the first husband as a punishment for hastening what should be delayed (i.e., intending divorce). This is analogous to a killer who inherits from his victim: he is prevented from inheritance as a punishment. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa: the marriage is valid and if consummated and then divorces, tahlil is effective, though the act is still sinful and disliked.

Key Terms
مولی (mawla): Master of a slave girl; owner.
نکاح مکروہ (nikah makruh): A marriage that is disliked (makruh) due to the condition of tahlil, but not necessarily invalid.
مورث کو قتل کرنے میں (maurith ko qatl karne mein): Analogy: A killer of a testator is prevented from inheritance as punishment; similarly, one who marries with condition of tahlil is prevented from its benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa), what is the ruling on a marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil?
A) The marriage is invalid (batil) and does not make the woman lawful.
B) The marriage is valid (sahih) and tahlil is effective if consummated and divorced.
C) The marriage is valid but tahlil is ineffective as punishment.
D) The marriage is fasid and must be annulled.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that a marriage with the condition of tahlil is valid and effective, but the condition itself is sinful and makes the marriage disliked.

Effect of Second Marriage on Prior Divorces: Shaykhayn vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of second marriage on prior divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether the second husband destroys less than three divorces, identify the proofs of Shaykhayn and Muhammad, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The second husband resets the divorce count to zero, giving the first husband three new divorces — even if only one or two were given initially.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does a second marriage wipe out the effect of fewer than three prior divorces? The ruling has significant practical consequences for remarriage possibilities. We will explore the positions of Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad, their proofs from Quran and Hadith, and the relied-upon position in the school.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
A free woman is given one or two divorces by her first husband. After her iddah ends, she marries another man, consummates the marriage, and then divorces. After completing her iddah from the second husband, she returns to the first husband.
The second marriage is valid and consummated.
2
Identify the disagreement
Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the second husband destroys all prior divorces, so the first husband regains the right to give three new divorces. Imam Muhammad holds that the second husband only destroys when three divorces were given; if less, the first husband retains the remaining number (e.g., if one was given, he can give two).
Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i agree with Muhammad.
3
Analyze Muhammad's proof
Muhammad cites the Quranic verse "فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غيره" (If he divorces her, she is not permissible for him after that until she marries another husband). The word 'حتى' indicates a limit (ghayah) for the severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah). Since severe prohibition only arises after three divorces, the second marriage cannot be a limit for fewer than three.
Thus, the second husband's role as terminator only applies when three divorces were given.
4
Analyze Shaykhayn's proof
Shaykhayn rely on the hadith "لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له" (Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done). The Prophet called the second husband 'muhallil', meaning the one who establishes permissibility (halal). This establishes a new, complete permissibility, which is only achieved by having three new divorces. Therefore, the second husband destroys all prior divorces, regardless of their number.
The new permissibility must be complete (kamil), not the previous incomplete one.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Shaykhayn: the second husband destroys all prior divorces, giving the first husband three new divorces. This is supported by the hadith and the reasoning of a complete new permissibility.
Imam Muhammad's view, though respected, is not followed for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرہ کو ایک یا دو طلاقین وید میں عورت کی عدت گذر چکی اور دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کر لیا پھر پہلے شوہر کے پاس لوٹ آئی تو تین طلاق کے ساتھ لوٹے گی
واذا طلق الحرة تطليقة او تطليقتين وانقضت عدتها وتزوجت بزوج أخر ثم عادت الى الزوج الأول عادت بثلث تطليقات ويهدم الزوج الثانى مادون الثلث كما يهدم الثلث وهذا عندابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لا يهدم مادون الثلث لأنه غاية للحرمة بالنص فيكون منهيا ولا انهاء للحرمة قبل الثبوت ولهما قوله عليه السلام لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له سماه محللا وهو المثبت للحل

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی آزاد بیوی کو ایک طلاق دی یا دو طلاقیں دیں اور اس عورت کی عدت گزرگئی ۔ پھر اس عورت نے دوسرے شوہر کے ساتھ نکاح کر لیا اور پھر دوسرے شوہر کی طلاق اور عدت سے فراغت پا کر پہلے شوہر کے پاس آگئی تو یہ عورت پہلے شوہر کے پاس تین طلاقوں کے ساتھ واپس آئے گی یعنی زوج اول از سر نو تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہوگا اور زوج ثانی تین طلاقوں سے کم ایک اور دو کو اسی طرح منہدم کر دیتا ہے جس طرح تین کو یہ مذہب شیخین کا ہے اور امام حمد کامذہب یہ ہے کہ زوج ثانی تین طلاقوں سے کم کو منہدم نہیں کرتا بلکہ زوج اول مابقی من الثلاث کا مالک رہے گا یعنی اگر پہلے ایک طلاق دے چکا تو اب باقی دو زوجا غیرہ میں لا تحل له سے حرمت غلیظہ مراد ہے اور اس حرمت غلیظہ کی غایت اور نہایت زوج ثانی سے نکاح کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ احتمی غایت کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے اور مغیا غایت کے ساتھ منتہی اور ختم ہو جاتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ زوج ثانی سے نکاح کرنا حرمت غلیظہ کو ختم کرنے والا ہے اور حرمت غلیظہ کے ثبوت سے پہلے حرمت کو ختم کرنے کے کوئی معنی ہی نہیں ہیں۔ لہذا تین طلاقوں سے کم کی صورت میں زوج ثانی کا وطی کرنا غیر معتبر ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں حرمت غلیظہ ثابت نہیں ہے اور جب اس صورت میں حرمت غلیظہ ثابت نہیں ہے تو زوج ثانی کا وطی کرنا اس کے لئے غایت نہیں ہو سکتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زوج ثانی تین طلاقوں سے کم کو منہدم نہیں کرتا اور جب تین سے کم منہدم نہیں ہوتیں تو زوج اول نکاح ثانی کے بعد تین طلاقوں کا مالک نہیں ہو گا بلکہ پہلی بار طلاق دینے کے بعد جو باقی رہ گئی تھی اس کا مالک ہو گا ایک ہو یا دو ہوں۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له ، اس حدیث سے وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ محدثین اس کو باب ماجاء في الزوج الثانی کے تحت بیان کرتے ہیں۔ پس محلل سے مراد زوج ثانی ہوگا گو یا حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے زوج ثانی کا نام حلل رکھا ہے اور محلل کے معنی مثبت محل کے ہیں اب رہی یہ بات کہ زوج نانی کی وجہ سے جو خلت ثابت ہوگی وہ حل سابق ہے یا حل جدید حل سابق تو ہو نہیں سکتی ورنہ تحصیل حاصل لازم آئے گا پس حل جدید کا ہونا متعین ہو گیا اور یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ حل جد ید اول کا غیر ہو اور اول حل ناقص ہے۔ لہذا حصل جدید کامل ہوگی اور کامل حالت ہوتی ہے تین طلاقوں سے پس ثابت ہوا کہ زوج نانی زوج اول کے لئے ازسرنو تین طلاقیں ثابت کر دیتا ہے خواہ زوج اول نے تین طلاقیں دی ہوں یا تین سے کم دی ہوں دونوں برابر ہیں۔
If a free woman is given one or two divorces, her iddah passes, she marries another husband, then returns to the first husband, she returns with three divorces. The second husband destroys less than three just as he destroys three. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He does not destroy less than three because he is the limit (ghayah) of prohibition by the text, so he is the terminator, and there is no termination of prohibition before its establishment. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' He called him muhallil, and he is the one who establishes permissibility. Translation and explanation follow.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of a second marriage on the number of divorces a first husband can give when he has given less than three divorces. The example: a free woman is given one or two divorces, her iddah ends, she marries another man (zawj thani), then after his divorce and her iddah, she returns to her first husband. According to Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the second husband 'destroys' (yahdim) the previous divorces, meaning the first husband regains the right to give three new divorces. According to Imam Muhammad, the second husband only destroys when all three divorces were given; if less, the first husband retains the remaining number (if he gave one, he now can give two; if two, he can give one). This is also the view of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. The proof for Shaykhayn is the hadith 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done' — the second husband is called 'muhallil,' which means 'the one who establishes permissibility.' The new permissibility is a complete, new permissibility, which is only possible with three divorces. Muhammad's proof is the Quranic verse 'فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غيره' — 'if he divorces her, she is not halal for him until she marries another husband.' The second marriage is the limit (ghayah) for the severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah). Since severe prohibition only arises after three divorces, the second husband cannot be the limit for less than three. The commentary elaborates that the second marriage creates a new complete permissibility (hal jadid kamil), which requires three divorces to exhaust. Thus, the first husband gets three new divorces regardless of the number given before.

Key Terms
یہدم (yahdim): The second husband 'destroys' the effect of previous divorces, meaning the first husband regains the right to give three new divorces.
حرمت غلیظہ (hurmah ghalizah): The severe prohibition that occurs after three irrevocable divorces (talaq ba'in baynuna kubra), which can only be removed by the woman marrying another husband and consummating.
محلل (muhallil): The second husband who, by marriage and consummation, makes the woman halal for her first husband after three divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Shaykhayn), what happens if a man divorces his wife once, her iddah ends, she marries another man, consummates, and then returns to the first husband?
A) The first husband can give only two more divorces.
B) The first husband can give three new divorces.
C) The marriage is invalid and the woman is not halal.
D) The first husband retains no right to divorce.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the second husband destroys all prior divorces, giving the first husband three new ones, based on the hadith of muhallil and the logic of a complete new permissibility.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner

Trusting a Woman’s Claim About ʿIddah and Remarriage
Ruling on when the first husband may believe the woman's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a husband may believe his wife's claim regarding iddah and remarriage after three divorces, and apply these conditions to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
A husband may trust his wife's claim about iddah and remarriage only if time permits and he is reasonably convinced.

When a man divorces his wife three times, she cannot return to him until she marries another man, is divorced, and completes two iddah periods. In many cases, the first husband cannot verify her claims about these events. This lesson explains when he is allowed to accept her word alone, relying on his predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) and the feasibility of the timeline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A man has given his wife three divorces. The woman claims her first iddah ended, she married another man, he consummated and divorced her, and her second iddah has also passed. She wishes to remarry the first husband.
This is a specific post-triple divorce remarriage case.
2
State the general ruling
The husband may believe her statement, meaning it is permissible for him to marry her based on her word alone.
The text says 'jāz' (it is permissible).
3
Extract the first condition: adequate time
The period since the first divorce must be sufficient for all the claimed events (her iddah, new marriage, consummation, second divorce, second iddah) to have realistically occurred.
The minimum period is disputed among scholars and will be explained later.
4
Extract the second condition: predominant belief (ghalabat al-zann)
The husband must have a strong personal conviction that she is truthful, not merely an assumption or doubt.
This is based on the principle that a mu'amalah or religious matter can rely on a single person's statement when the truth is hard to verify.
5
Understand the legal basis
The ruling is justified because the matter involves both worldly transaction (mu'amalah) and religious permissibility (tahrim and tahlil). The statement of one person is accepted in such matters when not repugnant to common sense.
No specific Qur'an or hadith is cited here; it is a juristic inference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کو تین طلاقیں دیں عورت نے کہا میری عدت گذر چکی اور دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کیا اور اس نے دخول کیا اور طلاق دیدی اور میری عدت گذر چکی اس سے شوہر اول کیلئے کب نکاح کرنا جائز ہے
واذاطلقها ثلثا فقالت قد انقضت عدتى وتزوجت ودخل بي الزوج وطلقنى و انقضت عدتى والمدة تحتمل ذالک جاز للزوج ان يصدقها اذا كان فى غالب ظنه انها صادقة لانه معاملة او امر ديني لتعلق الحل به وقول الواحد فيهما مقبول وهو غير مستنكر اذا كانت المدة تحتمله و اختلفوا فى ادنى هذه المدة وسنبينها
The woman was given three divorces. She said: 'My iddah has passed, I married another husband, he consummated with me, and he divorced me, and my iddah passed.' If the time period permits that, then it is permissible for the husband to believe her if it is his predominant opinion that she is truthful, because it is a transaction or a religious matter due to the connection of permissibility to it. And the statement of a single person in both matters is accepted and it is not objectionable if the time period permits it. And they differed regarding the minimum of this period, which we will clarify.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the permissibility of a husband believing his wife regarding her iddah and remarriage after he has given her three divorces. The scenario: the husband divorces his wife three times. The woman claims that her iddah has ended, she married another man, he consummated, divorced her, and her second iddah also ended. She wishes to return to the first husband. The ruling: the first husband may believe her if the time period (since the first divorce) is sufficient for all these events to have occurred, and if his dominant opinion is that she is truthful. The reason is that this is a matter both of worldly transaction (mu'amalah) and religious concern, since permissibility (halal) depends on it. The statement of a single woman is accepted in such matters as long as the time allows and it is not contrary to assumption. The scholars differed on the minimum period required, which the author says will be explained later.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death of the husband, during which a woman cannot remarry. For a divorced woman, it is three menstrual cycles (quru') or three months if she does not menstruate.
غلبة ظن (ghalabat al-zann): The predominant opinion or reasonable belief that a statement is true, based on circumstantial evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When may a husband who has given his wife three divorces believe her claim that her iddah has ended and she remarried and was divorced again?
A) At any time, regardless of the time elapsed.
B) Only if the time period permits such events and he believes she is truthful.
C) Only if she provides witnesses.
D) Never, because she is not trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The first husband may trust his wife’s claim about iddah and remarriage after triple divorce only when the timeline is feasible and he genuinely believes her.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Does a Second Husband Reset Less Than Three Divorces?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of second husband on less than three divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two opposing views within the Hanafi school (Shaykhayn vs. Imam Abu Hanifa) regarding the effect of a second husband on fewer than three divorces, explain the proofs for each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Second husband resets the count to three for the Shaykhayn; only resets if three were given according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Shaykhayn). The question is whether a second husband's marriage completely nullifies the effect of prior divorces, restoring the first husband's right to all three divorces, or whether it only does so when three divorces were initially given. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly determining the number of divorces a husband may give after a wife's intervening marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the core question
Read the passage to understand the factual scenario: a woman divorced once or twice, completes iddah, marries another man, consummates, gets divorced, then returns to her first husband. The core question: does the second husband's marriage reset the first husband's divorce count to three, or does the first husband retain only the remaining divorces?
This scenario only applies to a free wife (not a slave) and assumes both marriages were valid.
2
State the two positions
Identify and clearly articulate the two positions: (1) Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the second husband destroys all previous divorces, giving the first husband three new divorces. (2) Imam Abu Hanifa (and Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i): the second husband only destroys the severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) which only occurs after three divorces; thus for one or two divorces, the first husband retains the remaining divorces (one or two).
3
Examine the proof of Imam Muhammad (for the Shaykhayn)
Imam Muhammad (one of the Shaykhayn) uses Quran 2:230: 'And if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him thereafter until she marries another husband.' He argues that 'hata' (until) indicates a limit (ghayah) that applies only to severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah). Since severe prohibition only exists after three divorces, the second husband's marriage only resets when three were given. For less, there is no severe prohibition to terminate, so no reset.
This proof focuses on the existence of the prohibition. If no severe prohibition existed, the limit has no effect.
4
Examine the proof of the Shaykhayn (from hadith)
The Shaykhayn cite the hadith: 'May Allah curse the muhallil and the one for whom tahleel is done.' They argue that 'muhallil' refers to the second husband because he establishes halaliyyah (lawfulness) anew. This new halaliyyah must be complete (since it cannot be the previous deficient one), and completeness is only achieved with three divorces. Therefore, the second husband always establishes a new three-divorce capacity, regardless of the prior count.
The hadith is used to argue that the second husband creates a fully new marital bond, inherently resetting the count.
5
Determine the practical difference and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): if a woman had one or two divorces, according to Shaykhayn the first husband can give three new divorces after the second marriage; according to Abu Hanifa, he can only give the remaining one or two. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school is the view of the Shaykhayn, due to the strength of the hadith and its acceptance among later jurists.
This ruling affects subsequent divorce rights and the possibility of final separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مالک رہے گا یعنی اگر پہلے ایک طلاق دے چکا تو اب باقی دو کا مالک ہوگا اور اگر پہلے نکاح میں دو طلاقیں دے چکا تو اب ایک کا مالک ہو گا یہی قول ہے امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا ۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غیرہ میں لا تحل له سے حرمت غلیظہ مراد ہے اور اس حرمت غلیظہ کی غایت اور نہایت زوج ثانی سے نکاح کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ احتمی غایت کے لئے وضع کیا سکتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زوج ثانی تین طلاقوں سے کم کو منہدم نہیں کرتا اور جب تین سے کم منہدم نہیں ہوتیں تو زوج اول نکاح ثانی کے بعد تین طلاقوں کا مالک نہیں ہو گا بلکہ پہلی بار طلاق دینے کے بعد جو باقی رہ گئی تھی اس کا مالک ہو گا ایک ہو یا دو ہوں۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له ، اس حدیث سے وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ محدثین اس کو باب ماجاء في الزوج الثانی کے تحت بیان کرتے ہیں۔ پس محلل سے مراد زوج ثانی ہوگا گو یا حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے زوج ثانی کا نام حلل رکھا ہے اور محلل کے معنی مثبت محل کے ہیں اب رہی یہ بات کہ زوج نانی کی وجہ سے جو خلت ثابت ہوگی وہ حل سابق ہے یا حل جدید حل سابق تو ہو نہیں سکتی ورنہ تحصیل حاصل لازم آئے گا پس حل جدید کا ہونا متعین ہو گیا اور یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ حل جد ید اول کا غیر ہو اور اول حل ناقص ہے۔ لہذا حصل جدید کامل ہوگی اور کامل حالت ہوتی ہے تین طلاقوں سے پس ثابت ہوا کہ زوج نانی زوج اول کے لئے ازسرنو تین طلاقیں ثابت کر دیتا ہے خواہ زوج اول نے تین طلاقیں دی ہوں یا تین سے کم دی ہوں دونوں برابر ہیں۔ عورت کو تین طلاقیں دیں عورت نے کہا میری عدت گذر چکی اور دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کیا اور اس نے دخول کیا اور طلاق دیدی اور میری عدت گذر چکی اس سے شوہر اول کیلئے کب نکاح کرنا جائز ہے
Chapter of Divorce of the Sick Person. Commentary: The issue is that if a man gave his free wife one divorce or two divorces and her iddah passed, then she married another husband, and then after the second husband's divorce and completion of iddah she returned to the first husband, then this woman returns to the first husband with three divorces, i.e., the first husband will own three divorces anew, and the second husband destroys less than three, one and two, just as he destroys three. This is the madhhab of the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the second husband does not destroy less than three divorces; rather, the first husband remains the owner of the remainder of the three, i.e., if he had already given one divorce, he will now own the remaining two, and if he had given two divorces in the first marriage, he will now own one. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. Imam Muhammad's proof is that in the statement of Allah Most High, 'And if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him thereafter until she marries another husband,' the phrase 'she is not lawful' refers to severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah), and the extreme limit of this severe prohibition is marriage to a second husband, because the word 'hatta' is placed for the extreme limit (ghayah), and the thing limited ends with the limit. Thus it is established that marriage to a second husband is what terminates the severe prohibition, and before the establishment of severe prohibition, there is no meaning to terminating the prohibition. Therefore, in the case of less than three divorces, intercourse by the second husband is not considered effective, because in this case severe prohibition is not established, and when severe prohibition is not established, the intercourse of the second husband cannot be the limit. Thus it is established that the second husband does not destroy less than three divorces, and when less than three are not destroyed, then after the second marriage the first husband will not own three divorces but rather will own what remained after the first divorce, whether one or two. The proof of the Shaykhayn is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'May Allah curse the muhallil and the one for whom tahleel is done.' The way of argument from this hadith is that the hadith scholars include it under the chapter 'On the Second Husband'. So 'muhallil' refers to the second husband; it is as if the Prophet (peace be upon him) named the second husband 'muhallil', and the meaning of 'muhallil' is the one who establishes legality. Now, the question remains whether the legality established by the second husband is the previous legality or a new legality. It cannot be the previous legality, because that would entail the acquisition of something already acquired; thus it is determined that it is a new legality. And it is also necessary that the new legality be different from the first, and the first legality was deficient. Therefore, the new legality will be complete, and the complete state is from three divorces. Thus it is established that the second husband establishes three divorces anew for the first husband, whether the first husband gave three divorces or less than three, both are equal. The woman was given three divorces; she said, 'my iddah passed and I married another husband, and he had intercourse with me and divorced me, and my iddah passed.' For the first husband, when is it permissible to marry her?
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a second marriage on the count of divorces. The Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that if a woman is divorced fewer than three times (one or two), then after she marries another husband, consummates the marriage, and gets divorced, the first husband regains the right to all three divorces because the second marriage completely severs the previous marriage and establishes a new marital bond. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the second husband only destroys the prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) when three divorces were given; if less than three, no severe prohibition existed, so the second marriage cannot create a new three-divorce right. Imam Muhammad's proof is based on the Qur'anic verse (al-Baqarah 2:230): 'And if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him thereafter until she marries another husband.' He argues that the phrase 'hata' indicates a limit (ghayah) that only applies after severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah). Since three divorces create such prohibition, only then can the second husband's marriage lift it. For one or two divorces, the prohibition is not severe, so the second husband's act is not a 'limit' and does not reset the count. The Shaykhayn, on the other hand, use the hadith cursing the muhallil (the one who marries a woman to make her lawful for her former husband). They argue that the second husband is called 'muhallil' because he establishes halaliyyah anew. This new legality must be complete, hence the first husband gets three divorces anew. Both positions are well-known in the Hanafi school, with the Shaykhayn's view being more widely adopted in practice. The passage also notes that Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i agree with Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
منہدم کرنا (munhadim karnā): To destroy or annul (the effect of previous divorces) through the second husband's marriage.
حرمت غلیظہ (hurmah ghalīẓah): Severe prohibition that makes the wife permanently unlawful for the husband after three divorces.
محلل (muḥallil): The second husband who marries a woman to make her lawful for her former husband after three divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a man gives his wife one divorce, then she remarries another man and gets divorced, how many divorces does the first husband own after she returns?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The Shaykhayn's view (second husband resets the count to three) is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, based on the hadith on the muhallil and the understanding that the second husband creates a new, complete legal bond.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Acceptance of Woman's Statement on Iddah and Remarriage After Three Divorces
Ruling on accepting a woman's claim of iddah completion and remarriage after three talags.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a husband may accept his wife's claim of iddah completion and remarriage after three talags, and explain why her word suffices according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A woman's word on her iddah and remarriage is accepted if the time is plausible and the husband's dominant presumption is she is truthful, because it is a matter of transaction or religion where single testimony suffices.

In Hanafi fiqh, after a third divorce, the wife's claim about her iddah and subsequent remarriage can be accepted without witnesses under certain conditions. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the rationale and the intra-school disagreement on the minimum acceptable time period. Understanding this ruling clarifies the balance between evidentiary rigor and practical necessity in personal matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the first husband's acceptance of the wife's statement after three talags. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) for him to believe her if conditions hold.
The ruling is not obligatory; it is a permission.
2
Locate the dalil
The author classifies marriage as a mu'amalah (transaction) and an amr dini (religious matter). In both categories, Hanafi usul accepts the word of a single Muslim.
This is based on the practice of the Companions and the absence of imputation in such personal matters.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The fact that bud' is valuable makes it a transaction; the attachment of halal makes it a religious matter. In these areas, a single Muslim's report is accepted without witnesses, as established by the Companions' acceptance of single reports.
The text distinguishes this from matters involving huquq al-ibad where witnesses are required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The jurists differed on the minimum time for these events to be plausible. Imam Abu Hanifa said 60 days; the Sahibayn said 49 days.
This difference stems from how the start of the iddah is calculated (beginning or end of tuhr).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a woman claims a period less than 49 days, all reject it; between 49 and 59 days, it is accepted by Sahibayn only.
The Hanafi school accommodates both views, and the husband may follow either.

Ashraf al-Hidayah, commentary, Urdu Hidayah, volume 5, in the chapter on iddah, page 63, chapter on divorce of the sick person. Translation: And if a man divorced his (free) wife three times, (then after some time) she said, 'My iddah passed, and I married (another husband), and the second husband had intercourse with me, and he divorced me, and my iddah passed,' and the time period she mentions is plausible for all these things, then it is permissible for the first husband to believe her, provided that his predominant opinion is that this woman is truthful. Because it is a transaction or a religious matter, due to lawfulness being attached to it, and the statement of one Muslim is accepted in both. And this woman's informing is not objectionable when the time period allows it. And the jurists differed regarding the minimum of this time period, and we will explain it in the chapter on iddah. Commentary: The scenario is that a man gave his free wife three divorces. After some time, the woman said, 'My iddah passed, and I married another husband, he had intercourse with me, and he divorced me, and my iddah is complete.' And the time period she mentions is such that it is plausible for all these events. Then it is permissible for the first husband to believe her, on condition that his predominant opinion is that she is truthful. The proof is that marriage is a transaction or a religious matter. It is a transaction because the private part (bud') is considered valuable at the time of intercourse, and it is a religious matter because lawfulness is attached to marriage. In both, the statement of one Muslim is accepted. In religious matters (diyanat), the statement of one Muslim is accepted because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) used to accept the report of one just person without requiring plurality. And transactions are of two types: one that does not imply imputation (ilzam), such as agency (wakalah); in this, the report of one person is reliable, whether he is just or sinful, child or adult, Muslim or disbeliever, free or slave, male or female, without condition of number or justice. The second type is that which implies imputation, such as the rights of people (huquq al-'ibad); in this, number, justice, and the word 'shahadah' are necessary. In any case, in this issue, the informing of one woman is not objectionable when the time period allows it. Now, the question remains what is the minimum time period in which all these events can occur. Regarding this, there is disagreement among the jurists of the Ummah. The author of al-Hidayah promised to explain this disagreement in the chapter on iddah, but in reality, this promise was not fulfilled in the chapter on iddah. It is possible that he forgot after promising. However, the commentators of al-Hidayah, while explaining this disagreement, said that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, the minimum iddah period for both the first and second husband is sixty days, and according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is forty-nine days. According to the Sahibayn, the scenario is that the husband divorced his wife at the end of a period of purity (tuhr). Then the iddah of this woman is two tuhrs and three menstruations. The minimum duration of tuhr is fifteen days, and the minimum duration of menstruation is three days. So two tuhrs make thirty days, and three menstruations make nine days; thus all three combined become forty-nine days. And according to Imam Abu Hanifah, the explanation from Imam Muhammad's statement is that the husband divorced his wife at the beginning of a tuhr; then in this case...
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on accepting a woman's claim after three divorces that her iddah has expired, she has remarried, consummated, divorced again, and completed her second iddah. The author of al-Hidayah states that if the time period she mentions is plausible, the first husband may believe her, provided his predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) is that she is truthful. The reasoning is that this is a matter of both mu'amalah (transaction, since the private part is valuable) and amr dini (religious matter, since halaliyyah is attached). In both categories, the statement of a single Muslim is accepted without requiring witnesses. The author draws an analogy to the practice of the Companions who accepted reports from a single just person. He further distinguishes between matters that do not involve imputation (like agency) where any person's report is accepted, and those that involve imputation (like rights of people) where witnesses are required. Since this case does not involve imputation (it is about personal permissibility), one woman's statement suffices. The passage then notes a disagreement on the minimum time period for these events. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the minimum iddah for both spouses is sixty days, while the Sahibayn say forty-nine days. The Sahibayn's calculation is based on divorcing at the end of a tuhr: then the woman waits through two tuhrs (minimum 15 days each) and three menstruations (minimum 3 days each), totaling 49 days. Imam Abu Hanifa's view, as explained by Imam Muhammad, is based on divorcing at the beginning of a tuhr, which leads to a different calculation. The passage ends abruptly, but it indicates that the full explanation was promised for the chapter on iddah but not actually given there.

Key Terms
غالب ظن (ghālib al-ẓann): Predominant opinion; a level of certainty that suffices for accepting a report in non-judicial matters.
معاملہ (muʿāmalah): A transaction involving financial or proprietary value (e.g., marriage where the private part is considered valuable).
امر دینی (amr dīnī): A religious matter, i.e., an act of worship or a matter related to halal and haram.
عدت (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before she can remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A husband may accept his wife's claim of iddah completion and remarriage after three talags if the time is plausible and he has a dominant presumption of her truthfulness, because it is a matter where the word of one Muslim is accepted.

‘Iddah Calculation for a Woman Divorced by a Sick Husband: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Counting Tuhr Periods
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah calculation for a sick husband's divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the standard Hanafi calculation of 'iddah (60 days) and distinguish the variant narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad regarding the number of tuhr periods.

Core Idea
The 'iddah is always 60 days in Hanafi fiqh, but the number of tuhr periods counted varies if divorce occurs at the end of a tuhr.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the calculation of a woman's waiting period ('iddah) after divorce by a sick husband. While the standard ruling (based on Zahir al-Riwayah) counts three tuhr and three hayd, a rare narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad presents an alternative counting if the divorce occurs at the end of a tuhr. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi scholars maintain consistency in total days while differing in the number of purity periods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard Hanafi position
Recognize that the 'iddah is three tuhr (purity periods) and three hayd (menstrual periods), totaling 60 days. This is the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Minimum tuhr = 15 days; average hayd = 5 days.
2
Understand the durations assumed
The standard calculation uses minimum tuhr (15 days) and average hayd (5 days). Three tuhr = 45 days, three hayd = 15 days, total 60 days.
These are fixed figures for the purpose of calculation, not variable actual durations.
3
Identify the alternative riwayah
According to Hasan ibn Ziyad, if divorce occurs at the end of a tuhr, the 'iddah is two tuhr and three hayd. The tuhr in which divorce occurs is not counted.
This is a rare narration (Nawadir) from a Hanafi scholar, not a Prophetic hadith.
4
Note the different maximum hayd duration
In this alternate view, the maximum hayd (10 days) is used instead of the average. Two tuhr (30 days) + three hayd (30 days) still total 60 days.
The consistency of total days preserves the general ruling while adjusting for the specific timing.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
Both views result in 60 days total, but the number of complete tuhr periods after divorce differs. In practice, the 'iddah ends on day 60 from divorce regardless of the count of tuhr.
The dispute has no effect on the total duration, only on the conceptual breakdown.

Source Text

باب طلاق المريض

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم عورت کی عدت تین طہر اور تین حیض ہوں گے اور طہر کی اقل مدت پندرہ دن ہیں اور حیض کی درمیانی مدت پانچ دن پس تین طہر کی مجموعی مدت پینتالیس دن ہوئے اور تین حیض کی مجموعی مدت پندرہ دن اس طرح دونوں کی مجموعی مدت ساٹھ دن ہوگی۔
اور حسن بن زیاد کی روایت کے مطابق تخریج یہ ہوگی کہ شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو آخر طہر میں طلاق دی تو اس صورت میں اس عورت کی عدت دو طہر اور تین حیض ہوں گے اور طہر کی ادنی مدت پندرہ دن اور حیض کی اکثر مدت دس دن ہیں پس اس صورت میں دو طہر بھی تمہیں دن کے ہوں گے اور تین حیض بھی تمھیں دن کے اس طرح دونوں مل کر ساٹھ دن ہو جائیں گے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
عنایہ الکنایه، فتح القدیر معینی شرح صدایه )
جمیل احمد عفی عنہ سکروڈوی
Chapter of the sick person's divorce. The waiting period of the woman is three tuhr and three hayd. The minimum duration of tuhr is fifteen days, and the average duration of hayd is five days. So the total duration of three tuhr is forty-five days, and the total duration of three hayd is fifteen days. Thus the combined total is sixty days. According to the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad, the derivation would be: if the husband divorced his wife at the end of tuhr, then in this case the woman's waiting period is two tuhr and three hayd. The minimum duration of tuhr is fifteen days, and the maximum duration of hayd is ten days. So in this case, two tuhr are also thirty days, and three hayd are also thirty days. Thus both combined become sixty days. And Allah knows best what is correct. (Annotations: al-Inaya, Fath al-Qadir, Ma'ini Sharh Sada) Jamil Ahmad Afi 'Anhu Sakharwi.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the calculation of the 'iddah (waiting period) for a woman divorced by a sick husband. The standard ruling, based on the preferred view (Zahir al-Riwayah), is that the 'iddah consists of three menstrual cycles (quru'), which in the Hanafi school are defined as three periods of tuhr (purity) and three hayd (menstruation). The minimum tuhr is 15 days, and the average hayd is 5 days, so the total is 45 days of tuhr plus 15 days of hayd = 60 days. However, the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad (a Hanafi authority, but his riwayah is considered rare) provides an alternative calculation: if the husband divorces his wife at the end of her tuhr, then the 'iddah consists of only two tuhr and three hayd. This is because the tuhr in which the divorce occurs does not count. The maximum hayd is 10 days, so two tuhr (30 days) plus three hayd (30 days) also totals 60 days. Thus, both rulings result in the same total duration but differ in the number of cycles considered. The author concludes with 'Wallahu a'lam', indicating the reliance on Allah's knowledge.

Key Terms
عدة (‘iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between menstrual periods.
رواية (riwayah): A transmission or narration of a ruling attributed to a Hanafi authority, here specifically from Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the total duration of the 'iddah according to both the standard view and Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration?
A) 45 days
B) 60 days
C) 75 days
D) 90 days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the 'iddah at 60 days for a divorce by a sick husband, with a minor intra-school dispute over the counting of tuhr periods that does not change the total duration.

Definition and Conditions of Ila'
Defines Ila' and outlines its conditions and rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Ila', list its conditions, pillar, and ruling according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ila' is a four-month vow of abstinence; if kept, it triggers an irrevocable divorce.

Ila' is a form of marital prohibition that combines an oath with a threat of divorce. This lesson unpacks its legal structure: what constitutes the vow, who can perform it, and what happens when the period ends or is broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Look at the text's definition of Ila' as an oath to abstain from intercourse for four months or more. Note that the Arabic definition includes both indefinite and four-month specific oaths.
2
Note the conditions
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the husband must be eligible to give divorce (i.e., sane adult). According to Sahibayn, he must be eligible for the obligation of expiation (i.e., Muslim? The text implies a difference in condition).
The condition differs based on the jurist's view of the primary consequence.
3
Understand the pillar and ruling
The pillar (rukn) is the verbal expression: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months.' The ruling is: if he has intercourse, expiation becomes obligatory; if the full period passes without intercourse, a bain (irrevocable) divorce occurs.

باب الايلاء ۶۵ تشریح آلی یولی ایلاء قسم کھانا اور شریعت میں ایلاء کہتے ہیں چار ماہ یاز اند اپنی منکوحہ کے پاس نہ جانے کی قسم کھانا اور اس کی شرط امام صاحب کے نزدیک طلاق کا اہل ہونا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وجوب کفارہ کا اہل ہونا ہے اور اس کا رکن واللہ اقربک اربعہ اشہر کہنا ہے اور اس کا حکم عورت کے قریب جانے کی صورت میں کفارہ کا لازم ہونا اور مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کی صورت میں طلاق بائن کا واقع ہونا ہے۔ صاحب فتح القدیر نے بیان کیا ہے کہ بیوی کی تحریم چار طریقوں سے ہوتی ہے۔ (۱) طلاق (۲) ایلاء (۳) ظہار (۴) لعان ۔ ان چاروں میں سب سے پہلے طلاق کو ذکر فرمایا کیونکہ طلاق طرق تحریم میں اصل ہے اور اپنے وقت میں مباح ہے پھر ایلاء کو ذکر کیا گیا اس لئے کہ ایلا واباحت میں طلاق سے قریب تر ہے کیونکہ ایلاء یمین مشروع کا نام ہے ۔ مگر اس میں عورت کے حق وطی کو روکنے کی وجہ سے ظلم کے معنی بھی ہیں ۔ اس وجہ سے طلاق سے موخر کیا گیا۔

ایلاء کی تعریف
واذا قال الرجل لامرأته والله لا اقربك او قال والله لا اقربك اربعة اشهر فهومول لقوله تعالى للذين يولون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر الآية

ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ بخدا میں تجھ سے قربت نہیں کروں گا۔ یا کہا بخدا میں تجھ سے چار ماہ قربت نہیں کروں گا۔ تو شخص ایلاء کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے جو لوگ اپنی عورتوں سے ایلاء کرتے ہیں ان کے لئے چار ماہ کا انتظار ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ اور اس کی دلیل ظاہر ہے۔

مگر واضح ہو کہ ایلاء کی دوصورتیں ہیں ۔ (۱) شوہر کا قول واللہ لا اقرب ابدا اس صورت میں یہ شخص بالا جماع ایلاء کرنے والا ہے۔ (۲) اس کا قول والله اقربك اربعة اشهر - اس صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک ایلاء کرنے والا ہوگا اور امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کے نزدیک ایلاء کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ چار ماہ سے زائد کی قسم نہ کھائے ۔ کیونکہ ان حضرات کے نزدیک چار ماہ بعد ایلاء سے رجوع کر سکتا ہے لہذا چار ماہ پر ایک مدت زائدہ کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ چنانچہ امام مالک کے نزدیک کم از کم ایک دن زائد ہوگا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ایک لمحہ لیکن ان کا یہ قول ظاہر قرآن کے خلاف ہونے کی وجہ سے مردود ہوگا۔
Chapter of Ila'. Explanation of the word Ila': to swear an oath. In Shari'ah, Ila' is called swearing not to go near one's wife for four months or more. Its condition according to Imam Abu Hanifa is being eligible to give divorce, and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is being eligible for the obligation of expiation. Its pillar is saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months.' Its ruling is that if he approaches the wife, expiation becomes obligatory, and if the period of Ila' passes, a bain divorce occurs. The author of Fath al-Qadir stated that a wife becomes prohibited through four ways: (1) divorce, (2) Ila', (3) Zihar, (4) Li'an. Among these, divorce is mentioned first because it is the basis of prohibition and is permissible in its time. Then Ila' is mentioned because it is closer to permissibility than divorce, as Ila' is a legitimate oath, but it also involves oppression by preventing the wife's right to intercourse, so it is delayed after divorce.

Definition of Ila': When a man says to his wife, 'By Allah, I will not approach you,' or 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months,' he is a person who has performed Ila', due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'For those who swear off their wives, a waiting period of four months.'

Translation: If the husband said, 'By Allah, I will not have intercourse with you,' or 'By Allah, I will not have intercourse with you for four months,' then he becomes a person who has performed Ila'. Because Allah Almighty said: 'For those who swear off their wives, a waiting period of four months.' Explanation: The issue and its proof are clear.

But it should be clear that Ila' has two forms: (1) The husband says 'By Allah, I will never approach you' - in this case, he is unanimously a person who has performed Ila'. (2) He says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months' - in this case, according to us (Hanafis), he is a person who has performed Ila', but according to Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, he is not a person who has performed Ila' until he swears for more than four months. Because according to these scholars, he can retract from Ila' after four months, so there must be an additional period beyond four months. According to Imam Malik, at least one day extra, and according to Imam Shafi'i, one moment. But this statement of theirs is rejected because it is contrary to the apparent meaning of the Quran.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It begins by defining the linguistic and legal meaning of Ila': a vow to abstain from marital relations for a period of four months or more. The author then lists the conditions: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the husband must be legally capable of issuing divorce (i.e., sane and adult), while according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), he must be capable of being obligated to pay expiation (i.e., Muslim?). The pillar (rukn) is the verbal expression explicitly stating the four-month period. The ruling is that if he has intercourse during the period, expiation becomes due; if he abstains until the four months elapse, a bain (irrevocable) divorce occurs. The commentary cites Fath al-Qadir to note that a wife becomes prohibited through four methods: divorce, Ila', zihar, and li'an, with Ila' being closer to permissibility than divorce. The passage then provides the Quranic proof (Surah al-Baqarah 2:226) and distinguishes two forms of Ila': one with an indefinite period (e.g., 'forever') and one with a specific period of exactly four months. Regarding the second form, there is a significant inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school holds that swearing for exactly four months constitutes Ila', while the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools require an additional period beyond four months. Their reasoning is that after four months, the husband can retract, so the oath must extend beyond that to establish a threat of divorce. The Hanafi position refutes this on the basis of the clear Quranic text, which sets the period at exactly four months.

Key Terms
الايلاء (al-īlā'): A vow to abstain from sexual relations with one's wife for a period of four months or more, which if unbroken leads to a divorce.
اليمين (al-yamīn): An oath, which is the basis of Ila'.
التربص (al-tarabbus): The waiting period of four months prescribed in the Quran for the wife of one who has performed Ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of the oath for it to be considered Ila'?
A) One day
B) Four months
C) More than four months
D) One year

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a valid legal act when a husband capable of divorce or expiation swears to abstain from intercourse for four months, with prescribed consequences.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The Inter-Madhhab Dispute on the Minimum Period of Ila'
Disputes the validity of swearing for exactly four months.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the minimum period for Ila' and evaluate the counter-arguments of the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Core Idea
The Quranic 'four months' is the literal basis; any additional requirement is a deviation from the clear text.

The second form of Ila' — swearing to abstain for exactly four months — sparks a major inter-madhhab disagreement. The Hanafi school holds it valid based on the literal Quran, while three other Imams demand an extra period. This lesson explores the proof texts and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second form
The husband says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months.' This is distinct from the indefinite form.
The indefinite form is agreed upon; the dispute lies here.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the Hanafi school, this statement constitutes Ila'. The Quranic verse does not require more than four months.
3
State the opposing position
Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold that it does not constitute Ila' unless the period exceeds four months. Their reason: after four months, the husband can retract, so the oath must extend beyond to have binding effect.
Malik requires at least one extra day; Shafi'i requires one extra moment.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school refutes this by saying the Quranic text is clear; any addition is against the zahir. The retraction after four months is equivalent to the divorce that automatically occurs in the Hanafi view, so no extra period is needed.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Consequences of Intercourse During Ila': Hanth, Kaffarah, and Nullification
Ruling with proof on intercourse within Ila' and kaffarah dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband has intercourse during the Ila' period, identify the proof and the dispute with Imam Shafi'i, and explain why kaffarah is obligatory and Ila' is nullified.

Core Idea
Intercourse within Ila' breaks the oath, requiring expiation, and nullifies the Ila'—no divorce at period's end.

This passage covers the critical intersection of oath-breaking (hanth) and Ila'. When a husband swears to abstain, any intercourse within four months is a breach with two legal effects: mandatory expiation (kaffarah) and termination of the Ila' vow. The passage also engages a famous dispute with Imam Shafi'i's earlier view, showing how Hanafi usul distinguishes between worldly obligations and otherworldly forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what happens when the husband has intercourse within the Ila' period: he becomes hanith (breaks the oath), kaffarah becomes obligatory, and the Ila' is nullified.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is the general rule that breaking an oath requires kaffarah; Ila' is a valid oath. The opposing proof is Quran 2:226-227, which promises forgiveness for returning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafis argue that forgiveness in the Hereafter does not negate worldly obligations. The word 'fa'u' (return) triggers forgiveness but not exemption from kaffarah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Shafi'i (old opinion) held that no kaffarah is required because forgiveness implies no expiation. His new opinion aligns with the Hanafis.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi; it is supported by the general rules of oaths and by later agreement of Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad.

فان وطيها فى الاربعة الاشهر حنث فى يمينه ولزمته الكفارة لان الكفارة موجب الحنث وسقط الايلاء لان اليمين ترتفع بالحنث

ترجمہ . پس اگر چار ماہ میں عورت کے ساتھ وطی کر لی تو اپنی قسم میں حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس پر کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یمین حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے مرتفع ہو جاتی ہے

شخصی
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ کے اندر اندر اس عورت سے ولی کر لی تو شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث ہوگا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث تو ہو جائے گا مگر اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء قسم ہے اس میں حانث ہو چکا۔ اس وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پوری آیت ایلاء یہ ہے للذين يؤلون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر فان فائوا فان الله غفور الرحيم و ان عزموا الطلاق فان الله سميع علیم اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مدت ایلاء میں رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے مغفرت کا وعدہ فرمایا ہے اور مغفور کے فعل پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو گا ۔ مگر ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ مغفرت کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہے آخرت میں اور کفارہ واجب ہوتا ہے دنیا میں اور مغفرت فی الآخرت وجوب کفارہ فی الدنیا کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ امام شافعی کا قول قدیم ہے۔ ورنہ قول جدید کی بناء پر ان کے نزدیک بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔ بہر حال مدت ایلاء میں ولی کر لینے کے بعد جب حانث ہو گیا اور کفارہ واجب ہو گیا تو ایلا بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا ایلاء ساقط ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر چار ماہ گزرجائیں تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
For if he has intercourse with her within the four months, he breaks his oath, and expiation becomes obligatory upon him, because expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and the Ila' is nullified, because the oath is removed by breaking it.

Translation: So if within the four months he has intercourse with the wife, he becomes a breaker of his oath, and expiation becomes obligatory upon him, because expiation is the cause of breaking the oath. And Ila' becomes nullified because the oath is lifted due to breaking it.

Personal explanation: The explanation of the case is that if the husband had intercourse with this wife within the period of Ila', i.e., four months, then the husband becomes a breaker (hanith) of his oath, and expiation becomes obligatory upon him. Imam Shafi'i says that the husband becomes a breaker of his oath, but expiation is not obligatory upon him. Our proof is that expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and Ila' is an oath; he has broken it, therefore expiation becomes necessary. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is that the complete verse of Ila' is: 'For those who swear off their wives, a waiting period of four months; then if they return, indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful; and if they resolve on divorce, indeed Allah is Hearing, Knowing.' This verse indicates that in case of returning within the Ila' period, Allah has promised forgiveness, and expiation is not obligatory for an action that is forgiven. Therefore, expiation is not obligatory. Our response is that forgiveness is promised in the Hereafter, while expiation is obligatory in this world; forgiveness in the Hereafter does not contradict the obligation of expiation in this world. But this is the old opinion of Imam Shafi'i. According to his new opinion, expiation is also obligatory according to him, as it is in our madhhab, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. In any case, after having intercourse within the Ila' period, when he has become hanith and expiation has become obligatory, then Ila' also becomes nullified. The meaning of Ila' being nullified is that if the four months pass, divorce does not occur.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding the scenario where the husband has intercourse with his wife during the period of Ila' (the four months). The author asserts two consequences: (1) the husband becomes hanith (breaker of the oath) and must pay kaffarah (expiation), and (2) the Ila' itself is nullified, meaning that if the four months expire after the intercourse, no divorce takes place. The proof is that expiation is the legal consequence of breaking an oath. The passage includes an intra-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who initially held (in his old opinion) that expiation is not obligatory because the Quranic verse promises forgiveness for returning, implying that no penalty is needed. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forgiveness in the afterlife (which does not negate worldly obligations) and the worldly obligation of kaffarah. The passage notes that Imam Shafi'i later changed his position (new opinion) to agree with the Hanafis, and that Imams Malik and Ahmad also hold the same view as the Hanafis. Therefore, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that kaffarah is obligatory if intercourse occurs within the Ila' period. The nullification of Ila' means that the husband is no longer bound by the vow, and if he abstains after intercourse, no divorce occurs at the end of the four months.

Key Terms
الحنث (al-ḥanth): Breaking one's oath, specifically by having intercourse within the Ila' period.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath, consisting of freeing a slave, or feeding ten poor, or fasting three days.
سقوط الايلاء (suqūṭ al-īlā'): Nullification of Ila' due to intercourse, meaning the vow is no longer binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a husband has intercourse with his wife during the four-month Ila' period?
A) Ila' is nullified and no expiation is required
B) He becomes hanith and must pay kaffarah, and Ila' is nullified
C) The Ila' continues and he must complete the four months
D) A divorce automatically occurs

Key Takeaway
Intercourse within Ila' breaks the oath, obligates kaffarah, and nullifies the Ila' vow, preventing automatic divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Ruling on Not Approaching: Automatic Bain Divorce After Four Months
Rules automatic bain divorce after four months of abstinence, with disputes on qadi involvement and type of divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ila' when the husband does not approach his wife for four months and explain the key difference from the Shafi'i position regarding judicial involvement.

Core Idea
Ila' results in an automatic bain divorce after four months — no court order is needed.

This lesson covers a specific scenario of Ila' (vow of abstinence): when the husband does not have intercourse with his wife for the entire four-month period. According to the Hanafi school, a bain (irrevocable) divorce takes effect automatically upon expiry of the four months, without any need for a court decree. The passage presents the Hanafi proof based on the practice of eminent Companions and also contrasts with the Shafi'i view requiring judicial separation. By the end, you will understand the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? It is Ila' where the husband refrains from intercourse for four months. The ruling: one bain divorce occurs automatically at the end of the period.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof is primarily the practice (athar) of the Sahaba: 'Uthman, 'Ali, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Zayd ibn Thabit. This is supplemented by the principle that the Shari'ah retaliates against the husband's oppression by removing the marriage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the practice prove the ruling? The Companions implemented Ila' as an automatic divorce, and their consensus (or widespread practice) is a source of law for Hanafis. Additionally, the verse of Ila' (2:226) implies that after the period, either reconciliation or divorce follows, and the Hanafis take divorce as the default if no return occurs.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i requires the judge to pronounce the divorce (tafriq al-qadi), likening it to cases of impotence. Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab holds that the divorce is raj'i (revocable), not bain.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on the strong transmission from the Sahaba. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the Hanafi view over the minority opinion of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab.

Source Text
