وان لم يقربها حتى مضت اربعة اشهر بانت منه بتطليقة وقال الشافعي تبين بتفريق القاضي لانه مانع حقها في الجماع فينوب القاضي منابه فى التسريح كما فى الجب والعنة ولنا انه ظلمها بمنع حقها فجازاه الشرع بزوال نعمة النكاح عند مضى هذه المدة وهو الماثور عن عثمان وعلى والعبادلة الثلاثة وزيد بن ثابت رضوان الله عليهم اجمعين و كفى بهم قدوة ولانه كان طلاقافي الجاهلية فحكم الشرع بتاجيله الى انقضاء المدة

ترجمہ . اور اگر اس عورت سے قربت نہیں کی۔ حتی کہ چار ماہ گزر گئے ۔ تو اس سے ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو گئی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی کے جدا کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مرد اس عورت کے حق جماع کو روکنے والا ہے۔ پس قاضی چھٹکار ا دینے میں اس مرد کے قائم مقام ہوگا ، جیسے مقطوع الذکر اور حنین میں ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد نے عورت کا حق روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے اس کو بدلا دیا کہ اس مدت کے گزر جانے پر نکاح کی نعمت زائل ہو جائے گی اور یہی قول حضرت عثمان علی عبد اللہ بن عمر عبد اللہ ابن عباس اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان بزرگوں کا پیشوا ہونا کافی ہے اور اس لئے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء کرنا طلاق تھا تو شریعت نے اس کی حد اس مدت گزرنے تک مقرر کر دی۔

اور اگر شوہر مدت ایلاء میں بیوی کے ساتھ ولی نہیں کر سکا حتى کہ مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ گزر گئے تو علماء احناف کے نزدیک یہ عورت ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائے گی اور سعید بن المسیب اور ابو بکر بن عبد الرحمن بن الحارث کا قول یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔
And if he does not approach her until the four months pass, she becomes separated from him with one divorce. And al-Shafi'i said that she becomes separated by the separation of the judge, because the husband is preventing her right to intercourse, so the judge takes his place in setting her free, as in the case of the one whose penis is cut off and the impotent one. And our proof is that he oppressed her by preventing her right, so the Shari'ah rewarded him by removing the blessing of marriage at the passing of this period. This is the transmitted report from 'Uthman, 'Ali, the three 'Abdullahs (Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn al-Zubayr?) and Zayd ibn Thabit - may Allah be pleased with them all - and they are sufficient as exemplars. Also, in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was considered a divorce, so the Shari'ah gave it a limit until the expiry of the period.

Translation: And if he did not approach this wife until four months passed, then she became bain with one divorce. Imam Shafi'i said that she becomes bain by the separation of the judge, because the man is preventing her right to intercourse, so the judge stands in his place for releasing her, just as in the case of the impotent and the one whose male organ is cut off. And our proof is that the man oppressed her by preventing her right, so the Shari'ah recompensed him by removing the blessing of marriage at the end of this period. And this is the saying transmitted from 'Uthman, 'Ali, the three 'Abdullahs (Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn al-Zubayr?), and Zayd ibn Thabit - may Allah be pleased with them all - and they are sufficient as leaders. Also, in the period of Jahiliyyah, Ila' was divorce, so the Shari'ah set its limit until the expiry of the period.

And if the husband could not have intercourse with the wife within the Ila' period until the Ila' period, i.e., four months, passed, then according to Hanafi scholars, this woman becomes bain with one divorce. And the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and Abu Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith is that one raj'i divorce occurs.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) regarding the second scenario of Ila': when the husband does not have intercourse with his wife for the entire four-month period. The Hanafi ruling is that a bain (irrevocable) divorce automatically takes effect at the end of the four months. The passage includes a dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who holds that the divorce only takes place through a court order (tafriq al-qadi), because the husband is preventing the wife's right, so the judge acts as his deputy (na'ib) to pronounce the divorce, analogous to cases of impotence ('unnah) or castration (jabb). The Hanafi response is that the husband oppressed the wife by withholding her right, and the Shari'ah retaliates by automatically removing the marriage at the end of the period, without requiring court intervention. The passage provides evidence from the practices of prominent Sahaba: 'Uthman, 'Ali, 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, and Zayd ibn Thabit, who all held that the divorce occurs automatically upon expiry of the four months. The passage also mentions a historical continuity: in pre-Islamic times, Ila' was considered an immediate divorce, but Islamic law set a waiting period of four months. Additionally, the passage notes an intra-early dispute: while Hanafis consider the divorce to be bain (irrevocable), Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and Abu Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith considered it to be a raj'i (revocable) divorce. The Hanafi position (bain) is the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
البائن (al-bā'in): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage and contract.
تفريق القاضي (tafrīq al-qāḍī): Judicial separation, which Shafi'is require for Ila' divorce.
الصحابة (al-ṣaḥābah): The companions of the Prophet, whose consensus or practice is used as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the husband does not have intercourse with his wife during the four-month Ila' period?
A) The wife must go to court for divorce
B) One bain divorce occurs automatically
C) The Ila' continues indefinitely
D) The marriage remains valid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, Ila' results in an automatic bain divorce after four months of abstinence, without requiring any court order.

Talaq — Divorce

The Hanafi Ruling on Ila': Automatic Ba'in Talaq
Explaining the Hanafi ruling on Ila' with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ila' and explain why a ba'in talaq occurs automatically after four months without intercourse, citing the Quranic and rational proofs.

Core Idea
After four months of Ila' without intercourse, the marriage ends automatically with a ba'in talaq – no court needed.

Ila' is a husband's vow to abstain from intercourse for four months or more. The Hanafi school teaches that if he does not return within the four months, the marriage dissolves by itself. This lesson unpacks the textual proof from the Qur'an, the practice of the Companions, and the rational principle that underpins this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the two possible outcomes
Identify what happens if the husband returns (intercourse) vs. if he does not. Return breaks the oath with expiation; non-return triggers divorce.
The divorce is ba'in, not raj'i.
2
Examine the Quranic verse
Recite Surah Al-Baqarah 2:226-227. Note that it sets a waiting period and mentions return or divorce. The Hanafi school interprets 'return' as intercourse and treats the verse as implying automatic divorce after the period.
The verse does not mention expiation; the Hanafi school infers it from other texts.
3
Consider the Companion evidence
The ruling is narrated from Uthman, Ali, three Abdallahs, and Zaid. Their agreement suffices as a precedent.
This is a strong indicator of the school's position.
4
Understand the rational proof
The husband oppresses the wife by depriving her of her right. The law punishes him by removing the blessing of marriage after the fixed period.
This is a form of justice: the oppression is met with dissolution.
5
Acknowledge the intra-Hanafi variations
Though the relied-upon position is automatic ba'in talaq, some Hanafi scholars (Imam Muhammad, Sahibayn) gave the qadi a say. Know that the mufta bihi is the automatic view.
This nuance will be explored in the next lesson.

باب الإيلاء
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
القاضي لانه مانع حقها في الجماع فينوب القاضي منابه فى التسريح كما فى الجب والعنة ولنا انه ظلمها بمنع حقها فجازاه الشرع بزوال نعمة النكاح عند مضى هذه المدة وهو الماثور عن عثمان وعلى والعبادلة الثلاثة وزيد بن ثابت رضوان الله عليهم اجمعين و كفى بهم قدوة ولانه كان طلاقافي الجاهلية فحكم الشرع بتاجيله الى انقضاء المدة
ترجمہ . پس اگر چار ماہ میں عورت کے ساتھ وطی کر لی تو اپنی قسم میں حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس پر کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یمین حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے مرتفع ہو جاتی ہے اور اگر اس عورت سے قربت نہیں کی۔ حتی کہ چار ماہ گزر گئے ۔ تو اس سے ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو گئی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی کے جدا کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مرد اس عورت کے حق جماع کو روکنے والا ہے۔ پس قاضی چھٹکار ا دینے میں اس مرد کے قائم مقام ہوگا ، جیسے مقطوع الذکر اور حنین میں ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد نے عورت کا حق روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے اس کو بدلا دیا کہ اس مدت کے گزر جانے پر نکاح کی نعمت زائل ہو جائے گی اور یہی قول حضرت عثمان علی عبد اللہ بن عمر عبد اللہ ابن عباس اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان بزرگوں کا پیشوا ہونا کافی ہے اور اس لئے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء کرنا طلاق تھا تو شریعت نے اس کی حد اس مدت گزرنے تک مقرر کر دی۔
شخصی
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ کے اندر اندر اس عورت سے ولی کر لی تو شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث ہوگا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث تو ہو جائے گا مگر اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء قسم ہے اس میں حانث ہو چکا۔ اس وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پوری آیت ایلاء یہ ہے للذين يؤلون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر فان فائوا فان الله غفور الرحيم و ان عزموا الطلاق فان الله سميع علیم اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مدت ایلاء میں رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے مغفرت کا وعدہ فرمایا ہے اور مغفور کے فعل پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو گا ۔ مگر ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ مغفرت کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہے آخرت میں اور کفارہ واجب ہوتا ہے دنیا میں اور مغفرت فی الآخرت وجوب کفارہ فی الدنیا کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ امام شافعی کا قول قدیم ہے۔ ورنہ قول جدید کی بناء پر ان کے نزدیک بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔ بہر حال مدت ایلاء میں ولی کر لینے کے بعد جب حانث ہو گیا اور کفارہ واجب ہو گیا تو ایلا بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا ایلاء ساقط ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر چار ماہ گزرجائیں تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے یمین باقی نہیں رہتی اور یمین ہی کا نام ایلاء ہے پس جب یمین باقی نہ رہی تو ایلاء بھی باقی نہ رہے گا۔ اور اگر شوہر مدت ایلاء میں بیوی کے ساتھ ولی نہیں کر سکا حتی کہ مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ گزر گئے تو علماء احناف کے نزدیک یہ عورت ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائے گی اور سعید بن المسیب اور ابو بکر بن عبد الرحمن بن الحارث کا قول یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ عورت مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد قاضی کے تفریق کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد فرقت کا حکم موقوف رہے گا۔ چنانچہ اگر شوہر نے رجوع کرنے اور فرقت کرنے سے انکار کر دیا اور بیوی نے قاضی سے تفریق کا مطالبہ کیا تو قاضی کی تفریق طلاق رجعی ہوگی اور مبسوط میں یہ ہے کہ طلاق بائن ہوگی اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاکم کو اختیار ہے وہ اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے یا بائنہ یا دو یا تین یا نکاح کو سح کر دے اور امام محمد کامذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ حاکم اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے جیسا کہ امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا بھی یہ قول ہے۔ اصحاب خواہر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد حاکم اس عورت کو طلاق نہ دے، بلکہ اس کو کوڑے مار کر مجبور کرے اور قید میں ڈال دے یہاں تک کہ وہ رجوع کرے یا اس کو طلاق دے امام شافعی کا قول قدیم بھی یہی ہے۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ)
صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے چار ماہ یا زائد وطی نہ کرنے کی قسم کھا کر عورت کے حق جماع کو روک لیا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس سے شوہر کا ارادہ عورت کو ضرر پہنچانا اور ضیق میں مبتلا کرنا ہے۔ پس اصرار کی وجہ سے کیونکہ شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا اس لئے قاصی تشریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا اور قاضی کی یہ تفریق طلاق بائن ہوگی اور ایسا ہے جیسا کہ شوہر اگر مقطوع الذکر یا عمنین ہو تو قاضی شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دیتا ہے اور ان دونوں میں علت مشترکہ امساک بالمعروف فوت ہونے کے وقت عورت سے ضرر کو دور کرنا ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے عورت کے حق جماع کو روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے شوہر کو اس ظلم کا بدلہ اس طرح دیا کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد نعمت نکاح کو زائل کر دیا تا کہ عورت متعلقہ ضرر سے چھٹکارا پا سکے اور ظاہر ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے ذریعہ سے عورت چھٹکارا نہیں پاسکتی اس لئے یہ طلاق بائن ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارا مذ ہب یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد بینونت کا واقع ہونا حضرت عثمان، حضرت علی ،عبداللہ بن نود عبد اللہ بن عباس، عبد اللہ ابن عمر اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان حضرات صحابہ کا پیشوا ہونا ہمارے لئے کافی ہے۔ ہماری دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء طلاق بائن علی الفور تھا۔ یعنی ایلاء کے فورا بعد سے شوہر دائمی طور پر اپنی بیوی سے وطی نہیں کر سکتا تھا پس شریعت نے اس حکم کو مدت ایلاء گزر جانے تک کے لئے موجل کر دیا ہے۔ الہذا اس حکم میں علاوہ تا جیل کے کوئی تصرف نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جس طرح ایلاء کی وجہ سے زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی تھی اسی طرح اس وقت بھی طلاق بائن ہوگی مگر اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلے بینونت علی الفور تھی اور اب بینونت علی التراخی ہے اور جس طرح زمانہ جاہلیت میں بینونت تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں تھی اس طرح اسلام کے بعد بھی تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں رہے گی ۔ چار مہینے کے ساتھ قسم کھائی قسم مدت کے گذر جانے سے ختم ہو جائے گی البتہ اگر مو بد قسم اٹھائی تو وہ باقی رہے گی
فان كان حلف على اربعة اشهر فقد سقطت اليمين لانها كانت موقتة به وان كان حلف على الابد فاليمين
Chapter of Ila'. Commentary on Hidayah volume five. The qadi, because he prevents her right to intercourse, so the qadi takes his place in releasing, as in the case of the castrated and the impotent. And our proof: he oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law punished him by the removal of the blessing of marriage after the passing of this period. And this is narrated from Uthman, Ali, the three Abdallahs, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and they are sufficient as leaders. And because it was divorce in the Jahiliyyah, so the law delayed it until the end of the period. Translation: So if he has intercourse with the woman within four months, he becomes a breaker of his oath and expiation becomes obligatory upon him. Because expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and Ila' is nullified because the oath is removed due to breaking it. And if he does not approach that woman until four months pass, then she becomes ba'in with one talaq. Imam Shafi'i said: she becomes ba'in by the qadi's separation. Because the man is preventing her right to intercourse, so the qadi takes his place in giving release, as in the case of the castrated and the impotent. And our proof: the man oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law gave him the recompense that upon the passing of this period, the blessing of marriage is removed. And this saying is narrated from Uthman, Ali, Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Abbas, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and their leadership is sufficient. And because in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was divorce, so the law set its limit until the passing of that period. Personal: Explanation of the scenario: if the husband has intercourse with this woman within the period of Ila', i.e., four months, then the husband becomes a breaker of his oath and expiation becomes obligatory upon him. Imam Shafi'i says: the husband becomes a breaker of his oath but expiation is not obligatory upon him. Our proof: expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and Ila' is an oath, and he has broken it, so expiation becomes necessary. The proof of Imam Shafi'i: the complete verse of Ila' is: 'For those who swear abstention from their wives, a waiting period of four months. Then if they return, indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful. And if they resolve on divorce, indeed Allah is Hearing, Knowing.' From this verse it is understood that in the case of returning within the Ila' period, Allah has promised forgiveness, and expiation is not obligatory for an act that is forgiven. For this reason, expiation will not be obligatory. But our response: forgiveness is promised in the Hereafter, and expiation is obligatory in this world, and forgiveness in the Hereafter does not contradict the obligation of expiation in this world. But this is the old saying of Imam Shafi'i. Based on the new saying, according to him also, expiation will be obligatory, as is our madhhab, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. In any case, after having intercourse within the Ila' period, when he becomes a breaker and expiation becomes obligatory, then Ila' is also nullified. The meaning of Ila' being nullified is that if four months pass, divorce will not occur. The proof is that due to breaking the oath, the oath does not remain, and Ila' is the name of the oath. So when the oath does not remain, Ila' will not remain either. And if the husband could not have intercourse with his wife within the Ila' period such that the Ila' period, i.e., four months, passed, then according to the Hanafi scholars, this woman becomes ba'in with one talaq. And the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith is that one raj'i talaq occurs. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya volume five. And Imam Shafi'i said that this woman becomes ba'in by the qadi's separation after the Ila' period passes. That is, after the Ila' period passes, the ruling of separation is suspended. So if the husband refuses to return and refuses to separate, and the wife demands separation from the qadi, then the qadi's separation will be a raj'i talaq, and in al-Mabsut it is that the talaq will be ba'in. And Imam Muhammad said that the ruler has the option: he may give this woman one raj'i talaq, or ba'in, or two, or three, or annul the marriage. And the preferred view of Imam Muhammad is that the ruler should give her one raj'i talaq, as this is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. The view of the Sahibayn is that after the Ila' period passes, the ruler should not give her a talaq, but rather should beat her with whips and imprison her until he returns or divorces her. The old view of Imam Shafi'i is also this. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah) According to the statement of the author of al-Hidayah, the proof of Imam Shafi'i is that the husband swore an oath not to have intercourse for four months or more and prevented the woman's right to intercourse, and it is apparent that the husband's intent is to harm the woman and put her in difficulty. So because of his persistence, since the husband refrained from keeping her with kindness, the qadi in the matter of releasing with kindness will take the place of the husband and separate them, and this separation by the qadi will be a ba'in talaq. And this is similar to when the husband is castrated or impotent, the qadi takes his place and separates them. And in both cases, the common cause is removal of harm from the woman when the ability to keep her with kindness is lost. Our proof: the husband oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law gave the husband the recompense that after the Ila' period passes, the blessing of marriage is removed so that the woman can be free from the harm. And it is apparent that she cannot be freed through a raj'i talaq, so this talaq is ba'in. The author of al-Hidayah says: our madhhab, i.e., the occurrence of separation after the Ila' period passes, is narrated from Uthman, Ali, Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Abbas, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and their leadership is sufficient for us. Our second rational proof: in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was an immediate ba'in talaq, i.e., immediately after the Ila', the husband could not permanently have intercourse with his wife. So the law delayed this ruling until the Ila' period passes. Therefore, no change is made in this ruling other than the delay. So just as in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' caused a ba'in talaq, similarly now also a ba'in talaq will occur, with the difference that previously separation was immediate and now it is delayed. And just as in the Jahiliyyah, separation was not contingent on the qadi's separation, similarly after Islam, it will not be contingent on the qadi's separation. If he swore an oath for four months, then the oath is nullified because it was time-bound to it, and if he swore an oath forever, then the oath [remains].
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf ul-Hidaya presents the rulings of Ila' (vow of abstinence) and engages in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and other scholars. It begins by stating the Hanafi position: if the husband has intercourse within the four-month period, he breaks his oath (hanith) and must pay expiation (kaffarah); the Ila' is lifted. If he does not have intercourse and the four months pass, then one ba'in talaq occurs automatically. The passage then contrasts this with Imam Shafi'i's view: separation occurs only through the qadi's ruling, which produces a ba'in talaq. The Hanafi proof is that the husband oppressed the wife by preventing her right, so the law punishes him by dissolving the marriage after the period, narrated from several Companions. A second rational proof is that in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was immediate ba'in talaq; Islam only delayed it to the end of the period. The passage also discusses a secondary dispute regarding expiation: the Shafi'i school initially held that if the husband returns within the period, no expiation is needed because the Qur'an promises forgiveness. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forgiveness in the Hereafter and legal expiation in this world, noting that the Shafi'i school later changed its view. The passage further records intra-Hanafi differences: some scholars among the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad provide options for the qadi, but the relied-upon view is that one ba'in talaq occurs. The teacher should note the authority weight: this is from the Hanafi madhhab, relying on the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) and supported by Companion practice.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): A vow (yamin) made by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
الحانث (al-hanith): The one who breaks his oath; here, the husband who has intercourse within the Ila' period.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-ba'in): A final divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the husband does not have intercourse with his wife within the four-month Ila' period?
A) One ba'in talaq occurs automatically.
B) The wife must seek a qadi's ruling for separation.
C) The marriage continues until the husband decides.
D) Expiation is required but marriage continues.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Ila' leads to an automatic ba'in talaq after four months without intercourse, based on Quranic text, Companion practice, and rational justice.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The Ila' Dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Automatic Divorce and Expiation
Inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on Ila' rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the core points of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on Ila', including the automatic divorce and the obligation of expiation upon return, and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school says divorce is automatic after four months; the Shafi'i school says it requires a qadi's ruling. The dispute turns on the role of judicial authority and the interpretation of forgiveness in the Quran.

The rulings on Ila' are not uniform across the schools. Imam al-Shafi'i held that divorce does not occur automatically but only through a qadi's decree, and that no expiation is required if the husband returns within the period. The Hanafi school strongly disagrees, citing Companion practice and a rational proof. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the Hanafi responses.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Summarize: automatic ba'in talaq after four months without intercourse; expiation required if he returns within the period.
This is the reference point.
2
State the Shafi'i position (old view)
Separation occurs only through qadi's ruling; the qadi's separation is a raj'i talaq. Also, no expiation upon return because the Quran promises forgiveness.
The new view of Shafi'i aligns with Hanafi on expiation but still requires qadi for separation.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i analogizes to impotence: the husband is preventing the wife's right, so the qadi steps in to release her.
This qiyas is central to their argument.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to each Shafi'i argument
For the qiyas: the qadi is not needed because the law itself dissolves the marriage after the fixed period. For expiation: forgiveness in the Hereafter does not negate worldly expiation.
The Hanafi rely on Companion practice and a different interpretation.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Hanafi, no court needed; under Shafi'i, wife must go to court. Also, in Shafi'i old view, the separation is raj'i, so the husband can take her back without a new marriage; in Hanafi, it is ba'in.
This has significant implications for the wife's status.

باب الإيلاء
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
القاضي لانه مانع حقها في الجماع فينوب القاضي منابه فى التسريح كما فى الجب والعنة ولنا انه ظلمها بمنع حقها فجازاه الشرع بزوال نعمة النكاح عند مضى هذه المدة وهو الماثور عن عثمان وعلى والعبادلة الثلاثة وزيد بن ثابت رضوان الله عليهم اجمعين و كفى بهم قدوة ولانه كان طلاقافي الجاهلية فحكم الشرع بتاجيله الى انقضاء المدة
ترجمہ . پس اگر چار ماہ میں عورت کے ساتھ وطی کر لی تو اپنی قسم میں حانث ہو جائے گا اور اس پر کفارہ لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یمین حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے مرتفع ہو جاتی ہے اور اگر اس عورت سے قربت نہیں کی۔ حتی کہ چار ماہ گزر گئے ۔ تو اس سے ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو گئی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قاضی کے جدا کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مرد اس عورت کے حق جماع کو روکنے والا ہے۔ پس قاضی چھٹکار ا دینے میں اس مرد کے قائم مقام ہوگا ، جیسے مقطوع الذکر اور حنین میں ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد نے عورت کا حق روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے اس کو بدلا دیا کہ اس مدت کے گزر جانے پر نکاح کی نعمت زائل ہو جائے گی اور یہی قول حضرت عثمان علی عبد اللہ بن عمر عبد اللہ ابن عباس اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان بزرگوں کا پیشوا ہونا کافی ہے اور اس لئے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء کرنا طلاق تھا تو شریعت نے اس کی حد اس مدت گزرنے تک مقرر کر دی۔
شخصی
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ کے اندر اندر اس عورت سے ولی کر لی تو شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث ہوگا اور اس پر کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ شوہر اپنی قسم میں حانث تو ہو جائے گا مگر اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کفارہ حانث ہونے کا موجب ہے اور ایلاء قسم ہے اس میں حانث ہو چکا۔ اس وجہ سے اس پر کفارہ لازم ہو گا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پوری آیت ایلاء یہ ہے للذين يؤلون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر فان فائوا فان الله غفور الرحيم و ان عزموا الطلاق فان الله سميع علیم اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مدت ایلاء میں رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے مغفرت کا وعدہ فرمایا ہے اور مغفور کے فعل پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کفارہ واجب نہیں ہو گا ۔ مگر ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ مغفرت کا وعدہ کیا گیا ہے آخرت میں اور کفارہ واجب ہوتا ہے دنیا میں اور مغفرت فی الآخرت وجوب کفارہ فی الدنیا کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ لیکن یہ امام شافعی کا قول قدیم ہے۔ ورنہ قول جدید کی بناء پر ان کے نزدیک بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں۔ بہر حال مدت ایلاء میں ولی کر لینے کے بعد جب حانث ہو گیا اور کفارہ واجب ہو گیا تو ایلا بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا ایلاء ساقط ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر چار ماہ گزرجائیں تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے یمین باقی نہیں رہتی اور یمین ہی کا نام ایلاء ہے پس جب یمین باقی نہ رہی تو ایلاء بھی باقی نہ رہے گا۔ اور اگر شوہر مدت ایلاء میں بیوی کے ساتھ ولی نہیں کر سکا حتی کہ مدت ایلاء یعنی چار ماہ گزر گئے تو علماء احناف کے نزدیک یہ عورت ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائے گی اور سعید بن المسیب اور ابو بکر بن عبد الرحمن بن الحارث کا قول یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ عورت مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد قاضی کے تفریق کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد فرقت کا حکم موقوف رہے گا۔ چنانچہ اگر شوہر نے رجوع کرنے اور فرقت کرنے سے انکار کر دیا اور بیوی نے قاضی سے تفریق کا مطالبہ کیا تو قاضی کی تفریق طلاق رجعی ہوگی اور مبسوط میں یہ ہے کہ طلاق بائن ہوگی اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاکم کو اختیار ہے وہ اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے یا بائنہ یا دو یا تین یا نکاح کو سح کر دے اور امام محمد کامذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ حاکم اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے جیسا کہ امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا بھی یہ قول ہے۔ اصحاب خواہر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد حاکم اس عورت کو طلاق نہ دے، بلکہ اس کو کوڑے مار کر مجبور کرے اور قید میں ڈال دے یہاں تک کہ وہ رجوع کرے یا اس کو طلاق دے امام شافعی کا قول قدیم بھی یہی ہے۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ)
صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے چار ماہ یا زائد وطی نہ کرنے کی قسم کھا کر عورت کے حق جماع کو روک لیا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس سے شوہر کا ارادہ عورت کو ضرر پہنچانا اور ضیق میں مبتلا کرنا ہے۔ پس اصرار کی وجہ سے کیونکہ شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا اس لئے قاصی تشریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا اور قاضی کی یہ تفریق طلاق بائن ہوگی اور ایسا ہے جیسا کہ شوہر اگر مقطوع الذکر یا عمنین ہو تو قاضی شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دیتا ہے اور ان دونوں میں علت مشترکہ امساک بالمعروف فوت ہونے کے وقت عورت سے ضرر کو دور کرنا ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے عورت کے حق جماع کو روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے شوہر کو اس ظلم کا بدلہ اس طرح دیا کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد نعمت نکاح کو زائل کر دیا تا کہ عورت متعلقہ ضرر سے چھٹکارا پا سکے اور ظاہر ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے ذریعہ سے عورت چھٹکارا نہیں پاسکتی اس لئے یہ طلاق بائن ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارا مذ ہب یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد بینونت کا واقع ہونا حضرت عثمان، حضرت علی ،عبداللہ بن نود عبد اللہ بن عباس، عبد اللہ ابن عمر اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان حضرات صحابہ کا پیشوا ہونا ہمارے لئے کافی ہے۔ ہماری دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء طلاق بائن علی الفور تھا۔ یعنی ایلاء کے فورا بعد سے شوہر دائمی طور پر اپنی بیوی سے وطی نہیں کر سکتا تھا پس شریعت نے اس حکم کو مدت ایلاء گزر جانے تک کے لئے موجل کر دیا ہے۔ الہذا اس حکم میں علاوہ تا جیل کے کوئی تصرف نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جس طرح ایلاء کی وجہ سے زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی تھی اسی طرح اس وقت بھی طلاق بائن ہوگی مگر اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلے بینونت علی الفور تھی اور اب بینونت علی التراخی ہے اور جس طرح زمانہ جاہلیت میں بینونت تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں تھی اس طرح اسلام کے بعد بھی تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں رہے گی ۔ چار مہینے کے ساتھ قسم کھائی قسم مدت کے گذر جانے سے ختم ہو جائے گی البتہ اگر مو بد قسم اٹھائی تو وہ باقی رہے گی
فان كان حلف على اربعة اشهر فقد سقطت اليمين لانها كانت موقتة به وان كان حلف على الابد فاليمين
Chapter of Ila'. Commentary on Hidayah volume five. The qadi, because he prevents her right to intercourse, so the qadi takes his place in releasing, as in the case of the castrated and the impotent. And our proof: he oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law punished him by the removal of the blessing of marriage after the passing of this period. And this is narrated from Uthman, Ali, the three Abdallahs, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and they are sufficient as leaders. And because it was divorce in the Jahiliyyah, so the law delayed it until the end of the period. Translation: So if he has intercourse with the woman within four months, he becomes a breaker of his oath and expiation becomes obligatory upon him. Because expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and Ila' is nullified because the oath is removed due to breaking it. And if he does not approach that woman until four months pass, then she becomes ba'in with one talaq. Imam Shafi'i said: she becomes ba'in by the qadi's separation. Because the man is preventing her right to intercourse, so the qadi takes his place in giving release, as in the case of the castrated and the impotent. And our proof: the man oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law gave him the recompense that upon the passing of this period, the blessing of marriage is removed. And this saying is narrated from Uthman, Ali, Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Abbas, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and their leadership is sufficient. And because in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was divorce, so the law set its limit until the passing of that period. Personal: Explanation of the scenario: if the husband has intercourse with this woman within the period of Ila', i.e., four months, then the husband becomes a breaker of his oath and expiation becomes obligatory upon him. Imam Shafi'i says: the husband becomes a breaker of his oath but expiation is not obligatory upon him. Our proof: expiation is the consequence of breaking the oath, and Ila' is an oath, and he has broken it, so expiation becomes necessary. The proof of Imam Shafi'i: the complete verse of Ila' is: 'For those who swear abstention from their wives, a waiting period of four months. Then if they return, indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful. And if they resolve on divorce, indeed Allah is Hearing, Knowing.' From this verse it is understood that in the case of returning within the Ila' period, Allah has promised forgiveness, and expiation is not obligatory for an act that is forgiven. For this reason, expiation will not be obligatory. But our response: forgiveness is promised in the Hereafter, and expiation is obligatory in this world, and forgiveness in the Hereafter does not contradict the obligation of expiation in this world. But this is the old saying of Imam Shafi'i. Based on the new saying, according to him also, expiation will be obligatory, as is our madhhab, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. In any case, after having intercourse within the Ila' period, when he becomes a breaker and expiation becomes obligatory, then Ila' is also nullified. The meaning of Ila' being nullified is that if four months pass, divorce will not occur. The proof is that due to breaking the oath, the oath does not remain, and Ila' is the name of the oath. So when the oath does not remain, Ila' will not remain either. And if the husband could not have intercourse with his wife within the Ila' period such that the Ila' period, i.e., four months, passed, then according to the Hanafi scholars, this woman becomes ba'in with one talaq. And the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab and Abu Bakr ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith is that one raj'i talaq occurs. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya volume five. And Imam Shafi'i said that this woman becomes ba'in by the qadi's separation after the Ila' period passes. That is, after the Ila' period passes, the ruling of separation is suspended. So if the husband refuses to return and refuses to separate, and the wife demands separation from the qadi, then the qadi's separation will be a raj'i talaq, and in al-Mabsut it is that the talaq will be ba'in. And Imam Muhammad said that the ruler has the option: he may give this woman one raj'i talaq, or ba'in, or two, or three, or annul the marriage. And the preferred view of Imam Muhammad is that the ruler should give her one raj'i talaq, as this is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. The view of the Sahibayn is that after the Ila' period passes, the ruler should not give her a talaq, but rather should beat her with whips and imprison her until he returns or divorces her. The old view of Imam Shafi'i is also this. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah) According to the statement of the author of al-Hidayah, the proof of Imam Shafi'i is that the husband swore an oath not to have intercourse for four months or more and prevented the woman's right to intercourse, and it is apparent that the husband's intent is to harm the woman and put her in difficulty. So because of his persistence, since the husband refrained from keeping her with kindness, the qadi in the matter of releasing with kindness will take the place of the husband and separate them, and this separation by the qadi will be a ba'in talaq. And this is similar to when the husband is castrated or impotent, the qadi takes his place and separates them. And in both cases, the common cause is removal of harm from the woman when the ability to keep her with kindness is lost. Our proof: the husband oppressed her by preventing her right, so the law gave the husband the recompense that after the Ila' period passes, the blessing of marriage is removed so that the woman can be free from the harm. And it is apparent that she cannot be freed through a raj'i talaq, so this talaq is ba'in. The author of al-Hidayah says: our madhhab, i.e., the occurrence of separation after the Ila' period passes, is narrated from Uthman, Ali, Abdullah ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn Abbas, and Zaid ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all, and their leadership is sufficient for us. Our second rational proof: in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was an immediate ba'in talaq, i.e., immediately after the Ila', the husband could not permanently have intercourse with his wife. So the law delayed this ruling until the Ila' period passes. Therefore, no change is made in this ruling other than the delay. So just as in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' caused a ba'in talaq, similarly now also a ba'in talaq will occur, with the difference that previously separation was immediate and now it is delayed. And just as in the Jahiliyyah, separation was not contingent on the qadi's separation, similarly after Islam, it will not be contingent on the qadi's separation. If he swore an oath for four months, then the oath is nullified because it was time-bound to it, and if he swore an oath forever, then the oath [remains].
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf ul-Hidaya presents the rulings of Ila' (vow of abstinence) and engages in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and other scholars. It begins by stating the Hanafi position: if the husband has intercourse within the four-month period, he breaks his oath (hanith) and must pay expiation (kaffarah); the Ila' is lifted. If he does not have intercourse and the four months pass, then one ba'in talaq occurs automatically. The passage then contrasts this with Imam Shafi'i's view: separation occurs only through the qadi's ruling, which produces a ba'in talaq. The Hanafi proof is that the husband oppressed the wife by preventing her right, so the law punishes him by dissolving the marriage after the period, narrated from several Companions. A second rational proof is that in the Jahiliyyah, Ila' was immediate ba'in talaq; Islam only delayed it to the end of the period. The passage also discusses a secondary dispute regarding expiation: the Shafi'i school initially held that if the husband returns within the period, no expiation is needed because the Qur'an promises forgiveness. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forgiveness in the Hereafter and legal expiation in this world, noting that the Shafi'i school later changed its view. The passage further records intra-Hanafi differences: some scholars among the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad provide options for the qadi, but the relied-upon view is that one ba'in talaq occurs. The teacher should note the authority weight: this is from the Hanafi madhhab, relying on the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah) and supported by Companion practice.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): A vow (yamin) made by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
الحانث (al-hanith): The one who breaks his oath; here, the husband who has intercourse within the Ila' period.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-ba'in): A final divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i (old view) schools on Ila'?
A) Hanafi: divorce automatic and ba'in; Shafi'i: divorce by qadi and raj'i.
B) Hanafi: no expiation upon return; Shafi'i: expiation required.
C) Both schools agree that divorce is automatic.
D) Hanafi: requires qadi involvement; Shafi'i: automatic.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on Ila' centers on whether divorce is automatic or requires a qadi, and whether expiation is due upon return; the Hanafi view is supported by Companion practice and rational justice.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Ila' After the Period: Automatic Ba'in Divorce in the Hanafi School
Discusses multiple madhhab positions on Ila' and their proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ila' after the period (automatic ba'in divorce), distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Khawarij positions, and explain the Hanafi proofs from the Companions and rational analogy to Jahiliyyah.

Core Idea
Ila' ends with an automatic ba'in divorce after four months—no judge needed, no raj'i possibility.

Ila' is a serious marital vow where a husband swears to abstain from intercourse for four months or more. The schools disagree sharply on what happens when the period expires. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi view that the marriage terminates instantly with an irrevocable divorce, the Shafi'i insistence on judicial separation, and the key arguments behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that after the expiry of the Ila' period, a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce occurs automatically without any intervention by the judge. The ruling is based on the husband's oppression and the precedent from Jahiliyyah.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view, though some early Hanafi authorities differed.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that the marriage does not dissolve automatically. The wife must approach the judge, who gives a raj'i (revocable) divorce. The Khawarij go further, saying no divorce occurs; the husband is punished by flogging until he returns.
Imam Muhammad initially preferred a raj'i divorce by the judge, but the madhhab eventually settled on automatic ba'in.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof analogises Ila' to impotence: the husband's persistence in harm makes him unfit to keep the wife, so the judge steps in as his deputy to separate them, and the separation is a raj'i divorce to allow reconciliation.
The Khawarij rely on a literal reading that the husband must be coerced, not divorced.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that a raj'i divorce does not remove the harm because the husband can return without consent. Only a ba'in divorce terminates the harm effectively. Moreover, the ruling is automatic because the Shari'ah itself removes the nikah blessing as a punishment, independent of the judge.
A second rational proof uses the practice of Jahiliyyah: Ila' immediately caused ba'in divorce then; Islam only postponed it, not changed its nature. Therefore, the divorce remains ba'in and automatic.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In the Hanafi school, the wife becomes ba'in immediately after four months, so she can marry another after her 'iddah. In the Shafi'i school, she must seek the judge's separation, which is raj'i, giving the husband the chance to return during 'iddah.
This difference affects financial obligations and the possibility of reconciliation.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ عورت مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد قاضی کے تفریق کرنے سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد فرقت کا حکم موقوف رہے گا۔ چنانچہ اگر شوہر نے رجوع کرنے اور فرقت کرنے سے انکار کر دیا اور بیوی نے قاضی سے تفریق کا مطالبہ کیا تو قاضی کی تفریق طلاق رجعی ہوگی اور مبسوط میں یہ ہے کہ طلاق بائن ہوگی اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ حاکم کو اختیار ہے وہ اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے یا بائنہ یا دو یا تین یا نکاح کو سح کر دے اور امام محمد کامذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ حاکم اس عورت کو ایک طلاق رجعی دے جیسا کہ امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا بھی یہ قول ہے۔ اصحاب خواہر کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد حاکم اس عورت کو طلاق نہ دے، بلکہ اس کو کوڑے مار کر مجبور کرے اور قید میں ڈال دے یہاں تک کہ وہ رجوع کرے یا اس کو طلاق دے امام شافعی کا قول قدیم بھی یہی ہے۔ (معینی شرح ہدایہ)
صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے چار ماہ یا زائد وطی نہ کرنے کی قسم کھا کر عورت کے حق جماع کو روک لیا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اس سے شوہر کا ارادہ عورت کو ضرر پہنچانا اور ضیق میں مبتلا کرنا ہے۔ پس اصرار کی وجہ سے کیونکہ شوہر امساک بالمعروف سے رک گیا اس لئے قاصی تشریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا اور قاضی کی یہ تفریق طلاق بائن ہوگی اور ایسا ہے جیسا کہ شوہر اگر مقطوع الذکر یا عمنین ہو تو قاضی شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر دونوں میں تفریق کر دیتا ہے اور ان دونوں میں علت مشترکہ امساک بالمعروف فوت ہونے کے وقت عورت سے ضرر کو دور کرنا ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے عورت کے حق جماع کو روک کر اس پر ظلم کیا ہے پس شریعت نے شوہر کو اس ظلم کا بدلہ اس طرح دیا کہ مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد نعمت نکاح کو زائل کر دیا تا کہ عورت متعلقہ ضرر سے چھٹکارا پا سکے اور ظاہر ہے کہ طلاق رجعی کے ذریعہ سے عورت چھٹکارا نہیں پاسکتی اس لئے یہ طلاق بائن ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہمارا مذ ہب یعنی مدت ایلاء گزر جانے کے بعد بینونت کا واقع ہونا حضرت عثمان، حضرت علی ،عبداللہ بن نود عبد اللہ بن عباس، عبد اللہ ابن عمر اور زید بن ثابت رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین سے منقول ہے اور ان حضرات صحابہ کا پیشوا ہونا ہمارے لئے کافی ہے۔ ہماری دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ایلاء طلاق بائن علی الفور تھا۔ یعنی ایلاء کے فورا بعد سے شوہر دائمی طور پر اپنی بیوی سے وطی نہیں کر سکتا تھا پس شریعت نے اس حکم کو مدت ایلاء گزر جانے تک کے لئے موجل کر دیا ہے۔ الہذا اس حکم میں علاوہ تا جیل کے کوئی تصرف نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جس طرح ایلاء کی وجہ سے زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی تھی اسی طرح اس وقت بھی طلاق بائن ہوگی مگر اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلے بینونت علی الفور تھی اور اب بینونت علی التراخی ہے اور جس طرح زمانہ جاہلیت میں بینونت تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں تھی اس طرح اسلام کے بعد بھی تفریق قاضی پر موقوف نہیں رہے گی ۔ چار مہینے کے ساتھ قسم کھائی قسم مدت کے گذر جانے سے ختم ہو جائے گی البتہ اگر مو بد قسم اٹھائی تو وہ باقی رہے گی
Chapter of Ila'. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary of Hidayah Volume 5. Imam Shafi'i said: This woman becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) after the expiry of the Ila' period by the judge's separation. That is, after the expiry of the Ila' period, the ruling of separation is suspended. So if the husband refuses to return (to marital relations) and to separate, and the wife demands separation from the judge, then the judge's separation will be a raj'i divorce. And in al-Mabsut it is that it will be a ba'in divorce. Imam Muhammad said: The ruler has a choice; he may give this woman one raj'i divorce or one ba'in divorce, or two or three, or annul the marriage. And Imam Muhammad's chosen position is that the ruler should give one raj'i divorce, just as Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik also hold this view. The Khawarij's position is that after the expiry of the Ila' period, the ruler should not divorce her, but rather flog her and imprison him until he returns or divorces her. Imam Shafi'i's old view is also this. (Mu'ini Sharh Hidayah). According to the author of Hidayah, Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the husband swore not to have intercourse for four months or more, thereby preventing the woman's right to intercourse. And it is obvious that by this the husband intends to harm the woman and cause her distress. So due to his persistence, since the husband refrained from keeping her with kindness, the judge will stand in place of the husband for separation with kindness, and this separation by the judge will be a ba'in divorce. And it is like the case where if the husband is impotent (maqtū‘ al-dhakar or ‘innīn), the judge stands in place of the husband and separates them. And the common effective cause in both is to remove harm from the woman at the time when keeping with kindness is lost. Our proof is that the husband prevented the woman's right to intercourse and thus oppressed her. So the Shari'ah has punished the husband for this oppression by removing the blessing of marriage after the expiry of the Ila' period so that the woman can get rid of the related harm. And it is obvious that through a raj'i divorce the woman cannot get rid of it, so this divorce is ba'in. The author of Hidayah says: Our madhhab, i.e., that separation occurs after the expiry of the Ila' period, is narrated from 'Uthman, 'Ali, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas, 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, and Zayd ibn Thabit, may Allah be pleased with them all. And the leading status of these Companions is sufficient for us. Our second rational proof is that in the time of Jahiliyyah, Ila' used to result in immediate ba'in divorce. That is, from immediately after the Ila', the husband could not have intercourse with his wife permanently. So the Shari'ah postponed this ruling until the expiry of the Ila' period. Therefore, no further modification is made to this ruling besides the postponement. So just as in Jahiliyyah, Ila' resulted in ba'in divorce, similarly now it will be ba'in divorce, but with the difference that previously the separation was immediate, and now it is delayed. And just as in Jahiliyyah, the separation was not dependent on the judge's separation, similarly after Islam it will not be dependent on the judge's separation. If he swore for four months, the oath is void because it was time-bound. But if he swore perpetually, the oath remains.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling of Ila' (vow of abstinence) after the expiry of the four-month period. It opens by presenting Imam Shafi'i's position that the woman becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) only upon the judge's separation, and that separation is a raj'i divorce according to some narrations, or ba'in according to al-Mabsut. Then it presents Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's view that the judge has discretion to give one raj'i or ba'in divorce, or two or three, or annul the marriage, but his preferred opinion is to give one raj'i divorce, which is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik. The Khawarij (outliers) hold that the judge should not divorce but rather flog and imprison the husband until he returns or divorces. The passage then provides Imam Shafi'i's proof: the husband's oath prevents the wife's right to intercourse, causing harm, so the judge stands in his place to separate them, analogous to impotence cases, and the separation is ba'in. The Hanafi proof is twofold: first, the husband's oppression is punished by the removal of the nikah blessing after the period, which must be a ba'in divorce because a raj'i divorce does not fully remove harm; second, a rational proof tracing the ruling to Jahiliyyah where Ila' caused immediate ba'in divorce, with Islam merely postponing it, so the separation remains automatic and not dependent on the judge. The passage also notes support from several Companions. The author emphasizes that the Hanafi view is that after the expiry, separation occurs automatically as a ba'in divorce without judicial intervention. The last sentence transitions to the next lesson about the details of the oath.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā’): A vow of abstinence where a husband swears not to have sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
بائن (bā’in): An irrevocable divorce that terminates the marriage immediately, and the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage and consent.
رجعی (raj‘ī): A revocable divorce during the ‘iddah period where the husband can return to the wife without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling after the expiry of the Ila' period?
A) The woman becomes divorced automatically with a ba'in divorce.
B) The judge must separate them with a raj'i divorce.
C) The husband is coerced by flogging until he returns.
D) The marriage remains valid unless the husband divorces.

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi law, Ila' ends with an automatic ba'in divorce after four months—no judge, no forgiveness—highlighting the school's emphasis on protecting the wife from harm.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Oath in Ila': Perpetual vs. Limited and Recurrence After Remarriage
Explains rulings of limited and perpetual oaths and recurrence of divorce upon remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a perpetual and a time-bound oath in Ila', state the Hanafi ruling on the recurrence of divorce after remarriage, and identify the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on recurrence before remarriage.

Core Idea
A perpetual oath remains after ba'in divorce and triggers successive divorces upon remarriage, but a time-bound oath expires.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on Ila' when the husband's oath is either limited to four months or expressed as perpetual. The key legal insight is that a perpetual oath does not dissolve upon the first ba'in divorce but continues to bind the husband, causing new divorces each time he remarries without intercourse. A time-bound oath, however, lapses after its term. We also explore a subtle internal disagreement about whether a second divorce can occur before remarriage if the second four-month period ends during the wife's 'iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of oath
Read the opening: if the husband swore not to approach for exactly four months, the oath is time-bound. If he swore without limit (e.g., 'by Allah, I will never approach you'), it is perpetual. Classify each as yamīn muwaqqatāh or yamīn mu’abbadah.
The phrase 'fain kāna ḥalafa 'alā arba'ati ashhur' vs 'wa in kāna ḥalafa 'alāl-abad'.
2
Determine the effect after four months without intercourse
For a time-bound oath: the oath becomes void (saqatat al-yamīn) after four months. For a perpetual oath: a ba'in divorce occurs, but the oath remains (al-yamīn bāqiyah) because no hanth (breaking) happened.
The divorce is automatic in both cases under Hanafi law, but the survival of the oath differs.
3
Analyze the recurrence upon remarriage
If the husband remarries the same woman after the ba'in divorce, if the oath is perpetual, it revives (Ila' returns). Then if he again avoids intercourse for four months, a second divorce occurs. This can happen as many times as remarriage occurs (up to three total). The starting point for counting four months is the date of each new marriage.
The text explicitly says 'fain 'āda fatuzawwajahā 'āda al-īlā'.'
4
Examine the internal ikhtilaf on recurrence before remarriage
The majority of mashāyikh hold that no second divorce occurs before remarriage because after ba'in the wife has no right to intercourse, so the husband is not oppressing by not approaching. Faqih Abu Sahl and author of al-Muhit argue that if the second four-month period ends within the 'iddah, a second divorce does occur because the wife still has a right to revocability? Note: this dispute is about the scenario without remarriage.
This disagreement is recorded in the Tashreeh section.
5
Apply the ruling to subsequent marriages after a third divorce or intermediate marriage
If the husband marries her a third time, the same logic applies and a third divorce occurs after four months if no intercourse. If after a third divorce she marries another man and then returns to the first husband, the original perpetual oath does not cause a new divorce because it was tied to the first ownership, not the new marriage. The oath remains but can only be broken by intercourse or expiation.
This final scenario connects to the earlier dispute about tanzīz (immediate effect) mentioned in the text.

فان كان حلف على اربعة اشهر فقد سقطت اليمين لانها كانت موقتة به وان كان حلف على الابد فاليمين بقية لانها مطلقة ولم يوجد الحنث لترتفع به الا انه لا يتكرر الطلاق قبل التزوج لانه لم يوجد منع الحق بعد البينونة فإن عاد فتزوجها عاد الايلاء فان وطبها والوقعت بمضى اربعة اشهر تطليقة اخرى لان اليمين باقية لاطلاقها وبالتزوج ثبت حقها فيتحقق الظلم ويعتبر ابتداء هذه الايلاء من وقت التزوج فان تزوجها ثالثا عاد الايلاء ووقعت تمضى أشهر اخرى ان لم يقربها لما بيناه فان تزوجها بعد زوج اخر لم يقع بدلك الايلاء طلاق لتقيده بطلاق هذا الملك وهى فرع مسالة التنجيز الخلافية وقد مر من قبل واليمين باقية لاطلاقها وعدم الحنت فان وطيها كفر عن يمينه لوجود الحدث
ترجمہ : اگر چار ماہ پر قسم کھائی تھی تو قسم ساقط ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ قسم اس مدت کے واسطے موقت تھی۔ اور اگر اس نے ابدی (ہمیشہ کے لئے) قسم کھائی ہو تو قسم باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ قسم تو مطلق ہے اور حانث ہونا نہیں پایا گیا تاکہ حانث ہونے سے قسم دور ہو جاتی۔ مگر یہ کہ نکاح میں لانے سے پہلے طلاق مکرر نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بائنہ ہو جانے کے بعد (عورت کا حق روکنا نہیں پایا گیا۔ پس اگر اس نے بائنہ ہو جانے کے بعد پھر اس عورت سے نکاح کرلیا تو ایلا بھی لوٹ آیا۔ پس اگر پہلی کرنی (تو خیر تم لوٹ گئی) ورنہ تو چار ماہ گزرنے پر دوسری طلاق ہوگی۔ کیونکہ قسم تو مطلق ہونے کی وجہ سے (ابھی) باقی ہے اور نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے عورت کا حق ثابت ہو گیا پس ظلم محقق ہوگا اور اس ایلاء کی ابتداء (دوبارہ) نکاح میں لانے کے وقت معتبر ہوگی۔ پھر اگر تیسری بار اس سے نکاح کیا تو ایلا لوٹ آئے گا اور چار ماہ گزرنے پر تیسری طلاق واقع ہوگی بشرطیکہ چار ماہ کے اندر عورت سے قربت نہ کی ہو۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔ پھر اگر دوسرے شوہر کے بعد اس عورت سے نکاح کیا تو اس ایلاء کی وجہ سے کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی اس پہلی ملک کی طلاق کے ساتھ ایلاء کے مقید ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ اختلافی مسئلہ تجزیہ مسئلہ کی فرع ہے اور یہ مسئلہ پہلے گزر چکا۔ اور قسم ابھی تک باقی ہے۔ قسم کے مطلق ہونے اور حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ پھر اگر اس عورت سے اور وطی کر لی تو اپنی قسم کا کفارہ ادا کرے قسم توڑنے کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب چار ماہ گزر گئے اور شوہر نے عورت کے ساتھ وطی نہیں کی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں: ایک یہ کہ چار ماہ عورت کے قریب نہ جانے کی قسم کھائی تھی۔ دوم یہ کہ ہمیشہ کے لئے عورت کے قریب نہ جانے کی قسم کھائی ہے۔ مثلاً کہا: اللہ لا اقربک ابدا یا کہا: واللہ لا اقربک لفظ ابد ذکر کئے بغیر۔ پس صورت اولی میں بغیر وطی کے چار ماہ گزر جانے پر قسم ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں قسم چار ماہ کی مدت کے ساتھ موقت ہے۔ لہذا اس مدت کے گزر جانے سے قسم ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اگر چار ماہ گزر گئے اور شوہر نے وطی نہیں کی تو اس عورت پر ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی اور قسم باقی رہے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں قسم کسی وقت کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے لہذا یمین موبد ہوگی اور موجب حث یعنی وطی کے نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے مولی (شوہر) حانث بھی نہیں ہوا تاکہ یمین مرتفع ہو جاتی۔ اس وجہ سے یمین اپنے حال پر باقی رہے گی۔ البتہ نکاح سے پہلے اگر دوسرے چار ماہ گزر گئے تو عامتہ المشائخ کے نزدیک دوسری طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ بینونت کے بعد عورت کے حق جماع کو روکنا نہیں پایا گیا اس لئے کہ بینونت کے بعد جماع کے سلسلہ میں عورت کا کوئی حق ہی نہیں رہا پس شوہر ظالم نہیں ہوگا اور جب شوہر ظالم نہیں ہے تو زوال نعمت نکاح کے ساتھ اس کو بدلہ بھی نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ فقیہ ابو سہل اور صاحب محیط کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اگر انقضاء عدت سے پہلے پہلے چار ماہ گزر گئے تو دوسری طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور اسی
If he swore for four months, the oath is void because it was time-bound by it. And if he swore for perpetuity, the oath remains because it is absolute and breaking it (hanth) has not occurred to remove it. However, divorce does not recur before marriage because the prevention of right did not occur after separation (baynuna). Then if he returns and marries her, the Ila' returns. Then if he does not have intercourse with her, upon the expiry of four months, another divorce occurs because the oath remains due to its absoluteness, and by marriage her right is established, so oppression is realized, and the commencement of this Ila' is considered from the time of marriage. Then if he marries her a third time, the Ila' returns, and upon the expiry of another four months, a divorce occurs if he does not approach her, due to what we explained. Then if he marries her after another husband, no divorce occurs by this Ila' because it is restricted to the divorce of this ownership, and this is a branch of the controversial issue of tanzīz (immediate effect) which has passed earlier. And the oath remains due to its absoluteness and non-occurrence of hanth. Then if he has intercourse with her, he expiates for his oath due to the occurrence of hanth.
Translation: If he swore for four months, the oath is void. Because the oath was time-bound to that period. And if he swore perpetually (forever), the oath remains. Because the oath is absolute, and the occurrence of hanth has not been found such that the oath would disappear. But before marriage, divorce is not repeated. Because after becoming ba'in (irrevocably divorced), the prevention of her right is not found. So if after becoming ba'in he marries this woman again, the Ila' returns. So if he does not have intercourse (the first time? rather if he does not approach her), then upon the expiry of four months, a second divorce occurs. Because the oath remains due to its absoluteness, and by marriage her right is established, so oppression is realized, and the commencement of this Ila' is considered from the time of the second marriage. Then if he marries her a third time, the Ila' returns, and upon the expiry of four months, a third divorce occurs, provided he has not approached her within four months. Due to the reason we stated. Then if he marries her after another husband, no divorce occurs by this Ila' because the Ila' is restricted to the divorce of this (first) marriage, and this is a branch of the controversial issue of tanzīz (immediate effect) which has passed earlier. And the oath still remains due to its absoluteness and non-occurrence of hanth. Then if he has intercourse with this woman, he must expiate for his oath due to the occurrence of breaking it.
Explanation: The situation is that when four months pass and the husband has not had intercourse with his wife, there are two scenarios: (1) He swore not to approach his wife for four months. (2) He swore not to approach his wife forever, for example saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you ever' or saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you' without mentioning the word 'ever'. In the first scenario, after four months pass without intercourse, the oath is void. Because in this scenario the oath is time-bound to a four-month period. So with the expiry of that period, the oath is void. In the second scenario, if four months pass and the husband has not had intercourse, then one ba'in divorce occurs to this woman, and the oath remains. The proof is that in this scenario the oath is not restricted to any time, so it is a perpetual oath, and due to the absence of the cause of breaking (i.e., intercourse), the husband has not broken his oath such that the oath would be lifted. Therefore the oath remains as it was. However, before marriage, if another four months pass, according to the majority of scholars ('Ammat al-Mashayikh), a second divorce does not occur because after separation, prevention of the right to intercourse is not found, as after separation the woman has no right to intercourse. So the husband is not an oppressor, and when the husband is not an oppressor, he will not be punished by removal of the blessing of marriage. Faqih Abu Sahl and the author of al-Muhit hold that if four months pass before the expiry of the 'iddah, a second divorce will occur.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the effect of the oath in Ila' depending on whether it is limited to four months or perpetual, and the recurrence of divorce upon remarriage. The Arabic text begins with a concise legal statement: if the oath is for four months, it is void; if perpetual, it remains. Then it explains that divorce does not recur before remarriage because after ba'in divorce there is no right to prevent. But if the husband remarries her, the Ila' returns, and if he does not have intercourse, another divorce occurs after four months. This can continue up to three divorces. Interestingly, if he marries her after she has been married to another husband (i.e., after tahlil), this Ila' does not cause divorce because it is tied to the first marriage. The passage then gives an Urdu translation and a detailed clarification (Tashreeh) of the two scenarios. The first scenario: if the oath is only for four months, after four months the oath expires, and no further concern (a ba'in divorce already occurred if he didn't have intercourse? Actually, the text earlier said that if the oath is for four months and he doesn't have intercourse, the oath becomes void, but it seems the divorce occurs automatically, as per the Hanafi view. The Tashreeh clarifies that in the first scenario, after four months without intercourse, the oath is void—implying that no further Ila' remains, but the ba'in divorce has already taken effect from the initial Ila'. In the second scenario, with a perpetual oath, after four months a ba'in divorce occurs, and the oath remains. The Tashreeh then notes a disagreement: according to 'Ammat al-Mashayikh (majority), before remarriage, another four-month period does not cause a second divorce because there is no right to intercourse after ba'in. However, Faqih Abu Sahl and the author of al-Muhit hold that if the second four-month period ends before the 'iddah expires, a second divorce does occur. The passage ends mid-sentence, probably continuing the discussion. This lesson covers the complete unit from the start of the Arabic text to the end of the page, focusing on the details of the oath and its effects.

Key Terms
یمین موبدہ (yamīn mu’abbadah): A perpetual or absolute oath without a time limit, which continues until a hanth (breaking) occurs.
یمین موقتہ (yamīn muwaqqatāh): A time-bound oath limited to a specific period (here four months), which lapses with the end of that period.
حنث (hanth): The breaking of an oath by doing what was sworn not to do (here, having intercourse).
تنجیز (tanzīz): The immediate effect of a prior divorce pronouncement after remarriage, a disputed issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as described, if a husband swears perpetually not to approach his wife, and after four months a ba'in divorce occurs, then he remarries her but again does not have intercourse for four months, what happens?
A) No second divorce occurs because the oath expired.
B) A second ba'in divorce occurs after the second four-month period.
C) The marriage becomes fasid.
D) The husband must expiate for his oath.

Key Takeaway
A perpetual oath of Ila' persists through divorces and can cause successive divorces upon each remarriage, while a time-bound oath expires after its term, and after an intermediate marriage the original oath does not trigger a new divorce.

Ila' After Three Divorces: The Hanafi Position and Imam Zufar's View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ila' after three divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that ila' becomes void after three divorces and contrast it with Imam Zufar's opposing view.

Core Idea
Ila' is a suspended divorce; after three divorces, no divorce remains to suspend, so the ila' becomes void.

In this lesson, we explore a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of ila' when a husband has already divorced his wife three times. While the majority of Hanafi jurists hold that the ila' becomes void and no divorce occurs upon remarriage, Imam Zufar argues that the suspension remains valid. Understanding this dispute clarifies the nature of ila' as a suspended divorce and the limits of its operation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Articulate the majority Hanafi view that ila' becomes void after three divorces, meaning that if the couple remarries, no divorce will occur even if four months pass without intercourse.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar holds that the suspension (ta'liq) remains valid even after three divorces; thus, upon remarriage, if four months pass without intercourse, a divorce would occur.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that ila' is a deferred divorce (talaq mu'ajjal) and it takes effect on a limited number of divorces. After three divorces, no divorce remains to be suspended, so the ila' becomes void.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of divorce counting.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the majority, no divorce falls upon remarriage after three divorces; according to Imam Zufar, a fourth divorce would occur if the period passes without intercourse. The oath itself remains, but only expiation is due if broken.
The difference affects the status of the marriage after remarriage.
5
Locate the authority and tarjih
The majority view is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is chosen by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah. It is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Imam Zufar's view is marjuh (weak) and not acted upon.

Source Text

69. Chapter of Verses. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, Volume 5, the third type will occur because ila', in the matter of divorce, is in the position of a repeated condition, as if the husband had said: 'Every time four months pass and I do not approach you in them, you are irrevocably divorced.' And if the husband had specified this repeated condition, the ruling would be what we have stated. Therefore here too the same ruling will apply. And if after separation and passing of the iddat, this mooli (husband) again marries this woman, then ila' will also return. So if he has intercourse during the period of ila', the oath is broken and expiation of the oath becomes necessary; and if he did not have intercourse, then upon the passing of four months, a second divorce will occur. Because the oath, being absolute with respect to time, still remains; and due to remarriage, the woman's right is established, so injustice is realized. So through an irrevocable divorce this injustice will be removed, and the period of the second ila' will begin from the time of remarriage. But if remarriage occurred before the passing of the iddat, then the period of the second ila' will begin from the time of divorce, not from the time of remarriage (from al-Inayah). Then if he marries her a third time, ila' will return and upon passing of four months, a third divorce will occur, provided he did not have intercourse with the woman during that period. The proof has passed previously that the oath, being absolute with respect to time, still remains; and due to remarriage, the woman's right is established, so injustice will be realized (from al-Inayah). The author says: When through three divorces severe prohibition (hurmat ghalizah) is established for this woman, then she married another husband and also found a guardian; then the second husband divorced this woman and her iddat also passed. Then if the first husband, i.e., the mooli, marries this woman, no divorce will occur due to this ila'. Because this ila' was only tied to the first ownership. That is because ila' is in the position of suspension of divorce, and this issue is a branch of the disputed issue of tanziz which has passed in the Chapter of Oaths in Divorce: that according to Imam Zufar, suspension does not become void, and according to us it becomes void. It is stated in al-Mabsut: Whoever performed ila' from his wife, saying: 'By God, I will not have intercourse with you,' then he gave her three divorces unqualifiedly (munajjiz), then according to us the ila' became void, and according to Imam Zufar it did not become void. Our proof is that ila' is a deferred divorce, and it takes effect on a limited number of divorces; after three divorces have fallen upon this woman, no divorce remains, so ila' did not remain either. Similarly, if she became irrevocably divorced three times through this ila', then after a second husband he married her, then according to us ila' became void, and according to Imam Zufar it did not become void; however, the oath will remain. Because the oath is absolute with respect to time, and due to the absence of intercourse, he is not found to be a breaker of the oath; then if he has intercourse with this woman, he should pay the expiation of his oath, because now breaking the oath is realized. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of ila' after remarriage and after three divorces. The author explains that if a husband performs ila' (vow to abstain from intercourse for four months) and then divorces his wife irrevocably, and after her iddat remarries her, the ila' returns. If he has intercourse during the new marriage, his oath is broken and he must pay kaffarah; if not, after four months a second divorce occurs. This repeats for a third marriage. However, if three divorces have already occurred (making her haram for him unless she marries another), and then she marries another, gets divorced, and returns to the first husband, the original ila' does not cause a divorce because according to the Hanafi school, ila' is like a suspended divorce and after three divorces there is no remaining divorce to be suspended. Imam Zufar holds that the suspension remains valid. The author provides the Hanafi proof: ila' is a deferred divorce, and after three divorces no further divorce can be suspended, so the ila' becomes void. The oath itself (the vow) remains but only expiation is due if broken, not a divorce.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more, which may result in a divorce if he does not break his oath.
تعليق الطلاق (ta‘līq al-ṭalāq): Suspending the occurrence of a divorce upon a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the ila' after a husband divorces his wife three times, she marries another, and then returns to the first husband?
A) The ila' remains valid, and if four months pass without intercourse, a fourth divorce occurs.
B) The ila' becomes void, and no divorce occurs upon remarriage.
C) The ila' becomes void, but the husband must still pay kaffarah for his oath.
D) The ila' is transferred to the second husband.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a suspended divorce; after three divorces, no divorce remains to be suspended, so the ila' becomes void—a key distinction from the mere oath, which may still require expiation.

Ila' Invalid if Vow is for Less Than Four Months
States the final ruling and justification for ila' with short vow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a vow of abstinence for less than four months does not constitute ila', and trace the intra-Hanafi dispute including Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction.

Core Idea
A vow for less than four months is not ila' – adopted by Abu Hanifa after retracting based on Ibn Abbas's fatwa.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on ila' (a husband's oath to abstain from intercourse). The key point is that the oath must be for four months or more; a shorter oath does not bring the rules of ila' into effect. Imam Abu Hanifa initially held otherwise but retracted upon learning of Ibn Abbas's fatwa, which the Hanafi school treats as an authoritative interpretation (tafsir) of the Quranic text. We will walk through the textual and rational proofs, the intra-school difference, and the reasoning behind the final position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the final Hanafi ruling: a vow to abstain for less than four months does not make a man a mooli (one who performs ila').
This is a condition for the validity of ila'.
2
Examine the primary proof
Analyze the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'لا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر' – explain its legal force and why it is considered tafsir (interpretation) rather than an addition to the Quran.
Ibn Abbas's statement is from prophetic knowledge (muqaddarat).
3
Understand the rational proof
Follow the rational argument: if a man vows for one month, his abstention after that month is without impediment; such voluntary abstention cannot trigger divorce.
Analogous to a man who abstains without any oath.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the earlier view of Imam Abu Hanifa (same as Ibn Abi Layla) and note the retraction upon hearing Ibn Abbas's fatwa.
This shows the importance of prophetic tradition over initial qiyas.
5
Apply the ruling
Work through the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference between the two positions in a concrete scenario.
Ensure understanding of when a divorce would or would not occur.
