ترجمہ. پس اگر چار ماہ سے کم پر قسم کھائی تو یہ ایلاء کرنے والا نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ ابن عبائش کا قول ہے کہ چار ماہ سے کم میں ایلاء 
باب الايلاء
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم نہیں ہوتا اور اس لئے کہ (مولی ) کا عورت کے قریب جانے سے اکثر میں رکنا بغیر مانع کے ہے اور اس جیسے امتناع سے طلاق کا حکم
ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے چار ماہ سے کم اپنی بیوی کے قریب نہ جانے کی قسم کھائی تو شخص مولی یعنی ایلاء کرنے والا نہیں ہو گا مثلا کہاو الله لا اقربك شهرا یا کہاو الله لا اقریك شهرین - یا کہا والله لا اقربك ثلاثة اشهر اور ابن ابی لیلی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ شخص مولی ہے اگر چار ماہ تک اپنی اس بیوی سے وطی نہ کی تو یہ مطلقہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ شروع میں یہی فرماتے تھے مگر جب ان کو ابن عباس کا فتویٰ لا ایلاء فيما دون اربعة اشهر پہنچا تو حضرت امام صاحب نے اپنے قول سے رجوع فرما لیا تھا۔
مگر ابن عباس کا یہ فتویٰ ظاہر نص کے خلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے للذین یؤلون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر - اس آیت میں ایلاء مطلق ہے اور تربص چار ماہ کی مدت کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ پس آیت کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ایلاء کیا اگر چہ مدت قلیلہ کے ساتھ ہو مثلاً ایک دن کا یا اس سے بھی کم کا تو اس شخص پر چار ماہ کا تربص ( انتظار کرنا ، رکنا ) لازم ہوگا۔ پس ایلاء کو چار ماہ کی مدت کے ساتھ مقید کر نانص پر زیادتی کرنا ہے اور ابن عباس کے فتویٰ سے نص پر زیادتی کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ پس ابوحنیفہ نے اپنے قول سے کس لئے رجوع فرمایا۔
جواب :۔ ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کا یہ فتویٰ مقدرات میں واقع ہوا ہے اور مقدرات شرعیہ میں رائے کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ابن عباس نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر یہ فتویٰ دیا ہے اور کسی سے اختلاف بھی منقول نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس فتوی کونص کی تفسیر قرار دیں گے۔ نہ کہ تقلید اور آیت کی تقدیری عبارت ہوگی للذين يؤلون من نسائهم اربعة اشهر تربص اربعة اشهر یعنی ان لوگوں کے لئے جو اپنی عورتوں سے چار ماہ کا ایلاء کرتے ہیں چار ماہ تک کی مہلت ہے۔ پس آیت میں اول اربعۃ اشہر کو ثانی کے دلالت کرنے کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا ہے۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ جس شخص نے چار ماہ سے کم قسم کھائی ۔ مثلاً کہا کہ خدا کی قسم میں ایک ماہ اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ قربت یعنی وطی نہیں کروں گا۔ تو اب اس شخص کا ایک ماہ سے زائد مدت میں یعنی دوسرے تیسرے اور چوتھے ماہ میں وطی اور قربت سے رکنا بغیر مانع کے ہوگا کیونکہ بعد کے تین ماہ میں عدم قربان کی قسم نہیں پائی گئی ہے اور ایسی قسم جو چار ماہ سے کم پر منعقد ہو اس سے چار ماہ گزرنے پر طلاق کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسا کہ ایک شخص بغیر یمین کے چار ماہ یا اس سے زائد اپنی بیوی سے دلی نہیں کر سکا۔ تو اس صورت میں چار ماہ گزر جانے پر کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ ( عنایہ ) فواد فیہ کی نمیر کے مرجع میں تین احتمال ہیں (۱) اس ضمیر کا مرجع امتناع کو قرار دیا جائے (۲) اس حلف کو مرجع بنا ئیں جو بمثلہ سے مفہوم ہے (۳) اکثر مدت کو مرجع قرار دیا جائے۔ واضح ہو کہ صاحب ہدایہ اگر ولان الامتناع عن قربانها في بعض المدة فرما دیتے بجائے اکثر مدت کے ، تو عبارت زیادہ واضح ہو جاتی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
So if he swore an oath for less than four months, he is not a mooli (one who performs ila'), due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no ila' for less than four months,' and because his abstention from approaching her (the wife) for the greater part of the period is without an impediment, and by such abstention the ruling of divorce is not established. Translation: So if he swore an oath for less than four months, he will not be a mooli, i.e., one who performs ila'. Because Ibn Abbas said that there is no ila' for less than four months, and because the mooli's refraining from approaching the woman for the greater part of the period is without an impediment, and by such abstention the ruling of divorce is not established. Explanation of the case: If a person swears not to approach his wife for less than four months, e.g., he said: 'By God, I will not approach you for a month,' or 'By God, I will not approach you for two months,' or 'By God, I will not approach you for three months,' then Ibn Abi Layla says that such a person is a mooli; if he does not have intercourse with this wife for four months, she will become irrevocably divorced. Imam Abu Hanifa initially said the same, but when Ibn Abbas's fatwa 'There is no ila' for less than four months' reached him, Imam Sahib retracted from his statement. But this fatwa of Ibn Abbas is contrary to the apparent text (nass). Because Allah Almighty said: 'For those who swear off their wives, there is a waiting period of four months.' In this verse, ila' is absolute and the waiting period is restricted to four months. So the requirement of the verse is that whoever performs ila' with his wife, even if it be for a short period, e.g., one day or less, then a waiting period of four months becomes necessary for him. So restricting ila' to a period of four months is an addition to the text (nass), and adding to the text through Ibn Abbas's fatwa is impermissible. So why did Abu Hanifa retract from his statement? Answer: This fatwa of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) occurs in matters of legal estimation (muqaddarat), and in legal estimation opinion has no role. So it became known that Ibn Abbas gave this fatwa after hearing from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and no disagreement from anyone is transmitted. Therefore, this fatwa will be considered an interpretation of the nass, not a rejection. And the estimated expression of the verse would be: 'For those who perform ila' from their wives for four months, a waiting period of four months.' So in the verse, the first 'four months' has been omitted due to the second indicating it. The rational proof is that a person who swore an oath for less than four months, e.g., said: 'By God, I will not have intercourse with my wife for one month,' then this person's abstention from intercourse in the period beyond one month, i.e., the second, third, and fourth months, is without an impediment, because no oath of abstention is found for the later three months. And from an oath taken for less than four months, the ruling of divorce is not established upon the passage of four months, just as if a person without an oath did not have intercourse with his wife for four months or more, then in this case upon the passage of four months no divorce occurs (from al-Inayah). Regarding 'fīhi' (in it), there are three possibilities for the referent of the pronoun: (1) the referent is 'abstention', (2) the referent is 'this oath' which is understood from 'bi-mithlihi', (3) the referent is 'the greater part of the period'. It would be clearer if the author of al-Hidayah had said 'wa lāna al-imtinā‘ 'an qurbānihā fī ba‘ḍ al-mudda' instead of 'fī akthar al-mudda'. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that a vow to abstain from sexual intercourse for a period shorter than four months does not constitute legal ila' and therefore cannot result in a divorce upon the passage of four months. The primary proof is the statement of Ibn Abbas (ra) that there is no ila' for less than four months. The text also presents a rational proof: if a man swears to abstain for only one month, his continued abstention in the subsequent months (second, third, fourth) is not due to his oath but simply his own choice, and such voluntary abstention without a covering oath cannot trigger a divorce. Initially, Imam Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abi Layla held that any such oath, even for less than four months, constitutes ila'. However, when Imam Abu Hanifa learned of Ibn Abbas's fatwa, he retracted his earlier opinion. The text addresses an apparent objection: Ibn Abbas's fatwa seems to add a restriction to the Quranic verse, which mentions ila' without specifying a minimum period. The response is that Ibn Abbas's fatwa is based on prophetic knowledge (since he heard directly from the Prophet) and pertains to legal estimations (muqaddarat) where personal opinion has no place. Therefore, it is considered an interpretative clarification of the verse, not an addition. The rational proof further supports that the oath must cover the entire four-month period for it to have legal effect.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā’): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more, which may result in a divorce if he does not break his oath.
مقدرات شرعية (muqaddarāt shar‘iyyah): Legal matters that are estimated or determined by divine revelation, not by human reasoning, such as waiting periods, prescribed shares, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a man swears not to approach his wife for one month and then, without resuming intercourse, remains apart for four months?
A) He is a mooli and his wife becomes divorced after four months.
B) He is not a mooli and no divorce occurs.
C) He is a mooli but only if he explicitly intended ila'.
D) He must pay kaffarah for breaking his oath because he exceeded one month.

Key Takeaway
A vow to abstain from intercourse must be for four months or more to constitute valid ila' in the Hanafi school; otherwise, the rules of ila' do not apply.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Ila' Requires Oath of Four Months or More
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute on the duration required for Ila'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for Ila' and explain why an oath of less than four months does not constitute Ila', citing the Quranic proof and the reversal of Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
Ila' requires an oath of four months or more; a shorter oath does not trigger the waiting period.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author clarifies the definition of Ila'—a vow of abstinence from marital relations. While some early scholars, including Imam Abu Hanifa initially, held that any oath of abstinence constitutes Ila', the school later settled that the oath must be for four months or more. We will examine the Quranic text, the rational proof, and the role of Ibn Abbas's fatwa in resolving the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on Ila' duration
Identify the act: a husband swears not to approach his wife. The ruling: he becomes a Muli only if the oath is for four months or more. If less, he is not a Muli.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Ibn Abi Layla held that any oath of abstinence, regardless of duration, constitutes Ila'. Imam Abu Hanifa initially agreed but later retracted.
The dispute is within the early Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Verse 2:226 says: 'For those who take an oath of abstention from their wives, a waiting period of four months.' The Hanafi interpretation is that the oath itself must be for four months, as indicated by the implication of the waiting period.
The opposing view reads the verse as absolute regarding the oath duration.
4
Understand the rational proof
If a man swears for one month, his abstention in the subsequent three months is without an oath, so no Ila' is established. This is analogous to a man who abstains without any oath—no divorce occurs after four months.
This proof supports the condition that the oath must cover the full four months.
5
Note the significance of Ibn Abbas's fatwa
Ibn Abbas's statement 'There is no Ila' for less than four months' is accepted as a prophetic interpretation of the verse, not an independent opinion. Abu Hanifa retracted based on this authoritative fatwa.
This demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on Sahaba's interpretations in matters of muqaddarat.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم نہیں ہوتا اور اس لئے کہ (مولی ) کا عورت کے قریب جانے سے اکثر میں رکنا بغیر مانع کے ہے اور اس جیسے امتناع سے طلاق کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے چار ماہ سے کم اپنی بیوی کے قریب نہ جانے کی قسم کھائی تو شخص مولی یعنی ایلاء کرنے والا نہیں ہو گا مثلا کہاو الله لا اقربك شهرا یا کہاو الله لا اقریك شہرین - یا کہا والله لا اقربك ثلاثة اشهر اور ابن ابی لیلی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ شخص مولی ہے اگر چار ماہ تک اپنی اس بیوی سے وطی نہ کی تو یہ مطلقہ بائنہ ہو جائے گی حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ شروع میں یہی فرماتے تھے مگر جب ان کو ابن عباس کا فتویٰ لا ایلاء فيما دون اربعة اشهر پہنچا تو حضرت امام صاحب نے اپنے قول سے رجوع فرما لیا تھا۔
مگر ابن عباس کا یہ فتویٰ ظاہر نص کے خلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے للذین یؤلون من نسائهم تربص اربعة اشهر - اس آیت میں ایلاء مطلق ہے اور تربص چار ماہ کی مدت کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ پس آیت کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ایلاء کیا اگر چہ مدت قلیلہ کے ساتھ ہو مثلاً ایک دن کا یا اس سے بھی کم کا تو اس شخص پر چار ماہ کا تربص ( انتظار کرنا ، رکنا ) لازم ہوگا۔ پس ایلاء کو چار ماہ کی مدت کے ساتھ مقید کر نانص پر زیادتی کرنا ہے اور ابن عباس کے فتویٰ سے نص پر زیادتی کرنا نا جائز ہے۔ پس ابوحنیفہ نے اپنے قول سے کس لئے رجوع فرمایا۔
جواب :۔ ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما کا یہ فتویٰ مقدرات میں واقع ہوا ہے اور مقدرات شرعیہ میں رائے کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ابن عباس نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر یہ فتویٰ دیا ہے اور کسی سے اختلاف بھی منقول نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس فتوی کونص کی تفسیر قرار دیں گے۔ نہ کہ تقلید اور آیت کی تقدیری عبارت ہوگی للذين يؤلون من نسائهم اربعة اشهر تربص اربعة اشهر یعنی ان لوگوں کے لئے جو اپنی عورتوں سے چار ماہ کا ایلاء کرتے ہیں چار ماہ تک کی مہلت ہے۔ پس آیت میں اول اربعۃ اشہر کو ثانی کے دلالت کرنے کی وجہ سے ترک کر دیا ہے۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ جس شخص نے چار ماہ سے کم قسم کھائی ۔ مثلاً کہا کہ خدا کی قسم میں ایک ماہ اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ قربت یعنی وطی نہیں کروں گا۔ تو اب اس شخص کا ایک ماہ سے زائد مدت میں یعنی دوسرے تیسرے اور چوتھے ماہ میں وطی اور قربت سے رکنا بغیر مانع کے ہوگا کیونکہ بعد کے تین ماہ میں عدم قربان کی قسم نہیں پائی گئی ہے اور ایسی قسم جو چار ماہ سے کم پر منعقد ہو اس سے چار ماہ گزرنے پر طلاق کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسا کہ ایک شخص بغیر یمین کے چار ماہ یا اس سے زائد اپنی بیوی سے دلی نہیں کر سکا۔ تو اس صورت میں چار ماہ گزر جانے پر کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ ( عنایہ ) فواد فیہ کی نمیر کے مرجع میں تین احتمال ہیں (۱) اس ضمیر کا مرجع امتناع کو قرار دیا جائے (۲) اس حلف کو مرجع بنا ئیں جو بمثلہ سے مفہوم ہے (۳) اکثر مدت کو مرجع قرار دیا جائے۔ واضح ہو کہ صاحب ہدایہ اگر ولان الامتناع عن قربانها في بعض المدة فرما دیتے بجائے اکثر مدت کے ، تو عبارت زیادہ واضح ہو جاتی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Section of Ila'. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Five: It does not happen because the Muli's refraining from approaching the wife is mostly without an impediment, and from such abstinence the ruling of divorce is not established. Explanation: The case is that if a person swore an oath not to approach his wife for less than four months, then that person is not a Muli (one who performs Ila'), e.g., he said 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a month' or 'for two months' or 'for three months'. Ibn Abi Layla says that this person is a Muli; if he does not have intercourse with this wife for four months, she becomes irrevocably divorced. Imam Abu Hanifa initially held this view, but when the fatwa of Ibn Abbas reached him — 'There is no Ila for less than four months' — Imam Sahib retracted his statement. However, this fatwa of Ibn Abbas apparently contradicts the text because Allah Most High said: 'For those who take an oath of abstention from their wives, a waiting period of four months.' In this verse, Ila is absolute, and the waiting period is confined to four months. So the requirement of the verse is that whoever performs Ila with his wife, even if for a short period, e.g., a day or less, then a waiting period of four months becomes obligatory upon him. Thus confining Ila to a four-month term is an addition to the text, and it is not permissible to add to the text through Ibn Abbas's fatwa. So why did Abu Hanifa retract his statement? Answer: This fatwa of Ibn Abbas is concerning the divinely ordained measures (muqaddarat), and reason has no place in the divinely ordained measures. So it is known that Ibn Abbas gave this fatwa having heard it from the Prophet, and no disagreement is reported. Therefore this fatwa will be considered an interpretation of the text, not an independent opinion (taqlid). And the implied meaning of the verse would be: 'For those who take an oath of abstention from their wives for four months, a waiting period of four months.' So in the verse, the first 'four months' is omitted due to indication of the second. The rational proof is that if a person swore for less than four months, e.g., he said 'By Allah, I will not have intercourse with my wife for one month', then his refraining from intercourse in the period exceeding one month — i.e., in the second, third, and fourth month — is without an impediment, because no oath of abstention exists for the subsequent three months. And such an oath that is contracted for less than four months does not establish the ruling of divorce after four months have passed. Just as if a person without an oath refrains from his wife for four months or more, then when four months pass, no divorce occurs. (Inayah) Benefit: In 'ha' of 'fish' the referent has three possibilities: (1) the pronoun refers to 'abstention', (2) it refers to 'oath' understood from the context, (3) it refers to 'most of the period'. It is clear that if the author of Hidayah had said 'because the abstention from approaching her in some of the period' instead of 'most of the period', the expression would be clearer. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and dispute concerning the definition of Ila' (a vow of abstention from sexual relations with one's wife). The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: if a man swears not to approach his wife for less than four months, he does not become a 'Muli' (one who commits Ila'). The reason given is that a true Muli's refraining must be for most of the period without any legal impediment; otherwise, the ruling of divorce after four months does not apply. The text then contrasts this with the view of Ibn Abi Layla, who considered such a person a Muli, leading to a revocable divorce if intercourse does not occur within four months. Notably, Imam Abu Hanifa initially held this opposing view but retracted upon learning the fatwa of Ibn Abbas that 'there is no Ila for less than four months'. The passage then addresses a potential objection: Ibn Abbas's fatwa appears to contradict the apparent meaning of Quran 2:226, which mentions Ila in absolute terms and then imposes a four-month waiting period. The Hanafi response is that Ibn Abbas's fatwa concerns the 'divinely ordained measures' (muqaddarat), where human reason has no place. Therefore, Ibn Abbas's statement is accepted as a prophetic interpretation (tafsir) of the verse, not an independent opinion. The verse is understood by implication to mean: 'For those who take an oath of abstention from their wives for four months, there is a waiting period of four months.' The rational proof (dalil 'aqli) is provided: if a man swears for only one month, his abstention in the subsequent three months is without oath, so no Ila is established. The passage concludes with a textual note from 'Inayah clarifying the possible referents of the pronoun in the original Hidayah text.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-Ila'): A vow of abstention from sexual relations with one's wife, usually with an oath, which if continued for four months leads to divorce.
مولي (Muli): The husband who performs Ila' by swearing to abstain from his wife for four months or more.
تربص (tarabbus): The waiting period of four months imposed on the husband who has performed Ila', during which he may return to his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband swears not to approach his wife for two months, what is the Hanafi ruling according to the text?
A) He becomes a Muli and if he does not have intercourse within four months, divorce occurs.
B) He does not become a Muli because the oath is for less than four months.
C) He becomes a Muli only if he swears for exactly four months.
D) The ruling depends on whether he intends divorce.

Key Takeaway
Ila' only occurs when the husband swears to abstain for four months or more; a shorter oath does not impose the waiting period.

Compounding Oaths for Ila'
Explains when multiple oaths combine to form a valid Ila' and when they do not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on compounding oaths to determine whether a husband's multiple oaths constitute a valid Ila'.

Core Idea
Two oath periods combine only if said without pause or repetition of key words; otherwise, each stands alone.

The Hanafi school sets clear conditions for when a husband's multiple oaths to abstain from intercourse combine into a single Ila' period. This lesson unpacks the two key cases: when the oaths merge into a continuous four-month prohibition, and when they remain separate, preventing Ila' from being established. Understanding this distinction ensures correct application of the Ila' rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate the two cases presented: the first where oaths are joined with 'wa' and no interruption, the second where there is a one-day gap and repetition of key words.
The first leads to Ila', the second does not.
2
Understand the condition for combination
Combination requires three conditions: the co-ordinate clause does not repeat 'Allah' or the negative particle, and there is no pause (fasl) between the clauses.
If any condition is missing, the second oath is independent.
3
Apply the principle to the second case
In the second case, three conditions are absent: the name 'Allah' and the negative are repeated, and there is a one-day pause. Hence the second oath is independent.
The total prohibition period does not reach four months.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
The text states that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad agree with this ruling, indicating it is not exclusively Hanafi.
This consensus strengthens the position.

پس وہ پہلی قسم کے بعد دو ماہ کی ولی سے رک گیا اور دوسری قسم کے بعد اول کی طرف منسوب کرتے ہوئے اس نے اپنے آپ کو ایک دن کم چار ماہ کی ولی سے روک دیا ہے۔ پس دونوں قسموں میں مدت منع ( چار ماہ ) پوری نہیں پائی گئی ۔ اس وجہ سے یہ شخص ایلاء کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا
If he swears with these words: 'I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' then he is a Muli. And if he says, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' then he is a Muli because he joined them with the conjunction, just as if he had joined them with the plural form. Translation: And if he said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' then this person becomes a Muli. Because he joined both with the conjunction, it became like joining with a plural word. Explanation: The case is that if a person said to his wife, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' then this person is a Muli. The proof is that he joined both with the conjunction (wa). So it is as if he joined with the plural form, as if he said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months.' So this is a single oath, and if he has intercourse with his wife during this period, expiation (kaffarah) becomes obligatory upon him. If the husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months' and then remained silent for a day, then said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' he is not a Muli. And if he remained for a day, then said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' he is not a Muli because the second is an independent beginning. And he became prohibited by the first oath for two months, and by the second for four months, except for the day he remained, so the period of prohibition is not complete. Explanation: The case is that if the husband said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months' and remained silent for a day, then said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' then this person is not a Muli. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad are of the same view. The principle is that if the name 'Allah' is not mentioned in the co-ordinate clause, nor is the negative particle mentioned, and there is no pause between the first and second clauses, then the ruling of the co-ordinate is included in the ruling of the first. As in the above case. But if any of these three conditions is missing, then the second speech is independently binding, having no connection with the first speech. Therefore, in the second case, he is not a Muli because these three conditions are absent. There is a separation of one day between the first and second, and the word 'Allah' and the negative particle are repeated in the co-ordinate. So he refrained from intercourse for two months by the first oath, and by the second oath he prevented himself from intercourse for four months minus one day, attributing it to the first. Thus in both oaths, the period of prohibition (four months) is not complete. For this reason, this person is not a Muli.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a principle about when multiple oaths combine to form a valid Ila'. Two cases are presented. First, if a husband says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' he becomes a Muli because the conjunction (wa) joins the two periods into a single four-month oath. This is considered one oath, and breaking it requires expiation. Second, if he swears for two months, remains silent for a day, then swears again for two months after the first two, he does not become a Muli. The reason is that the second oath is independent (mubtada'), and the total prohibition is not a continuous four months: the first oath prohibits for two months, the second for four months minus the day of silence, so the cumulative period is less than four full months. The passage mentions that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad agree with this ruling. The underlying principle is that if the co-ordinate clause lacks the name 'Allah', the negative particle, and is not separated by a pause, it is treated as part of the first; otherwise, it is an independent oath. In the second case, all three conditions are absent, so the oaths do not combine. The passage concludes that the man is not a Muli because the prohibited period never reaches four months in either oath alone.

Key Terms
حرف الجمع (harf al-jam'): The conjunction 'wa' (and), which joins two clauses into one.
یمین واحدہ (yamin wahidah): A single oath, which when broken requires one expiation (kaffarah).
فصل (fasl): A separation or interruption between two speeches, here a period of one day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He is a Muli because the total is four months.
B) He is not a Muli because the second oath is independent and the total prohibition is less than four months.
C) He is a Muli only if he intended divorce.
D) He is a Muli only if he said the second oath within the same hour.

Key Takeaway
Two oath periods combine into one Ila' only if they are said without a pause and without repeating the name of Allah or the negative particle.

Oath with Indefinite Exception: Does It Create Ila'?
Inter-madhhab dispute on Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an oath with an indefinite exception and evaluate the Shafi'i/Zufar counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
An indefinite exception in an oath prevents Ila' because the husband can have intercourse without kaffarah.

The Hanafi school addresses a specific dispute: does saying 'I will not approach you for a year except for one day' make the husband a mūlī? Imam Zufar argues yes by analogy to ijarah, but the majority Hanafi position says no. Understanding the reasoning behind each view is crucial for applying Ila' correctly. This lesson walks through the dispute, the proofs, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Recognize that the Hanafi school holds that an oath with an indefinite exception does not constitute Ila'.
2
State the opponent's view
Imam Zufar (and Shafi'i) argue that it does create Ila' by analogy to ijarah.
The opponent is Zufar; Shafi'i also follows this view.
3
Examine the opponent's proof (qiyas)
Understand the analogy: In ijarah, an indefinite exception is deferred to the end to validate the contract; similarly, the excepted day is deferred, making the prohibition nearly a year.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The Hanafi response is that the analogy fails because ijarah requires specification for validity, whereas an oath is valid with indefiniteness. Thus the exception remains indefinite, and the husband can have intercourse without kaffarah.
This is called qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, the husband is not a mūlī, so the wife cannot seek immediate intervention. Under Zufar/Shafi'i, he is a mūlī, and the wife can approach the court after four months of abstention.
This difference has real-world implications for the wife's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال والله لا اقربك سنة الا يو مالم يكن موليا خلافا لزفر وهو يصرف الاستثناء الى اخرها اعتبارا بالاجارة فتمت مدة المنع ولنا ان المولى من لايمكنه القربان اربعة اشهر الابشئ يلزمه ويمكنه ههنالان المستثنى يوم منكر بخلاف الاجارة لان الصرف الى الاخر لتصحيحها فانها لا تصح مع التنكير ولا كذلك اليمين ولــوقـــربـهــا فـي يـوم والباقى اربعة اشهر واكثر صار موليا لسقوط الاستثناء
And if he said, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except for a day,' he is not a mūlī, contrary to Zufar. He (Zufar) refers the exception to the end of the year by analogy to ijarah, so the period of prohibition is completed. Our proof: the mūlī is one who cannot have intercourse for four months except with something that becomes obligatory upon him. Here he can do so because the excepted day is indefinite (nakirah), unlike ijarah where the exception is referred to the end to validate it, as ijarah is not valid with indefiniteness. The oath is not like that. And if he has intercourse with her on a day while four months or more remain, he becomes a mūlī because the exception has dropped.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning Ila'. The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) holds that an oath saying 'I will not approach you for a year except for one day' does not constitute Ila', because the excepted day is indefinite (nakirah) – it could be any day. Since the husband can have intercourse on that indefinite day without incurring any kaffarah, the condition of being unable to approach for four months without obligation is not met. Imam Zufar (and Imam Shafi'i) disagree, analogizing to ijarah: in a rental contract, if one says 'I rent this house for a year except one day,' the exception is pushed to the end to preserve the contract's validity. They apply the same logic here, so the excepted day is the last day of the year, making the prohibition nearly a full year, thus Ila' occurs. The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: ijarah requires specification to be valid, so the exception must be deferred to avoid invalidity. But an oath is valid even with indefiniteness, so the exception remains indefinite and no Ila' occurs. However, if the husband actually has intercourse on any day while four months or more remain, the exception is considered dropped and he becomes a mūlī because he has violated the oath's intent.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period exceeding four months, triggering legal consequences.
مول (mūlī): A husband who has taken an oath that prevents him from intercourse for four months without incurring kaffarah.
استثناء (istithnā'): An exception made in an oath, which can affect the ruling on Ila' depending on whether it is definite or indefinite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'Wallahi la aqrabuk sanatan illa yawman' (I will not approach you for a year except for one day), does this constitute Ila'?
A) Yes, because the exception is indefinite and deferred.
B) No, because the exception is indefinite and he can have intercourse without kaffarah.
C) Yes, by analogy to ijarah.
D) No, unless he specifies the exact day.

Key Takeaway
An indefinite exception in an Ila' oath prevents the husband from being a mūlī because it allows intercourse without kaffarah, according to the Hanafi school.

When Intercourse Occurs: The Exception Drops and Ila' Applies
Clarification of when Ila' applies despite an indefinite exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that if a husband has intercourse on an indefinite day while four months or more remain, the exception drops and he becomes a mūlī.

Core Idea
Actual intercourse while four months remain nullifies the indefinite exception, establishing Ila'.

In the previous lesson, we saw that an oath with an indefinite exception does not initially make the husband a mūlī. However, the text adds a critical qualification: if the husband actually has intercourse on any day while four months or more remain of the oath period, the exception is considered dropped. At that point, the husband becomes a mūlī because he can no longer claim the indefinite day as an exception. This lesson explores that condition and its legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger event
The husband has intercourse on a day during the oath period when four months or more remain.
The exact day is not specified; any day qualifies.
2
Explain why the exception drops
Because the husband has now used the indefinite exception, he cannot later rely on it. The entire remaining period becomes a continuous prohibition without exception.
The exception is 'consumed' by the act of intercourse.
3
Apply the definition of mūlī
After the intercourse, the husband cannot have intercourse again for the remaining four months or more without kaffarah. This matches the definition of mūlī.
The condition of being unable to approach for four months without obligation is now met.
4
Note the practical consequence
The wife can now seek judicial intervention after four months from the day after intercourse pass without the husband approaching again.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf if the opposing school applies, but here it's a Hanafi internal consequence.

Source Text

He (Zufar) refers the exception to the end of the year by analogy to ijarah, so the period of prohibition is completed. Our proof: the mūlī is one who cannot have intercourse for four months except with something that becomes obligatory upon him. Here he can do so because the excepted day is indefinite (nakirah), unlike ijarah where the exception is referred to the end to validate it, as ijarah is not valid with indefiniteness. The oath is not like that. And if he has intercourse with her on a day while four months or more remain, he becomes a mūlī because the exception has dropped.

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning Ila'. The Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) holds that an oath saying 'I will not approach you for a year except for one day' does not constitute Ila', because the excepted day is indefinite (nakirah) – it could be any day. Since the husband can have intercourse on that indefinite day without incurring any kaffarah, the condition of being unable to approach for four months without obligation is not met. However, if the husband actually has intercourse on any day while four months or more remain, the exception is considered dropped and he becomes a mūlī because he has violated the oath's intent.

Oath Not to Enter a City: Does It Create Ila'?
Ruling that such an oath does not create Ila' because he can bring her out without obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether an oath not to enter a city where the wife lives constitutes Ila' and explain the rationale based on the possibility of circumvention.

Core Idea
An oath not to enter a city does not create Ila' if the husband can bring his wife out without breaking his oath.

In Hanafi fiqh, Ila' is a specific type of vow that directly prevents marital intercourse for four months without kaffarah. This lesson examines a particular scenario: a husband swears not to enter a city (Kufa) while his wife resides there. Does this make him a mūlī? The Hanafi answer is no, and the reasoning reveals an important principle about the definition of Ila'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is the husband's oath not to enter Kufa. The ruling is that this oath does NOT create the status of Ila'. The husband is not considered a mūlī.
2
Identify the Key Condition of Ila'
For Ila' to occur, the oath must prevent the husband from having intercourse with his wife for four months without incurring a kaffarah. If a legal workaround exists that avoids both the oath and kaffarah, the condition is not met.
The essential element is the inability to have intercourse without kaffarah.
3
Trace the Talil (Reasoning)
The text's reasoning is: 'because he can have intercourse without anything becoming obligatory upon him by bringing her out of Kufa.' The husband can arrange for his wife to leave Kufa (e.g., by sending an agent) so that he can be with her without violating his oath. Thus, the oath does not effectively prevent intercourse.
The talil shows that the possibility of circumvention negates Ila'.
4
Confirm the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school is unanimous that such an oath does not create Ila'. The ruling is mufta bihi and found in Zahir al-Riwayah.
No ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال وهو بالبصرة والله لا ادخل الكوفة وامرأته بهالم يكن موليا لانه يمكنه القربان من غير شي يلزمه بالاخراج من الكوفة
And if he said, while he is in Basra, 'By Allah, I will not enter Kufa,' while his wife is in Kufa, he is not a mūlī because he can have intercourse without anything becoming obligatory upon him by bringing her out of Kufa.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This is a ruling on a specific scenario: a husband swears not to enter a city (Kufa) where his wife resides. According to the Hanafi school, this does not make him a mūlī because the definition of mūlī requires that the husband be unable to have intercourse with his wife for four months without incurring a kaffarah. Here, the husband can have intercourse without violating his oath by bringing his wife out of Kufa (e.g., by sending a representative to relocate her). Thus, he is not prevented from intercourse by his oath in a way that triggers Ila'.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): A vow that prevents intercourse for four months without kaffarah; here the oath does not meet that condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he cannot enter Kufa to approach her.
B) No, because he can bring his wife out of Kufa without breaking his oath.
C) Yes, if he has no agent to bring her out.
D) No, only if the oath was about intercourse directly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an oath not to enter a city does not make one a mūlī if the husband can legally and practically bring his wife out without violating the oath.

intermediate
6 min
Swearing by Hajj, Fast, Sadaqah, 'Itq, or Talaq Creates Ila
Ruling that such oaths create Ila' due to hardship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that swearing by obligations involving hardship creates Ila' and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding swearing by freeing a slave.

Core Idea
A consequence with significant hardship (mashaqqa) makes an oath preventive, even if a remote escape exists.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a husband swears by acts that involve hardship—Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, or divorce—that he will not approach his wife. The text rules that such an oath creates Ila', the legal status of a husband who has sworn to abstain from intercourse. It also presents a disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding the case of freeing a slave. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle that the preventive nature of an oath is judged by the real threat, not hypothetical workarounds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage begins by listing five consequences (Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, divorce) that, when sworn upon as a condition for approaching one's wife, constitute Ila'. The basis is that these consequences involve hardship (mashaqqa), which makes the oath preventive.
The hardship is the key: the husband is deterred because fulfilling the consequence is burdensome.
2
Locate the specific dispute
The text singles out the case of freeing a slave ('itq) and introduces a disagreement with Abu Yusuf. Understand the scenario: the husband says, 'If I approach you, my slave is free.'
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the school is generally agreed on the other four consequences.
3
Outline Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf argues that the husband can sell the slave before approaching, thereby avoiding the consequence. Since he can escape the obligation, the oath does not genuinely prevent intercourse, so it should not be Ila'.
His reasoning is that the preventive effect is negated by a practical alternative.
4
Explain the majority response (Muhammad and Abu Hanifa)
Muhammad (and by implication Abu Hanifa) respond that selling the slave is a remote possibility (mawhum). The immediate threat of freeing the slave is real and deterrent; the hypothetical sale does not remove the prevention. Therefore, it is Ila'.
The principle: remote possibilities do not undermine the current preventive effect.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the majority view: swearing by freeing a slave constitutes Ila'. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling and is applied in fatwa.
The text sides with the majority, emphasizing that selling is mawhum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولو حلف بحج او بصوم أو بصدقة او عتق او طلاق فهومول لتحق المنع باليمين وهو ذكر الشرط والجزاء وهذه الاجزية مانعة لمافيها من المشقة وصورة الحلف بالعتق ان يعلق بقربانها عتق عبده وفيه خلاف ابی يوسف فانه يقول يمكنه البيع ثم القربان فلايلزمه شئ وهما يقولان البيع موهوم فلا يمنع المانعية فيه والحلف بالطلاق ان يعلق بقربانها طلاقها او طلاق صاحبتها وكل ذالك مانع
He said: And if he swore by Hajj, or fasting, or charity, or freeing a slave, or divorce, then he is a mūlī because the prevention is established by the oath. And he mentioned the condition and the consequence, and these consequences are preventive due to the hardship they contain. The form of swearing by freeing a slave is that he makes freeing his slave conditional on approaching her. And in this there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf, for he says: He can sell (the slave) then approach, so nothing becomes obligatory upon him. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: Selling is a remote possibility, so it does not prevent the preventive nature. And the oath by divorce is that he makes her divorce or the divorce of her co-wife conditional on approaching her. And all of that is preventive.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage establishes that when a husband swears by acts of worship – Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, or divorce – that he will not approach his wife, such an oath constitutes Ila'. The reasoning is that these consequences involve great hardship (mashaqqa), so the oath effectively prevents intercourse, fulfilling the definition of Ila'. The text then details the case of 'itq (freeing a slave). If the husband says, 'If I approach you, my slave is free,' Abu Yusuf argues that he can sell the slave first and then approach, so no obligation (kaffarah) applies, and thus it should not be Ila'. However, Imam Muhammad and (presumably) Imam Abu Hanifa respond that selling is a mere hypothetical (mawhum) and does not remove the preventive effect because the slave is currently owned and the threat of freedom is real. The relied-upon position is that it does constitute Ila'. Similarly, swearing by divorce (making divorce conditional on approach) is also preventive. All such oaths are considered Ila'.

Key Terms
مشقة (mashaqqa): Hardship; the quality that makes an act a valid deterrent in the context of Ila'.
عتق ('itq): Freeing a slave; used as a conditional consequence in an oath that may create Ila'.
موهوم (mawhum): A remote or hypothetical possibility; used to argue that selling the slave is not a realistic escape.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if a husband swears by freeing his slave if he approaches his wife, does this constitute Ila'?
A) No, because he can sell the slave first.
B) Yes, because selling is considered a remote possibility (mawhum).
C) Yes, only if the slave is valuable.
D) No, because freeing a slave is a good deed.

Key Takeaway
An oath involving hardship creates Ila' even if a hypothetical escape exists; the majority Hanafi view relies on the principle that mawhum does not negate prevention.

Oaths Constituting Ila' in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on Ila' oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which oaths constitute Ila' according to the Hanafi school and explain the rational proof (talil) that establishes Ila' through burdensome consequences, as well as state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the oath by freeing a slave.

Core Idea
An oath by any burdensome action, not only by Allah, constitutes Ila' if it creates a real deterrent against intercourse.

The Hanafi school expands the scope of Ila' beyond oaths by Allah. This lesson explores the ruling from Al-Hidayah that oaths by Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, or divorce all establish Ila'. The key is the deterrent effect (mana') of the consequence. We will also examine an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding the oath by freeing a slave, and see how the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that oaths by Hajj, fasting, charity, freeing a slave, and divorce all make the husband a muli (one who takes Ila').
This is the core ruling from the matn.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: these consequences are burdensome, creating a preventive effect (mana') against intercourse.
The proof does not come from a specific text but from general legal reasoning (talil).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf objects to the oath by freeing a slave because the slave can be sold. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond that sale is a remote possibility (mawhum) and does not negate the deterrent.
This shows how the Hanafi school handles differing assessments of hypothetical scenarios.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if the husband has intercourse without selling the slave, according to Abu Yusuf no Ila' is established; according to the majority, Ila' is established and leads to divorce after four months.
Understanding the practical consequence is crucial for issuing fatwa.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ حلف بالعتق کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عورت کی قربت پر اپنے غلام کا آزاد ہو نا معلق کرے اور اس ثبوت ایلاء میں ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر اپنے نام کے آزاد ہونے کو مثلاً شوہر نے کہا کہ اگر تجھ سے ولی کروں تو تجھے کو طلاق ہے۔ یا میری فلاں بیوی کو طلاق ہے۔ تو طلاق کے خوف سے اس سے وطی نہیں کر سکتا۔ پس یہی ایلا ء ہے۔ الہذا اگر اس نے چار ماہ کے اندر اندر ولی کر لی تو مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور اگر بغیر ولی کے چار ماہ گزر گئے تو یہ عورت ایک طلاق کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائے گی ۔ واللہ اعلم۔
If he swears by Hajj or fasting or charity or freeing (a slave) or divorce, then he is a muli because the prevention is achieved by the oath, and it is a mention of condition and consequence. These consequences are preventive due to the hardship in them. The form of the oath by freeing a slave is that he suspends the freeing of his slave upon her intimacy. There is a disagreement with Abu Yusuf, for he says: he can sell (the slave) then have intimacy, so nothing is binding on him. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: sale is imagined (unlikely), so it does not negate the preventiveness. The oath by divorce is that he suspends her divorce or the divorce of her co-wife upon intimacy, and all that is preventive. Translation: The author said: If a person swears by Hajj or fasting or charity or freeing a slave or divorce, then he is a muli, because abstention from intimacy is achieved by the oath, and the oath is a mention of condition and consequence. These consequences are preventive because there is severe hardship in them. The form of swearing by freeing a slave is that he suspends the freeing of his slave upon the woman's intimacy, and there is a disagreement of Abu Yusuf in this, because Abu Yusuf says: it is possible for him to sell the slave then have intimacy, so nothing (expiation) is binding on him. The two say: selling is an imagined matter (unlikely), so it does not remove the preventiveness. And the swearing by divorce... Explanation: Previously, the mention of oaths by Allah in Ila' was made. Now, here, oaths without Allah are being commenced... Thus, Imam Quduri said: If he swears by Hajj... or fasting... or charity... or freeing a slave... or divorce... In all these cases, this person will be a muli... The proof is that... when the condition is committed, the consequence will definitely occur, and there is hardship in the occurrence of the consequence... Therefore, in all these cases, Ila' is established... And the author of Hidayah said: The form of the oath by freeing a slave is that he suspends the freeing of his slave upon the woman's intimacy... Abu Yusuf holds that it is not Ila' because the slave can be sold first... The two say that selling is a remote possibility... And the oath by divorce... So, this is Ila'. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah explaining the types of oaths that constitute Ila' (the oath of abstention from marital relations). The core ruling is that Ila' is not limited to oaths by Allah; oaths by other actions that create a significant deterrent also establish Ila'. The author lists five types: Hajj (pilgrimage), fasting, charity, freeing a slave, and divorce. The reasoning is that these actions are burdensome (mushaqqah), so they deter the husband from having intercourse. The text then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the oath by freeing a slave. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that since the husband can sell the slave before having intercourse, the deterrent is not inevitable; hence it does not constitute Ila'. However, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) counter that selling is a remote possibility (mawhum) and does not negate the preventive effect. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two shaykhs, making such an oath valid for Ila'. The passage also clarifies that the oath by divorce, whether it suspends the wife's own divorce or that of a co-wife, is also a valid Ila'. The consequence of Ila' is that if four months pass without intercourse, one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) occurs.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): An oath by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a period of four months or more, which, if maintained, results in a ba'in divorce.
عتق ('itq): Freeing a slave; in this context, it is used as the consequence (jaza') of an oath, i.e., if the husband has intercourse, he must free his slave.
مانع (māni'): A preventive factor that deters the husband from having intercourse, thereby establishing Ila'. The text uses 'māni'' to describe the effect of the oath's consequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an oath by freeing a slave in the context of Ila'?
A) It does not constitute Ila' because the slave can be sold.
B) It constitutes Ila' because selling is a remote possibility.
C) It is invalid because the oath must be by Allah.
D) It is only valid if the slave is not owned by the husband.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes Ila' through oaths by any burdensome action that deters intercourse, and the oath by freeing a slave is valid according to the majority.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Ila' with Revocably vs Irrevocably Divorced Women
Ruling with proof (ta'lil) on Ila' validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Ila' from a revocably divorced woman versus an irrevocably divorced woman and explain the underlying rationale (marital bond).

Core Idea
Ila' requires an existing marital bond; it is valid after revocable divorce but invalid after irrevocable divorce.

Ila' (an oath to abstain from marital relations) is a mechanism that can lead to divorce if four months pass without intercourse. But not every woman is subject to Ila'. This lesson examines a key distinction: the status of the woman – whether she is revocably or irrevocably divorced – determines the validity of the oath. The rule hinges on the presence or absence of the marital bond (zawjiyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is Ila' (an oath to abstain from intercourse). The passage states that Ila' from a revocably divorced woman makes the husband a muli (valid Ila'), while from an irrevocably divorced woman it does not.
The ruling is binary: valid or invalid, based on the type of divorce.
2
Define the two types of divorce
A revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) allows the husband to take his wife back during her 'iddah without a new contract; the marital bond persists. An irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) severs the marriage completely; the husband cannot return except with a new contract.
3
Locate the reason (ta'lil)
The passage provides the reason: 'because the marital bond exists in the first but not in the second.' This is the key legal cause ('illa) that determines the ruling.
The 'illa is the presence or absence of the marital bond.
4
Apply the ruling to hypotheticals
Test: If a man swears to abstain from intercourse with his wife after giving one revocable divorce, the Ila' is valid. If he swears after giving three divorces (irrevocable), the Ila' is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر مطلقہ رجعیہ سے ایلاء کیا مولی ہوگا اور اگر مطلقہ بائنہ سے ایلاء کیا مولی نہیں ہوگا وان الى من المطلقة الرجعية كان موليا وان الى من البائنة لم يكن موليالان الزوجية قائمة في الاولى دون
If he performs Ila' from a revocably divorced woman, he is a muli; and if he performs Ila' from an irrevocably divorced woman, he is not a muli. And if he takes an oath of Ila' from a revocably divorced woman, he is a muli; and if from an irrevocably divorced woman, he is not a muli, because the marital bond exists in the first but not in the second.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This brief passage presents a clear ruling: Ila' is only valid when the marital bond (zawjiyyah) exists. In a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i), the marriage is not fully dissolved; the wife remains in the husband's protection and can be taken back without a new contract. Therefore, an oath of abstinence from intercourse during the 'iddah period constitutes Ila'. If four months pass without intercourse, the Ila' takes effect and a ba'in divorce occurs. In contrast, an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) completely severs the marital bond. Since there is no marriage, there can be no Ila'—the husband cannot be bound by an oath of abstention from relations because there are no marital relations to abstain from. The reason (ta'lil) given is explicit: the marital bond is present in the first case but absent in the second. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqa raj‘iyya): A woman who has been divorced with a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i), meaning the husband can take her back during the 'iddah without a new marriage contract.
مطلقة بائنہ (muṭallaqa bā’ina): A woman who has been divorced with an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in), where the marriage is completely severed and the husband cannot take her back except with a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can Ila' be validly performed from a woman who has been irrevocably divorced (ba'in)?
A) Yes, because she is still his wife.
B) No, because the marital bond no longer exists.
C) Yes, if the husband intends to remarry her.
D) No, only if the divorce was revocable.

Key Takeaway
The validity of Ila' depends on the existence of the marital bond; it is valid with a revocably divorced woman but not with an irrevocably divorced woman.

Ila' with a Revocably Divorced Woman is Valid
States ruling on ila with muttalaqa raj'iyya and refutes objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ila' with a revocably divorced woman and explain the textual basis that overrides the rational objection.

Core Idea
Ila with a revocably divorced woman is valid because the Quranic text includes her as a wife, even if the right to intercourse is absent.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author establishes a key ruling regarding ila' (oath of abstention) when the wife is in a revocable divorce state. The ruling is based on textual inclusion in the Quranic verse 'For those who swear abstinence from their wives' despite a rational objection that the husband is not oppressing a right. We will analyze the proof and the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Note the ruling for revocably divorced woman (valid) and irrevocably divorced woman (invalid).
The distinction hinges on whether the woman remains a wife textually.
2
Understand the proof
The Quranic text 'min nisā'ikum' includes revocably divorced women because they remain wives during iddah, as per verse 'their husbands are more entitled to take them back'.
3
Consider the objection
Objection: no right to intercourse, so husband is not oppressive; why is ila valid?
The passage acknowledges the rational objection.
4
Analyse the response
The response: the text (nass) is authoritative over the underlying rationale (ma'nā). The revocably divorced woman is textually included.
This is a key principle: textual specification over rationale.
5
Determine the consequence
If the iddah expires before the four-month ila period, the ila drops because the locus (the wife) is lost.
This shows the condition that the wife must be in wedlock during the ila period.

Chapter of Ila'. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary Urdu Hidayah Volume 5. Second: And the place of ila is from among our women by the text. So if the waiting period expires before the end of the ila period, the ila drops due to the loss of the locus. Translation: And if he makes ila from his revocably divorced woman, then he will become a muli (one who makes ila). And if he makes ila from an irrevocably divorced woman, then he will not become a muli because in the revocably divorced woman, being a wife is present, and in the irrevocably divorced woman, it is not. And the situation is that the locus of ila is women who are our wives, by the Quranic text. Then if before the passing of the period, the waiting period of the revocably divorced woman passes, then the ila also drops due to the loss of the locus. Explanation: The case is that if a person made ila from his revocably divorced woman, then according to the four imams and the majority of scholars, he will become a muli. And if he made ila from an irrevocably divorced woman, then by consensus he will not be a muli. The proof is that matrimony is present in the revocably divorced woman, and in the irrevocably divorced woman matrimony is not present. And the locus of ila is women who are our wives, because Allah Most High said: 'For those who swear abstinence from their wives.' And after making irrevocable divorce, matrimony does not remain. For this reason, the irrevocably divorced woman will not be the locus of ila. But if he has intercourse with this irrevocably divorced woman, then due to the oath, expiation becomes obligatory. In contrast to the revocably divorced woman, she is the locus of ila because after revocable divorce, matrimony remains. This is why in our view, intercourse with the revocably divorced woman during her waiting period is permissible. Yes, if before the ila period, i.e., four months, the waiting period of the revocably divorced woman ends, then ila drops, because due to the expiry of the waiting period, the locus is lost. Here an objection arises: that ila with a revocably divorced woman should not be valid, because ila is the punishment for oppression by preventing the right to intercourse, and for the revocably divorced woman, there is no right to intercourse, neither past nor future. For this reason, the revocably divorced woman has no authority to demand intercourse. Even that it is recommended for the husband to return without intercourse by words. So the husband is not an oppressor. Therefore, the punishment of the oppressor, i.e., ila, should not apply. The answer is that in the textually specified matter, the text is authoritative, not the meaning of the text. And the revocably divorced woman is included in 'our women' due to the text, because Allah Most High said: 'And their husbands have more right to take them back.' And this verse was revealed about revocable divorce. And the husband is the ba'l (master). Therefore, the woman, i.e., the revocably divorced woman, is his wife. And whatever ruling applies to the wives, due to 'for those who swear abstinence from their wives', that ruling will also apply to the revocably divorced woman, because the revocably divorced woman is also among the wives.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the validity of ila (an oath to abstain from intercourse) with a revocably divorced woman (mutallaqa raj'iyya). The author states that ila is valid with such a woman because she is still considered a wife textually (by Quranic verses), even though the husband does not have the right to enforce intercourse during her waiting period. The passage clarifies that if the waiting period expires before the four-month ila period, the ila becomes void because the locus (the wife) is gone. An objection is raised that since the revocably divorced woman has no right to intercourse, the husband is not an oppressor, so ila should not apply. The answer is that the text ('our women') includes her because the Quran says 'their husbands are more entitled to take them back', so she remains a wife. Thus the ruling is based on the text, not the underlying rationale.

Key Terms
ایلاء (īlāʾ): An oath to abstain from intercourse with one's wife for a period of four months or more.
مطلقہ رجعیہ (muṭallaqa rajʿiyya): A woman who has received one or two revocable divorces and is still in her waiting period (ʿiddah).

Ila and Zihar with a Non-Wife Before Marriage
Ruling on ila/zihar spoken before marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ila/zihar statements made to an unrelated woman before marriage and apply the distinction between oath and zihar formula regarding expiation.

Core Idea
Words of ila or zihar spoken before marriage are void and never become valid; only a binding oath triggers expiation.

This lesson examines a unique scenario: a man makes a statement of ila or zihar to a woman who is not his wife, then later marries her. Does the statement become operative after marriage? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the absence of the 'locus' (mahall) at the time of utterance. Understanding this ruling clarifies the importance of the legal subject (wife) for these institutions and the distinction between a binding oath and a mere declaration of zihar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two statements
The man says either an oath (wallahi la aqrabuk) or a zihar formula (anti alayya ka zahr ummi). Note the legal nature of each.
The first is a yamin (oath), the second is a declaration of zihar.
2
Assess the locus at time of utterance
The woman is ajnabiyya (not a wife). Ila and zihar require a wife as mahall. Therefore both statements are void (batil) when uttered.
Locus = mahall, the subject of the legal ruling.
3
Consider the effect of subsequent marriage
Marriage after the statement does not retroactively make the statement valid. The void remains void.
The passage compares it to the sale of a dead animal.
4
Determine the binding nature of the oath
The first statement is a validly contracted oath (yamin). The zihar formula is not an oath, so only the first can be broken.
The oath is valid even though ila is not established.
5
Apply the consequence of intercourse
If the man marries and has intercourse, he breaks the oath (hanith) and must pay kaffara. If he used the zihar formula, no expiation is required.
Kaffara for breaking an oath is feeding/clothing 10 poor or fasting 3 days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لیکن اگر اس شخص نے اس عورت کے ساتھ ولی کر لی تو کفارہ واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ولی کرنے سے حانث ہونا پایا گیا اور حانث ہونے کا موجب کفارہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور حانث ہونا اس لئے پایا گیا کہ یمین حانث ہونے کے حق میں منعقد ہو چکی تھی مگر یہ کفارہ کا واجب ہونا اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ اجنبیہ عورت سے واللہ لا اقربک کہا ہو اور اگر اجنبیہ سے انت على كظهر امی کہا اور نکاح کر لینے کے بعد اس سے وطی کر لی تو کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ اول یعنی والله لا اقربک کیمین ہے نہ کلام ثانی ۔
And if he said to an unrelated woman: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' then he married her, he will not be a muli nor a muzahir. And if he said to an unrelated woman: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' then he married her, he will not be a muli nor a muzahir because the speech at its utterance occurred void due to the absence of the locus, so it cannot become valid after that. And if he approaches her, he will pay expiation due to the realization of breaking the oath, because the oath was validly contracted in his regard. Translation: And if he said to an unrelated woman (non-wife): 'I swear by Allah, I will not have intercourse with you' or 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' then he married this woman, then this person will neither be a muli nor a muzahir because the speech at the time of its utterance became futile due to the absence of the locus, so after that this speech cannot turn back and become valid. And if he has intercourse with this woman, he will give expiation, due to the realization of being a breaker of the oath, because the oath was already validly contracted in his regard. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary Urdu Hidayah Volume 5. Explanation: The case is that a person said to an unrelated woman: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' Then that person married this unrelated woman. Then this person will neither be a muli nor a muzahir. The proof is that due to the absence of the locus of ila and zihar, the speech that was uttered became futile at the time of its utterance. Because the locus of ila and zihar is 'our women,' so this became like the sale of a dead animal. Therefore, the speech 'By Allah, I will not approach you' and 'You are to me like the back of my mother' became null and void, and a speech that occurs as null cannot turn back and become valid. For this reason, this speech also cannot turn back and become valid. But if this person has intercourse with this woman, then expiation becomes obligatory. Because by having intercourse, breaking the oath is realized, and the cause of breaking the oath is expiation. For this reason, expiation becomes obligatory. And breaking the oath is realized because the oath was already validly contracted in his regard. But this obligation of expiation is in the case when he said to the unrelated woman: 'By Allah, I will not approach you.' And if he said to the unrelated woman: 'You are to me like the back of my mother' and after marriage he had intercourse with her, then expiation is not obligatory. The reason for the difference is that the first (i.e., 'By Allah, I will not approach you') is an oath, not the second speech.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on ila and zihar when spoken to a woman who is not the speaker's wife. Such statements are void at the time because the locus (a wife) does not exist. Even if he later marries her, the statements do not become ila or zihar. However, if he actually has intercourse with her after marriage, he becomes a breaker of the oath (hanith) and must pay expiation (kaffara) if he had made an oath using 'wallahi la aqrabuk'. But if he used the zihar formula, no expiation is required because it is not a binding oath. The basis is that the speech was void when uttered, and void cannot become valid later.

Key Terms
اجنبیہ (ajnabiyya): A woman who is not the speaker's wife (non-mahram).
یمین (yamīn): An oath, here specifically the statement 'By Allah, I will not approach you'.
حنث (ḥanith): The state of having broken an oath, which triggers the obligation of expiation (kaffara).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to a non-mahram woman 'By Allah, I will not approach you,' then later marries her and has intercourse, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) He becomes a muli
B) He becomes a muzahir
C) He must pay expiation for breaking the oath
D) No expiation is required

Key Takeaway
Ila and zihar statements are only valid when spoken to one's wife; oaths made before marriage are binding and require expiation if broken after marriage.

Duration of Ila for a Slave Woman: Two Months
States Hanafi ruling on ila duration for a slave woman and refutes Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of ila for a slave woman, explain the qiyas to 'iddah, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Hanbali argument.

Core Idea
Ila for a slave woman is two months — slavery halves the separation period, just as it halves 'iddah.

This lesson addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the duration of ila when the wife is a slave. The Hanafi school rules that the period is two months, half of the four months for a free woman, by analogy to the 'iddah. The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools hold that all women are equal in this matter. We will examine the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ila? What is the Hanafi ruling for a slave woman?
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The proof is qiyas to the 'iddah of a slave woman.
The passage explicitly states the analogy: 'like the duration of 'iddah'.
3
Understand the opposing proof
The Shafi'i/Hanbali argue based on the purpose of ila (exposing oppression).
Their proof is that all women are equal in the need to expose oppression.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: the length of the waiting period before separation can be sought.
Hanafi: 2 months; Shafi'i/Hanbali: 4 months.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باندی کے ایلاء کی مدت
ومدة ايلاء الامة شهران لان هذه مدة ضربت اجلاً للبينونة فتتنصف بالرق كمدة العدة ترجمہ اور باندی کے ایلاء کی مدت دو ماہ ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ مدت ایلاء بائنہ ہونے کے لئے میعاد مقرر کی گئی ہے۔ پس وہ رقیق ہونے کی وجہ سے آدھی رہ جائے گی جیسے عدت کی مدت ( کا حال ہے )۔
تشریح:۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ باندی اگر کسی کی بیوی ہو تو اس کے ایلاء کی مدت دو ماہ ہیں اس کا شوہر آزاد ہو یا غلام۔ یہی قول ہے حضرت عمر کا اور امام مالک کا مشہور مذہب یہ ہے کہ غلام کی بیوی کے ایلاء کی مدت دو ماہ ہے اس کی بیوی آزاد ہو یا باندی اور امام شافعی اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ آزاد مرد اور غلام آزاد عورت اور باندی سب برابر ہیں اور تمام کی مدت ایلاء چار ماہ ہے۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدت ایلاء ظالم کی تشہیر کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور اس میں آزاد عورت اور باندی دونوں برابر ہیں۔ کیونکہ حق جماع روک کر دونوں کا شوہر ظالم ہے۔ (عنایہ ) اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدت ایلاء ( چار ماہ) بائنہ ہونے کے لئے مقرر کی گئی ہے۔ پس رقیت کی وجہ سے آدھی رہ جائے گی ۔ جیسا کہ باندی کی طلاق اور اس کی عدت کی مدت آزاد عورت کی طلاق اور اس کی عدت کی مدت کا نصف ہے۔
Duration of ila of a slave woman. And the duration of ila of a slave woman is two months, because this duration is set as a term for separation, so it is halved by slavery, like the duration of 'iddah. Translation: And the duration of ila of a slave woman is two months. Because this ila duration is set as a time limit for becoming separated (bā'in). So due to being a slave, it becomes half, as is the case with the duration of 'iddah. Explanation: They say that if a slave woman is someone's wife, then her ila duration is two months, whether her husband is free or slave. This is the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). And Imam Malik's famous madhhab is that the ila duration of a slave's wife is two months, whether his wife is free or slave. And Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad said that free man and slave, free woman and slave woman are all equal, and all have an ila duration of four months. The proof of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad is that the ila duration is for exposing the oppressor, and in this, free woman and slave woman are equal, because by preventing intercourse, the husband of both is an oppressor. (From 'Inaya). And our proof is that the ila duration (four months) is set for separation. So due to slavery, it becomes half, just as the divorce of a slave woman and her 'iddah duration are half of the divorce of a free woman and her 'iddah duration.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute over the duration of ila for a slave woman. The Hanafi school holds that it is two months, because the primary purpose of the ila period is to set a limit for separation (bainuna), and since a slave woman's rights are half, the period is halved, analogous to 'iddah. The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools argue that ila is to expose the oppressor, so all women are equal in that, thus four months. The Hanafi response uses qiyas (analogy) to the 'iddah of a slave woman, which is also half of a free woman's 'iddah.

Key Terms
أمة (ama): A female slave who is owned and may be married.
رق (riqq): Slavery, a legal status that reduces certain rights and obligations by half.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 1 month
D) 3 months

Key Takeaway
Ila for a slave woman is two months because slavery halves the separation period, just as it halves 'iddah.
