و اذا تشاق الزوجان و خافا ان لا يقيما حدود الله فلا بأس بان تفتدى نفسها منه بمال يخلعها به لقوله تعالى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به فاذا فعل ذلك وقع بالخلع تطليقة بائنة ولزمها المال لقوله عليه السلام الخلع تطليقة بائنة ولأنه يحتمل الطلاق حتى صار من الكنايات والواقع بالكنايات بائن الا ان ذكر المال عن النية هنا ولانها لا تتسلم المال الا لتسلم لها نفسها وذالك بالبينونة اغنى

ترجمہ اور جب میاں بیوی باہم جھگڑا کریں اور دونوں کو یہ ڈر ہو کہ اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ رکھ سکیں گے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو اپنی جان کا فدیہ دے دے ایسے بال کے ساتھ جس کے ذریعہ شوہر اس کو ضلع دیدے۔ دلیل قول باری تعالیٰ فلا جناح علیہما فیما افتقدت به ہے یعنی ان دونوں پر کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو فدیہ دیدے۔ پس جب شوہر اور بیوی نے ایسا کر لیا تو خلع کی وجہ سے ایک طلاق بان واقع ہوگی اور عورت پر مال لازم ہو گا کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ضلع دینا ایک طلاق بائن ہے اور اس لئے کہ ضلع دینا طلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ کنایہ کی طلاقوں میں سے ہو گیا اور کنایات طلاق سے جو طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے وہ بائنہ ہوتی ہے مگر یہاں مال کے ذکر نے نیت سے بے نیاز کر دیا اور اس لئے کہ عورت مال ( کی ذمہ داری قبول نہیں کرتی مگر اس لئے کہ اس کی جان اس کے قبضہ میں ہو جائے اور یہ بائنہ ہونے سے ہوگا۔
Chapter of Khul'. Translation: This chapter is about the rulings of khul'. Explanation: Khul' has been delayed after Ila for two reasons. First, because Ila does not involve wealth, so it is closer to divorce, unlike khul' which involves compensation from the wife. Second, because Ila stems from the husband's nushuz (disobedience), while khul' is based on the wife's nushuz. So what relates to the husband (Ila) is mentioned first, and what relates to the wife (khul') is mentioned later. (from Inayah) A third reason is that Ila is free from wealth, so it is like a simple matter, while khul' involves wealth, so it is like a compound matter, and the simple precedes the compound. The legitimacy of khul' is established by four sources: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, consensus of the Ummah, and rational proof. From the Book of Allah: His statement 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves' meaning that the wife may give a ransom to free herself. From the Sunnah: The story of Jamila bint ‘Abdullah who was under Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas and came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) saying 'I do not criticize Thabit in religion or character, but I fear disbelief in Islam due to my intense hatred of him.' He said: 'Would you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes, and more.' He said: 'As for the extra, no.' This shows that a wife may give compensation to free herself, and this is called khul'. Legitimacy is also established by consensus and rational analogy: the ownership of marriage is analogized to the ownership of retaliation, i.e., just as ownership of retaliation is not property but it is permissible to take compensation for it, similarly, the ownership of marriage is not property but it is permissible to take compensation for it, and giving divorce in exchange for compensation is called khul'. Linguistically, khul' (with damm or fatha on kha) means to remove and take off, as in 'remove your sandals'. But khul' with fatha is used for literal removal, and with damm for metaphorical removal. In Shariah, khul' means taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul'. The conditions of khul' are the same as those of divorce, and its ruling is that a bain divorce occurs. Its description according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that from the husband's side, khul' is an oath, and from the wife's side it is compensation, so the rulings of oath apply to the husband and those of compensation to the wife. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), from both sides, khul' is an oath. If the spouses fear that they cannot maintain the limits of Allah, the wife may ransom herself with wealth to obtain khul'. Proof: the verse 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves'. When the husband does that, a bain divorce occurs and the wife is liable for the wealth, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Khul' is a bain divorce', and because khul' carries the possibility of divorce, thus it is among the kinayat (ambiguous expressions), and divorce through kinayat is bain. But here the mention of wealth dispenses with intention, and because the wife does not accept liability for wealth except to obtain her freedom, which occurs through bain.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the chapter of Khul' (divorce for ransom). It begins by explaining why khul' is placed after Ila in the text: for three reasons—Ila does not involve wealth, Ila stems from the husband's nushuz while khul' from the wife's, and Ila is simple while khul' is compound. The legitimacy of khul' is established by four sources: the Quranic verse 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves', the hadith of Jamila and Thabit, consensus, and rational analogy to the ownership of retaliation (qisas). Linguistically, khul' means 'removal', and in Shariah it is the husband taking wealth from the wife in exchange for ending the marriage using the word khul'. The conditions are the same as those for divorce, and the ruling is that a bain divorce occurs. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa considers khul' as an oath from the husband's side and compensation from the wife's, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it an oath from both sides. The text then presents a matn (core ruling) and its translation: when spouses fear they cannot maintain Allah's limits, the wife may give wealth to obtain khul', which results in a bain divorce. The proof is the Quranic verse, the hadith, and the reasoning that khul' is a kinayah (ambiguous expression) but the mention of wealth makes intention unnecessary.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): In Shariah, khul' is the husband taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul'. It results in a bain divorce.
بینونہ (baynunah): The state of separation after a bain divorce, where the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage contract.
یمین (yameen): An oath by Allah which if broken requires kaffarah. In khul', the husband's statement is akin to an oath according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a source for the legitimacy of khul' according to the text?
A) Quran (2:229)
B) Hadith of Jamila
C) Analogy (Qiyas) to sale of property
D) Consensus (Ijma)

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a valid divorce by mutual consent with compensation, based on Quran, Sunnah, ijma, and analogy to qisas, resulting in a bain divorce where the wife owes the agreed wealth.

The Legal Nature of Khul': Oath or Compensation?
Analyzing the intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the nature of khul' as an oath or compensation, and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa regards khul' as an oath from the husband and compensation from the wife; the Sahibayn differ, affecting the legal consequences.

While khul' is firmly established as a valid transaction leading to bain divorce, its precise legal nature is debated among the early Hanafi authorities. This lesson examines the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students on whether khul' constitutes an oath or a contract of sale. Understanding this dispute deepens our appreciation of how different characterizations affect ancillary rulings.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's view
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that from the husband's side, khul' is an oath (yameen); from the wife's side, it is compensation (mu'awada). Thus, the husband's pronouncement is treated like an oath (requiring kaffarah if broken), while the wife's obligation is contractual.
This view treats the two sides asymmetrically due to the nature of milk al-nikah.
2
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider both sides as oaths. They argue that the transaction is bilateral and each party makes a commitment akin to an oath.
Sahibayn: consensus in the Madhhab that it's an oath from both sides? Actually they differ.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine what difference this makes in practice. If only the husband's side is an oath, then the wife's obligation is not based on oath (so no kaffarah for her if she fails to pay? Actually she must pay; but the nature affects whether intention is needed for the husband's statement). According to the text, the mention of wealth dispenses with intention (niyyah). Under the Sahibayn's view, both sides would require intention as oaths.
The text implies that under Abu Hanifa's view, the husband's statement is a kinayah, but the mention of wealth makes it clear. Under Sahibayn, both sides need intention? Not explicitly stated.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand that later Hanafi scholarship prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's view as reflected in Al-Hidayah and other authoritative works. The mufta bihi position is that from the husband's side it is an oath and from the wife's side it is compensation.
This is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah and the detailed analysis of the proofs.

بــــاب الــخــلــع
ترجمہ (یہ ) باب (احکام ) خلع کے ( بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح ضلع کو ایلاء سے دو وجہوں سے موخر کیا گیا ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ ایلاء میں مال نہیں ہوتا اس لئے وہ طلاق سے زیادہ قریب ہے اس کے برخلاف ضلع کہ اس میں عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ کے معنی موجود ہیں۔ دوم یہ کہ ایلاء کا معنی شوہر کی جانب سے نشوز اور نافرمانی کا جذبہ ہے اور ضلع کا مبنی عورت کی جانب سے نشوز اور نافرمانی کا جذبہ ہے پس جس چیز کا تعلق مرد کے ساتھ ہے یعنی ایلاء اس کو پہلے بیان کیا ہے اور جس چیز کا تعلق عورت کے ساتھ ہے یعنی خلع اس کو بعد میں بیان کیا ہے۔ (عنایه) تیسری وجہ یہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ ایلاء مال سے خالی ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بمنزلہ مفرد کے ہے اور ضلع عورت کی جانب سے مال ہوتا ہے اس لئے وہ بمنزلہ مرکب کے ہے اور چونکہ مفرد مقدم ہوتا ہے مرکب پر اس لئے ایلاء کو پہلے بیان کیا گیا اور خلع کو بعد میں ۔ اور خلع کی مشروعیت کتاب اللہ ، سنت، اجماع امت اور دلیل عقلی چاروں سے ثابت ہے۔ کتاب اللہ مثلاً باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے۔ فلا جناح عليها فيما افتدت به یعنی ان دونوں پر کوئی مضائقہ نہیں اس بارے میں کہ عورت فدیہ دے دے ( اپنی جان کا ) الوسنت رسول یہ ہے، ان جميلة كانت تحت ثابت بن قيس بن شماس فجائت الى رسول الله وقالت لا اعيب على ثابت في دين ولا خلق و لكنى اخشى الكفر في الاسلام لشدة بغضى اياه فقال علیه السلام اتر دین عليه حديقته فقالت نعم و زيادة فقال عليه السلام اما الزيادة فلا یعنی جمیلہ نامی عورت ثابت بن قیس بن شماس کے نکاح میں تھی وہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس آکر کہنے لگی کہ میں ثابت کو اس کے دین و اخلاق میں برانہیں کہتی ہوں لیکن میں نفاق مع الاسلام سے ڈرتی ہوں اس لئے کہ مجھ کو اس سے انتہائی نفرت ہے۔

آپ نے فرمایا کہ کیا تو اس کو اس کا باغ واپس کر دے گی اس نے کہا جی ہاں! اور زیادہ بھی۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ زیادہ کی تو ضرورت نہیں۔

اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ عورت اپنے آپ کو آزاد کرانے کے لئے اپنی طرف سے عوض دے سکتی ہے اور اسی کا نام ضلع ہے اور ضلع کی مشروعیت پر اجماع امت بھی ہے اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ملک نکاح کو قیاس کیا گیا ہے ملک قصاص پر یعنی جس طرح ملک قصاص مال نہیں مگر اس کا عوض لینا جائز ہے اس طرح ملک نکاح بھی اگر چہ مال نہیں ہے لیکن اس کا عوض لینا جائز ہے اور عوض لے کر طلاق دینا ہی ضلع کہلاتا ہے۔ لغوی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ضلع نام ہے ان کے قول خلعت المراة زوجہا اور اختلعت منہ بمالیا کا خلع بضم الخاء اور فتح الخاء دونوں طرح آیا ہے معنی ہیں نزع یعنی الگ کرنا اور نکال ڈالنا۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول فاخلع نعلیک یعنی اپنے دونوں جوتوں کو نکال ڈال ۔ مگر خلع بفتح الخاء نزع حقیقی کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اور ضلع بالضم نزع مجازی کے لئے ۔

شریعت میں ضلع کہتے ہیں عورت سے لفظ ضلع کے ساتھ ملک نکاح کے مقابلہ میں مال لینا اور خلع کی شرط وہ ہے جو طلاق کی شرط ہے اور اس کا حکم طلاق بائن کا واقع ہونا ہے اور اس کی صفت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ شوہر کی طرف سے خلع یمین ہے اور عورت کی طرف سے معاوضہ لہذا شوہر کی جانب سے یمین کے احکام کی رعایت کی جائے گی اور عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ کے احکام کی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں جانب سے خلع یمین ہے۔

میاں بیوی کو جھگڑے کا خوف ہو کہ ایک دوسرے کے حقوق ادا نہیں کر سکیں گے تو عورت مال دے کر خلع کر سکتی ہے
و اذا تشاق الزوجان و خافا ان لا يقيما حدود الله فلا بأس بان تفتدى نفسها منه بمال يخلعها به لقوله تعالى فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به فاذا فعل ذلك وقع بالخلع تطليقة بائنة ولزمها المال لقوله عليه السلام الخلع تطليقة بائنة ولأنه يحتمل الطلاق حتى صار من الكنايات والواقع بالكنايات بائن الا ان ذكر المال عن النية هنا ولانها لا تتسلم المال الا لتسلم لها نفسها وذالك بالبينونة اغنى

ترجمہ اور جب میاں بیوی باہم جھگڑا کریں اور دونوں کو یہ ڈر ہو کہ اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ رکھ سکیں گے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو اپنی جان کا فدیہ دے دے ایسے بال کے ساتھ جس کے ذریعہ شوہر اس کو ضلع دیدے۔ دلیل قول باری تعالیٰ فلا جناح علیہما فیما افتقدت به ہے یعنی ان دونوں پر کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو فدیہ دیدے۔ پس جب شوہر اور بیوی نے ایسا کر لیا تو خلع کی وجہ سے ایک طلاق بان واقع ہوگی اور عورت پر مال لازم ہو گا کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ضلع دینا ایک طلاق بائن ہے اور اس لئے کہ ضلع دینا طلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ کنایہ کی طلاقوں میں سے ہو گیا اور کنایات طلاق سے جو طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے وہ بائنہ ہوتی ہے مگر یہاں مال کے ذکر نے نیت سے بے نیاز کر دیا اور اس لئے کہ عورت مال ( کی ذمہ داری قبول نہیں کرتی مگر اس لئے کہ اس کی جان اس کے قبضہ میں ہو جائے اور یہ بائنہ ہونے سے ہوگا۔
Chapter of Khul'. Translation: This chapter is about the rulings of khul'. Explanation: Khul' has been delayed after Ila for two reasons. First, because Ila does not involve wealth, so it is closer to divorce, unlike khul' which involves compensation from the wife. Second, because Ila stems from the husband's nushuz (disobedience), while khul' is based on the wife's nushuz. So what relates to the husband (Ila) is mentioned first, and what relates to the wife (khul') is mentioned later. (from Inayah) A third reason is that Ila is free from wealth, so it is like a simple matter, while khul' involves wealth, so it is like a compound matter, and the simple precedes the compound. The legitimacy of khul' is established by four sources: the Book of Allah, the Sunnah, consensus of the Ummah, and rational proof. From the Book of Allah: His statement 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves' meaning that the wife may give a ransom to free herself. From the Sunnah: The story of Jamila bint ‘Abdullah who was under Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas and came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) saying 'I do not criticize Thabit in religion or character, but I fear disbelief in Islam due to my intense hatred of him.' He said: 'Would you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes, and more.' He said: 'As for the extra, no.' This shows that a wife may give compensation to free herself, and this is called khul'. Legitimacy is also established by consensus and rational analogy: the ownership of marriage is analogized to the ownership of retaliation, i.e., just as ownership of retaliation is not property but it is permissible to take compensation for it, similarly, the ownership of marriage is not property but it is permissible to take compensation for it, and giving divorce in exchange for compensation is called khul'. Linguistically, khul' (with damm or fatha on kha) means to remove and take off, as in 'remove your sandals'. But khul' with fatha is used for literal removal, and with damm for metaphorical removal. In Shariah, khul' means taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul'. The conditions of khul' are the same as those of divorce, and its ruling is that a bain divorce occurs. Its description according to Imam Abu Hanifa is that from the husband's side, khul' is an oath, and from the wife's side it is compensation, so the rulings of oath apply to the husband and those of compensation to the wife. According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), from both sides, khul' is an oath. If the spouses fear that they cannot maintain the limits of Allah, the wife may ransom herself with wealth to obtain khul'. Proof: the verse 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves'. When the husband does that, a bain divorce occurs and the wife is liable for the wealth, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Khul' is a bain divorce', and because khul' carries the possibility of divorce, thus it is among the kinayat (ambiguous expressions), and divorce through kinayat is bain. But here the mention of wealth dispenses with intention, and because the wife does not accept liability for wealth except to obtain her freedom, which occurs through bain.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the chapter of Khul' (divorce for ransom). It begins by explaining why khul' is placed after Ila in the text: for three reasons—Ila does not involve wealth, Ila stems from the husband's nushuz while khul' from the wife's, and Ila is simple while khul' is compound. The legitimacy of khul' is established by four sources: the Quranic verse 'there is no sin upon them if they ransom themselves', the hadith of Jamila and Thabit, consensus, and rational analogy to the ownership of retaliation (qisas). Linguistically, khul' means 'removal', and in Shariah it is the husband taking wealth from the wife in exchange for ending the marriage using the word khul'. The conditions are the same as those for divorce, and the ruling is that a bain divorce occurs. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa considers khul' as an oath from the husband's side and compensation from the wife's, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it an oath from both sides. The text then presents a matn (core ruling) and its translation: when spouses fear they cannot maintain Allah's limits, the wife may give wealth to obtain khul', which results in a bain divorce. The proof is the Quranic verse, the hadith, and the reasoning that khul' is a kinayah (ambiguous expression) but the mention of wealth makes intention unnecessary.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): In Shariah, khul' is the husband taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul'. It results in a bain divorce.
یمین (yameen): An oath by Allah which if broken requires kaffarah. In khul', the husband's statement is akin to an oath according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
معاوضة (mu'awada): Compensation or exchange, akin to a contract of sale. In khul', the wife's payment is considered mu'awada according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the nature of khul' from the wife's side?
A) It is an oath (yameen).
B) It is compensation (mu'awada).
C) It is a gift (hiba).
D) It is a conditional divorce.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the dispute on the nature of khul' by preferring Imam Abu Hanifa's view that it is an oath for the husband and compensation for the wife, affecting the need for intention and the categorization of the wife's obligation.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Khul': Definition, Proofs, and Ruling
Defines khul', presents proofs, and states ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of khul', identify the primary proofs (Quran, hadith, ijma, qiyas), and explain why it results in one talaq ba'in in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Khul' is a form of divorce initiated by the wife with compensation, resulting in one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in).

In this lesson, we examine the classic Hanafi ruling on khul' (divorce by redemption). We begin with its linguistic and legal definition, then explore the proofs that establish its legitimacy: a clear Quranic verse, a prophetic hadith, consensus of the Ummah, and a rational analogy to the ownership of retaliation. The lesson concludes with the ruling that khul' effects one talaq ba'in and obligates the wife to pay the agreed compensation.

Guided Path
1
Define the Act
Read the passage and isolate the legal definition of khul': 'taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul' or its equivalent.'
Note the linguistic shift from literal removal (khul' with fatha) to legal removal (khul' with damm).
2
Identify the Primary Proofs
Locate the Quranic verse (2:229), the hadith (khul' is a talaq ba'in), the statement of ijma, and the qiyas to qisas. For each, note the type of evidence and its weight.
The Quranic proof is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala; the hadith is ahad but sufficient.
3
Derive the Ruling
From the proofs, conclude that khul' is legitimate and results in one talaq ba'in. The wife's compensation becomes wajib.
The ruling is based on the combination of textual and rational proofs.
4
Connect to Kinayah Divorces
Understand why khul' is classified as a kinayah (ambiguous) divorce. Note that the mention of mal (wealth) dispenses with the need for explicit intention.
Kinayah divorces normally require intention, but the mention of compensation substitutes for it.
5
Summarize the Legal Effect
State the outcome: one talaq ba'in immediately, and the wife must pay the compensation.
The divorce is effective upon the husband's declaration and acceptance of the compensation.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ حالت منهم [؟]
آپ نے فرمایا کہ کیا تو اس کو اس کا باغ واپس کر دے گی اس نے کہا جی ہاں! اور زیادہ بھی۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ زیادہ کی تو ضرورت نہیں۔
اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ عورت اپنے آپ کو آزاد کرانے کے لئے اپنی طرف سے عوض دے سکتی ہے اور اسی کا نام ضلع ہے اور ضلع کی مشروعیت پر اجماع امت بھی ہے اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ملک نکاح کو قیاس کیا گیا ہے ملک قصاص پر یعنی جس طرح ملک قصاص مال نہیں مگر اس کا عوض لینا جائز ہے اس طرح ملک نکاح بھی اگر چہ مال نہیں ہے لیکن اس کا عوض لینا جائز ہے اور عوض لے کر طلاق دینا ہی ضلع کہلاتا ہے۔ لغوی تحقیق یہ ہے کہ ضلع نام ہے ان کے قول خلعت المراة زوجہا اور اختلعت منہ بمالیا کا خلع بضم الخاء اور فتح الخاء دونوں طرح آیا ہے معنی ہیں نزع یعنی الگ کرنا اور نکال ڈالنا۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول فاخلع نعلیک یعنی اپنے دونوں جوتوں کو نکال ڈال۔ مگر خلع بفتح الخاء نزع حقیقی کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اور ضلع بالضم نزع مجازی کے لئے۔
شریعت میں ضلع کہتے ہیں عورت سے لفظ ضلع کے ساتھ ملک نکاح کے مقابلہ میں مال لینا اور خلع کی شرط وہ ہے جو طلاق کی شرط ہے اور اس کا حکم طلاق بائن کا واقع ہونا ہے اور اس کی صفت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ شوہر کی طرف سے خلع یمین ہے اور عورت کی طرف سے معاوضہ لہذا شوہر کی جانب سے یمین کے احکام کی رعایت کی جائے گی اور عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ کے احکام کی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دونوں جانب سے خلع یمین ہے۔

میاں بیوی کو جھگڑے کا خوف ہو کہ ایک دوسرے کے حقوق ادا نہیں کر سکیں گے تو عورت مال دے کر خلع کر سکتی ہے

اغنى
ترجمہ اور جب میاں بیوی باہم جھگڑا کریں اور دونوں کو یہ ڈر ہو کہ اللہ کی حدود کو قائم نہ رکھ سکیں گے تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو اپنی جان کا فدیہ دے دے ایسے بال کے ساتھ جس کے ذریعہ شوہر اس کو ضلع دیدے۔ دلیل قول باری تعالیٰ فلا جناح علیہما فیما افتتدت به ہے یعنی ان دونوں پر کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اس کو فدیہ دیدے۔ پس جب شوہر اور بیوی نے ایسا کر لیا تو خلع کی وجہ سے ایک طلاق بان واقع ہوگی اور عورت پر مال لازم ہو گا کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ضلع دینا ایک طلاق بائن ہے اور اس لئے کہ ضلع دینا طلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے یہاں تک کہ وہ کنایہ کی طلاقوں میں سے ہو گیا اور کنایات طلاق سے جو طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے وہ بائنہ ہوتی ہے مگر یہاں مال کے ذکر نے نیت سے بے نیاز کر دیا اور اس لئے کہ عورت مال ( کی ذمہ داری قبول نہیں کرتی مگر اس لئے کہ اس کی جان اس کے قبضہ میں ہو جائے اور یہ بائنہ ہونے سے ہوگا۔
Chapter of Khul'. Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary of Bidayah. He said: Will you return his garden to him? She said: Yes, and more. He said: There is no need for more. From this verse and hadith it is known that a woman can give compensation from herself to free herself, and this is called khul'. There is ijma of the Ummah on its legitimacy. Rational proof: the ownership of marriage is analogized to the ownership of retaliation (qisas); just as ownership of retaliation is not property but taking compensation for it is permissible, similarly ownership of marriage is not property but taking compensation for it is permissible, and giving divorce in exchange for compensation is called khul'. Linguistic investigation: khul' is derived from 'khala'at al-mar'atu zawjaha' and 'ikhtala'at minhu bi malin'; it comes with damm and fatha on the kha, meaning removal and extraction, like Allah's saying 'Fakhla' na'layka' (So take off your sandals). But khul' with fatha is used for literal removal, and with damm for metaphorical removal. In Shariah, khul' means taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul'. Its condition is the same as for divorce, and its ruling is the occurrence of a revocable divorce (talaq ba'in). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, its nature is: from the husband's side it is an oath (yamin), and from the wife's side it is a compensation (mu'awada). Therefore, from the husband's side the rules of oaths are observed, and from the wife's side the rules of compensation. According to the two disciples (Sahibayn), khul' is an oath from both sides. When the spouses quarrel and fear that they cannot uphold Allah's limits, the woman can give compensation and the husband can give khul'. Allah says: 'There is no blame on them for that by which she ransoms herself.' So when they do this, one irrevocable divorce occurs by khul', and the wealth becomes obligatory on her. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce.' And because khul' admits divorce such that it becomes from the kinayah (ambiguous) divorces, and what occurs by kinayah is irrevocable, but the mention of wealth dispenses with the need for intention here. And because the woman does not accept the wealth except for her self to become free, and that is by irrevocability.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the topic of khul'. It begins by defining khul' both linguistically and legally, establishing its legitimacy through Quran (Surah al-Baqarah 2:229), hadith, ijma, and rational analogy to qisas. The ruling is that khul' results in one talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce). The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa considers khul' from the husband's side to be an oath (yamin) and from the wife's side a compensation (mu'awada), whereas the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it an oath from both sides. This difference affects the application of rules regarding oaths and compensation. The passage also explains that khul' is from the category of kinayah (ambiguous) divorces, where intention is normally required, but the mention of the compensation (mal) serves as a substitute for intention, making the divorce effective without express intention. The core idea is that khul' is a legitimate form of divorce initiated by the wife with compensation, resulting in one irrevocable divorce.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): In Shariah, taking wealth from the wife in exchange for the ownership of marriage using the word khul' or equivalent, resulting in divorce.
تطليقة بائنة (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, but allows remarriage without a new nikah only if the couple recontract.
یمین (yamin): An oath; in context of khul', it refers to a declaration that effects divorce, subject to rules of oaths.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One talaq raj'i (revocable divorce)
B) One talaq ba'in (irrevocable divorce)
C) Faskh (annulment)
D) No divorce occurs until the husband expresses intention

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a legitimate form of divorce where the wife offers compensation, resulting in one talaq ba'in and an obligatory payment.

Talaq — Divorce

The Nature of Khul': Oath or Compensation? Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether khul' is an oath (yamin) from both sides or only from the husband's side, and evaluate the practical implications of each view.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa considers khul' an oath from the husband and compensation from the wife; the Sahibayn consider it an oath from both—a difference that affects the ruling on oath-breaking.

While the Hanafi school agrees that khul' results in one talaq ba'in, there is an important internal difference about its legal nature. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that from the husband's side it is an oath (yamin), and from the wife's side it is a compensation (mu'awada). The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is an oath from both sides. This lesson explores the basis of each view and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Point
What exactly is contested: the nature of khul' from each party's perspective. Is the wife's offer an oath or a compensation?
The validity of khul' itself is not disputed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's View
Explain that the husband's declaration is a yamin (subject to oath rules) and the wife's payment is a compensation (subject to contract rules).
Oath rules include kaffarah for breaking; compensation rules focus on the transfer of wealth.
3
State the Sahibayn's View
They consider both sides as yamin, so both parties are subject to oath rules.
This view treats khul' as a mutual dissolution akin to a shared oath.
4
Analyze the Practical Difference
For example, if the husband breaks an oath after khul', what are the consequences? Under Abu Hanifa, the husband would be liable for kaffarah only if he intended an oath; under Sahibayn, the wife would also be bound by oath rules.
The difference only emerges when oath-related issues arise.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon view is Imam Abu Hanifa's, as stated by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
This is the standard fatwa position.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Khul': Talaq or Faskh?
Presents and rebuts Shafi'i argument that khul' is faskh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khul', explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the difference.

Core Idea
Khul' is talaq ba'in, not faskh, because a complete marriage does not admit annulment.

This lesson examines the disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the legal nature of khul'. While both agree on its permissibility, they differ on whether it constitutes a divorce (talaq) or an annulment (faskh). The consequence is crucial for counting divorces and the establishment of permanent prohibition (hurmah ghalizah). We will walk through the proofs and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school considers khul' to be one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in). The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce.'
Talaq ba'in causes immediate separation but does not reduce the number of future divorces to zero; it consumes one of three.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that khul' is faskh (annulment) of the marriage contract, not a divorce. This means it does not count toward the three divorces.
Faskh dissolves the marriage without affecting the divorce count.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on the Quranic sequence (al-Baqarah 2:229): first 'divorce is twice', then 'no blame on them for ransom', then 'if he divorces her, she is not lawful until she marries another'. Counting khul' as divorce would make four. Also, marriage is a contract like sale, admitting faskh by mutual consent (present in khul' but not in divorce).
The sequence is interpreted as a chronological order by Shafi'i.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the Quranic sequence does not imply chronological order; it only mentions different rulings. Moreover, marriage after consummation is a complete contract that does not admit faskh. Options like khiyar al-'ayb apply before completion, not after.
The hadith explicitly states khul' is talaq; rational analogy (qiyas) is overridden by istihsan based on the clear text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a couple performs khul' after two divorces, in the Hanafi school this counts as a third divorce, making the wife permanently prohibited (hurmah ghalizah) until she marries another. In the Shafi'i view, it does not count as a divorce, so the husband retains one remaining divorce option.
This is the key practical difference that affects real-life fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الخلع
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین باہم جھگڑا کرنے لگیں اور یہ محسوس کر لیں کہ اب اللہ کے حدود یعنی حقوق زوجیت ادا نہیں کرسکیں گے۔ تو اس بارے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اپنی جان کا اپنے شوہر کو فدیہ دیدے اور شوہر اس مال کے بدلے اس کو بذریعہ ضلع طلاق دیدے۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ہے۔ آیت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مرد پر کوئی گناہ نہیں فدیہ لینے میں اور عورت پر کوئی گناہ نہیں فدیہ دینے میں ۔ یہ فدیہ دینا عورت کی جانب سے در حقیقت اپنے آپ کو قید سے رہا کرانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ عورتیں اپنے شوہروں کے پاس قیدیوں کے درجہ میں ہوتی ہیں۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے عورتوں کا نام اساری (قیدی ) ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے اتقوا الله فى النساء فانهن عندكم عوان یعنی عورتوں کے بارے میں اللہ سے ڈرو، اس لئے کہ وہ تمھارے پاس قیدی ہیں۔ ( ترندی منقول از مینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور جار اللہ بخشتری نے بیان کیا ہے کہ یہ آیت فلا جناح الآية ثابت اور ان کی بیوی کے سلسلہ میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور یہ اسلام میں سب سے پہلے ضلع تھا۔ یہ حدیث باب الخلع کے تحت تفصیل کے ساتھ ذکر کر دی گئی ہے۔ معینی نے ثابت کی بیوی کے تین نام ذکر کئے ہیں (۱) حبیبہ (۲) حمیلہ (۳) جمیلہ ۔ جواز ضلع میں علاوہ امام مزنی کے کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اصحاب ظواہر نے دو شرطوں کے ساتھ ضلع کی اجازت دی ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ عورت اپنے شوہر سے نفرت کا اظہار کرے دوم یہ کہ عورت کو یہ خوف ہو کہ حقوق زوجیت ادا نہیں ہو سکیں گے اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ ضلع صرف بادشاہ کی اجازت سے جائز ہے اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ خلع صرف اس صورت میں جائز ہے جب عورت شوہر کی اطاعت کا انکار کر دے اور یہ کہہ دے کہ میں تیرے لئے غسل جنابت نہیں کروں گی اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ ضلع اس صورت میں جائز ہے جب نافرمانی اور اعراض کا مظاہرہ ہونے لگے۔
جب میاں بیوی نے یہ کام کر ڈالا یعنی بیوی نے فدیہ دے دیا اور شوہر نے ضلع کر دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے عورت پر ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر مال واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ ہے کہ ضلع فسخ نکاح ہے طلاق نہیں ۔ شمرہ اختلاف اس مسئلہ میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ اگر کسی شخص نے دو طلاقوں کے بعد ضلع کیا تو احناف کے نزدیک حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جائے گی اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک حرمت غلیظہ ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خدا وند قدوس نے مسئلہ طلاق کو اس ترتیب کے ساتھ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ سب سے پہلے فرمایا الطلاق مرتان پھر فرمایا: فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت بد یعنی مسئلہ خلع کو پھر اس کے بعد فرمایا فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنكح زوجا غیرہ ۔ اب اگر مذہب احناف کے مطابق ضلع کو طلاق مان لیا جائے تو طلاقیں چار ہو جائیں گی حالانکہ طلاقیں صرف تین مشروع کی گئی ہیں پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلع طلاق نہیں ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح بیع کی طرح عقد ہے اور عقد فسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ حتی کہ خیار عدم کفاء ۔ خیار عیب اور خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے تمھارے نزدیک بھی نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ نکاح فسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور فسخ کے لئے رضا مندی ضروری ہے اور باہمی رضامندی صرف ضلع میں ہوتی ہے نہ کہ طلاق میں اس وجہ سے ضلع فسخ نکاح ہوگا نہ کہ طلاق ۔
ہماری دلیل حدیث ہے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الخلع تطلیقة بائنہ دوسری دلیل اور امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نکاح تمام اور مکمل ہونے کے بعد فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا در خیار عدم كفاءة خیار عیب اور خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے فسخ قبل التمام ہے نہ کہ بعد
Chapter of Khul'. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 5. Explanation of the case: If the spouses quarrel and realize they cannot uphold Allah's limits (marital rights), then there is no harm if the woman ransoms herself from her husband with wealth, and the husband divorces her by khul' in exchange for that wealth. Proof: Allah's saying 'There is no blame on them for that by which she ransoms herself.' The meaning is that there is no sin on the man in taking the ransom, and no sin on the woman in giving it. Paying ransom is in fact for the woman to free herself from captivity, because women are like captives with their husbands. The Prophet (peace be upon him) referred to women as 'asara (captives). He said: 'Fear Allah regarding women, for they are captives with you.' This verse was revealed concerning Thabit and his wife, and this was the first khul' in Islam. The hadith is mentioned in detail under this chapter. Ma'ini mentioned three names of Thabit's wife: (1) Habiba, (2) Humayla, (3) Jameela. There is no disagreement on the permissibility of khul' except for Imam al-Muzani. However, the Zahiri scholars permit it with two conditions: (1) the woman shows hatred for her husband, and (2) she fears inability to fulfill marital rights. One group says khul' is only permissible with the ruler's permission. Another says it is only permissible if the woman refuses obedience and says 'I will not perform ghusl of janaba for you.' Another says it is permissible when disobedience and aversion become apparent. When the spouses do this, one irrevocable divorce occurs and the wealth becomes obligatory on the woman. Imam Shafi'i has a saying that khul' is faskh of the marriage, not divorce. The consequence of this difference appears if a person performs khul' after two divorces: according to the Hanafis, the third divorce (ghalizah) is established, while according to Shafi'i, it is not established. Imam Shafi'i's proof: Allah mentioned divorce in order: first 'Divorce is twice', then 'There is no blame on them for that by which she ransoms herself' (the issue of khul'), then after that 'If he divorces her, she is not lawful for him until she marries another husband.' If khul' is counted as divorce according to the Hanafis, then there would be four divorces, while only three are legislated. Thus khul' is not divorce. His second proof: Marriage is a contract like sale, and a contract admits annulment (faskh). Even in your school, marriage is annulled due to option of unsuitability (khiyar al-kafa'a), option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), and option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh). Thus it is established that marriage admits faskh, and mutual consent is necessary for faskh, and mutual consent only occurs in khul', not in divorce. Therefore khul' is faskh, not divorce. Our proof: The hadith 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce.' And the answer to Shafi'i's rational proof is that marriage, after it is complete and perfect, does not admit faskh; the options of unsuitability, defect, and puberty result in faskh before completion, not after.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the legal nature of khul'. The Hanafi position, as established earlier, is that khul' is a form of divorce (talaq) resulting in one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in). Imam Shafi'i, however, considers khul' to be an annulment (faskh) of the marriage contract, not a divorce. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is significant: if a man has already given two divorces and then performs khul', the Hanafi school counts this as a third divorce, making the wife permanently prohibited (hurmah ghalizah) until she marries another. In the Shafi'i view, since khul' is faskh, it does not consume a divorce, so the husband retains one remaining divorce. The passage presents two Shafi'i proofs: (1) the sequential arrangement in the Quran suggests khul' is between the 'twice' and the 'if he divorces her' clause, so counting khul' as a divorce would lead to four divorces; (2) marriage is a contract that admits faskh through various options, and mutual consent (present in khul') is characteristic of faskh, not talaq. The Hanafi response to the first proof is that the Quranic sequence does not necessarily imply chronology; rather, khul' is a type of talaq, and the 'if he divorces her' refers to a divorce after the two, so there is no need for a fourth. The Hanafi response to the second proof is that marriage, once complete and consummated, does not admit faskh except in cases of defects present at the time of contract (khiyar al-'ayb, etc.), which are considered before completion. After completion, only divorce can dissolve the marriage. The core idea is that the Hanafi school defends the position that khul' is talaq ba'in, not faskh.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of a contract; in context of nikah, dissolution of marriage without divorce, not reducing the number of divorces.
حرمت غلیظہ (hurmah ghalizah): A severe prohibition; after three divorces, the wife becomes permanently prohibited to the husband until she marries another.
خیار (khiyar): Option or right to annul a contract upon discovering a defect or lack of suitability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the nature of khul'?
A) Khul' is valid only with the ruler's permission.
B) After two talags, khul' counts as a third divorce in the Hanafi school but not in the Shafi'i school.
C) Khul' requires witnesses.
D) Khul' cannot be done during pregnancy.

Key Takeaway
Understanding whether khul' is talaq or faskh directly impacts the count of divorces and the establishment of permanent prohibition (hurmah ghalizah).

Definition and Permissibility of Khul'
Defines khul' and cites its Quranic proof, then discusses variant conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of khul', identify its primary Quranic proof, and explain the Hanafi position that it is permissible without restrictive conditions.

Core Idea
Khul' is a permissible divorce initiated by the wife with compensation; the Quran clearly permits it.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of khul'—a form of divorce where the wife offers compensation to her husband to obtain her release. The Hanafi school holds that khul' is permissible whenever the spouses genuinely fear they cannot maintain marital limits, without requiring additional conditions. We will examine the primary proof from the Quran (Al-Baqarah 2:229) and the historical case of Thabit ibn Qays, which established the practice. Understanding this ruling is essential for differentiating the unconditional Hanafi view from stricter positions of other madhahib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of khul'
Khul' is divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (fidyah) given to the husband. The scenario: spouses quarrel and fear they cannot uphold Allah's limits (marital rights).
The compensation can be more or less than the mahr.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse Al-Baqarah 2:229: 'فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به' (There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with).
This verse was revealed regarding Thabit ibn Qays and his wife, the first khul' in Islam.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'fala junaha' (no sin) indicates permissibility. The general wording 'fima iftadat bih' covers any agreed compensation, making khul' lawful without sin.
The negation of sin establishes permissibility (ibahah) in Hanafi usul.
4
Contrast with restrictive views
Other schools impose conditions: Zahiris require hatred and fear of transgression; some require king's permission; others require refusal of obedience. Hanafi school does not impose these conditions—khul' is permissible as long as both spouses agree.
Imam Muzani (Shafi'i) is reported to have dissented on permissibility itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الخلع
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین با ہم جھگڑا کرنے لگیں اور یہ محسوس کر لیں کہ اب اللہ کے حدود یعنی حقوق زوجیت ادا نہیں کرسکیں گے۔ تو اس بارے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ عورت اپنی جان کا اپنے شوہر کو فدیہ دیدے اور شوہر اس مال کے بدلے اس کو بذریعہ ضلع طلاق دیدے۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت به ہے۔ آیت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مرد پر کوئی گناہ نہیں فدیہ لینے میں اور عورت پر کوئی گناہ نہیں فدیہ دینے میں ۔ یہ فدیہ دینا عورت کی جانب سے در حقیقت اپنے آپ کو قید سے رہا کرانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ عورتیں اپنے شوہروں کے پاس قیدیوں کے درجہ میں ہوتی ہیں۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے عورتوں کا نام اساری (قیدی ) ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ ارشاد ہے اتقوا الله فى النساء فانهن عندكم عوان یعنی عورتوں کے بارے میں اللہ سے ڈرو، اس لئے کہ وہ تمھارے پاس قیدی ہیں۔ ( ترندی منقول از مینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور جار اللہ بخشتری نے بیان کیا ہے کہ یہ آیت فلا جناح الآية ثابت اور ان کی بیوی کے سلسلہ میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور یہ اسلام میں سب سے پہلے ضلع تھا۔ یہ حدیث باب الخلع کے تحت تفصیل کے ساتھ ذکر کر دی گئی ہے۔ معینی نے ثابت کی بیوی کے تین نام ذکر کئے ہیں (۱) حبیبہ (۲) حمیلہ (۳) جمیلہ ۔ جواز ضلع میں علاوہ امام مزنی کے کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اصحاب ظواہر نے دو شرطوں کے ساتھ ضلع کی اجازت دی ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ عورت اپنے شوہر سے نفرت کا اظہار کرے دوم یہ کہ عورت کو یہ خوف ہو کہ حقوق زوجیت ادا نہیں ہو سکیں گے اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ ضلع صرف بادشاہ کی اجازت سے جائز ہے اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ خلع صرف اس صورت میں جائز ہے جب عورت شوہر کی اطاعت کا انکار کر دے اور یہ کہہ دے کہ میں تیرے لئے غسل جنابت نہیں کروں گی اور ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ ضلع اس صورت میں جائز ہے جب نافرمانی اور اعراض کا مظاہرہ ہونے لگے۔
Chapter of Khul'. The explanation of the issue is that if spouses start quarrelling and realize that they cannot uphold Allah's limits (i.e., marital rights), then there is no harm if the woman gives her husband a ransom (fidyah) for herself, and the husband divorces her in exchange for that property. The proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with.' The meaning of the verse is that there is no sin on the man in taking the ransom and no sin on the woman in giving it. This giving of ransom by the woman is essentially to free herself from captivity, because women are in the position of captives with their husbands, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) described women as captives (asara). He said: 'Fear Allah regarding women, for they are captives with you.' (Tirmidhi, quoted from Mini Sharh Hidayah). And Jalal al-Din al-Bukhari stated that this verse (Fala junaha...) was revealed concerning Thabit and his wife, and this was the first khul' in Islam. This hadith is mentioned in detail under this chapter. Ma'ini mentioned three names of Thabit's wife: (1) Habibah, (2) Humaylah, (3) Jamilah. There is no disagreement regarding the permissibility of khul' except from Imam Muzani. However, the Zahiri scholars permitted khul' with two conditions: first, the woman expresses hatred toward her husband; second, she fears she cannot fulfil marital rights. One group held that khul' is only permissible with the king's permission. Another group held that khul' is only permissible when the woman refuses obedience and says she will not perform ghusl for him. Another group held that khul' is permissible when disobedience and aversion manifest.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on khul' by defining the scenario in which khul' is legislated. When marital discord reaches a point where both spouses fear they cannot maintain the limits set by Allah—meaning they cannot fulfil the rights of marriage—then it is permissible for the wife to offer compensation (fidyah) to her husband in exchange for her release, and for the husband to accept it and give her a divorce. The primary proof is the Quranic verse in Surah al-Baqarah (2:229): 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with.' The author explains that this verse was revealed concerning the case of Thabit ibn Qays and his wife, which was the first instance of khul' in Islam. The wife came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) complaining that she disliked her husband's appearance and could not fulfil his rights, so the Prophet instructed her to return the garden her husband had given her as mahr, after which the Prophet separated them with a single divorce. The author further supports the permissibility by citing the hadith that women are captives (asara) with their husbands, meaning they are bound to marriage and may seek release through khul'. Thus, khul' is a form of ransom to free oneself. The author notes that there is near-consensus on the permissibility of khul'; only Imam Muzani disagreed. Various later groups imposed conditions: the Zahiris required both hatred and fear of transgression; others required the wife's explicit refusal of obedience; yet others required royal permission. The Hanafi position, however, does not restrict khul' to these conditions—it is permissible whenever the spouses genuinely fear they cannot maintain marital limits.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (fidyah) given to the husband.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation paid by the wife to the husband in a khul' divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 'And if you fear a breach between them, appoint an arbiter'
B) 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with'
C) 'Divorce is twice, then retention in honor or release in kindness'
D) 'And do not take anything from what you have given them'

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a permissible divorce by compensation, proven by Quran 2:229, and the Hanafi school does not impose additional restrictive conditions.

Is Khul' a Divorce or Annulment? Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents Shafi'i view that khul' is faskh and Hanafi rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that khul' is a bain talaq and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using textual and rational proofs.

Core Idea
Khul' is a bain divorce per Hanafi school based on explicit hadith; Shafi'i considers it an annulment.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does khul' dissolve the marriage as a divorce (talaq) or as an annulment (faskh)? The Hanafi school rules that khul' constitutes one bain talaq, while Imam al-Shafi'i (in one opinion) considers it a faskh. The difference is not merely academic—it has profound practical consequences, especially when determining whether a third divorce has occurred. Let us walk through the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its direct proof
Begin by identifying the Hanafi position: khul' results in one bain talaq. Note the proof: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which explicitly calls khul' a 'bain talaq'.
This is a clear nass (text) that the Hanafis prioritize over qiyas.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its two proofs
The Shafi'i argument has two parts: (1) The Quranic ordering of divorce verses would imply four divorces if khul' were talaq, contradicting the limit of three. (2) Marriage is a contract that can be annulled (faskh) due to defects or mutual consent, so mutual consent in khul' indicates faskh.
These are rational and textual proofs that challenge the Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each Shafi'i proof
First rebuttal: The hadith overrides qiyas. Second rebuttal: The options (kufu', defect, puberty) operate before marriage is complete—they prevent completion, not annul a completed contract. Khul' occurs after completion, so it must be talaq (severance). Third rebuttal: The Quranic verses describe the same third divorce in two modes (with and without compensation), not two separate divorces.
The Hanafi response uses an analogy: describing a pen as 'with price' or 'by price' does not multiply the pen.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a man divorces his wife twice and then performs khul', the Hanafi school counts this as the third divorce, leading to hurmat ghalizah (irrevocable prohibition). The Shafi'i school does not count it as a third divorce, so the wife can remarry the same husband without tahlil.
This difference directly affects the permissibility of remarriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب میاں بیوی نے یہ کام کر ڈالا یعنی بیوی نے فدیہ دے دیا اور شوہر نے ضلع کر دیا تو اس کی وجہ سے عورت پر ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر مال واجب ہوگا اور امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ ہے کہ ضلع فسخ نکاح ہے طلاق نہیں ۔ شمرہ اختلاف اس مسئلہ میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ اگر کسی شخص نے دو طلاقوں کے بعد ضلع کیا تو احناف کے نزدیک حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جائے گی اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک حرمت خلیفہ ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خدا وند قدوس نے مسئلہ طلاق کو اس ترتیب کے ساتھ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ سب سے پہلے فرمایا الطلاق مرتان پھر فرمایا: فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت بد یعنی مسئلہ خلع کو پھر اس کے بعد فرمایا فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتى تنکح زوجا غیرہ ۔ اب اگر مذہب احناف کے مطابق ضلع کو طلاق مان لیا جائے تو طلاقیں چار ہو جائیں گی حالانکہ طلاقیں صرف تین مشروع کی گئی ہیں پس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خلع طلاق نہیں ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح بیع کی طرح عقد ہے اور عقد منح کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ حتی کہ خیار عدم کفا ء ۔ خیار حق اور خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے تمھارے نزدیک بھی نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ نکاح فسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور نسخ کے لئے رضا مندی ضروری ہے اور باہمی رضامندی صرف ضلع میں ہوتی ہے نہ کہ طلاق میں اس وجہ سے ضلع فسخ نکاح ہوگا نہ کہ طلاق ۔
ہماری دلیل حدیث ہے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الخلع تطلیقہ بائنہ دوسری دلیل اور امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نکاح ۔ تمام اور مکمل ہونے کے بعد فتح کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا در خیر عدم كفاءة خیار حق اور خیار بلوغ کی وجہ سے صبح قبل التمام ہے نہ کہ بعد التمام ۔ لہذا ان تینوں کی وجہ سے اتمام نکاح سے رکھنا کہلائے گا نہ کہ نسخ کرنا اور رہ ضلع تو وہ تمام عقد کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور نکاح تمام عقد کے بعد فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا اس وجہ سے ضلع کو فسخ نکاح قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا۔ البتہ نکاح تمام ہونے کے بعد قطع فی الحال کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہماری درخواست ہے کہ ضلع سے رفع قید اور قطع نکاح کے معنی مراد لئے جائیں اور رفع قید اور قطع نکاح نام ہے طلاق کا ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ خلع طلاق ہے نہ کہ نسخ۔
اور رہا امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ خلع کو طلاق ماننے کی صورت میں طلاقیں چار ہو جاتی ہیں تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ذکر فرمایا کہ تیسری طلاق بعوض ہو یا بغیر عوض اس کے بعد عورت کے لئے حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ طلاق بعوض کو فلا جناح عليهما فيما افتدت بہ کے ساتھ ذکر فرمایا ہے اور طلاق بغیر عوض کو فان طلقها الآیه کے ساتھ حاصل یہ کہ اگر ایک چیز کو دو طرح سے بیان کر دیا جائے تو وہ ایک ہی چیز رہتی ہے دو نہیں ہو جاتی ۔ مثلاً آپ اپنے دوست سے کہیں کہ یہ قلم دید و قیمت دید یا با قیمتا تو قلم ایک ہی رہے گا۔ دو طرح ذکر کر دینے سے دو نہیں ہوں گے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ فلا جناح الآية اور فان طلقها الآیة میں ایک ہی طلاق مذکور ہے نہ کہ دو پس اس تقریر کی بنیاد پر طلاقیں تین ہوں گی نہ کہ چار۔
When the husband and wife have done this—i.e., the wife gave the ransom and the husband performed khul'—then as a result one bain talaq will occur to the woman, and the property becomes obligatory on the woman. Imam al-Shafi'i has one saying that khul' is an annulment (faskh) of the marriage, not a divorce. The fruit of this difference will appear in this issue: if a person performed khul' after two divorces, then according to the Hanafis, irrevocable prohibition (hurmat ghalizah) becomes established, whereas according to Imam al-Shafi'i, irrevocable prohibition will not be established. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that Allah Most High mentioned the matter of divorce in this order: first He said 'Divorce is twice,' then He said 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with'—the issue of khul'—then after that He said 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband.' Now if, according to the Hanafi school, khul' is considered a divorce, then divorces would become four, whereas only three divorces have been legislated. So this indicates that khul' is not a divorce. The second proof is that marriage is a contract like sale, and a contract can be subject to rescission (faskh). Even according to you, marriage is annulled due to option of lack of equality, option of defect, and option of puberty. So it is established that marriage can be annulled, and annulment requires mutual consent. Mutual consent only occurs in khul', not in talaq. Therefore, khul' is an annulment, not a divorce. Our proof is the hadith: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Al-Khul' is a bain talaq.' The second proof is the response to Imam al-Shafi'i's rational proof: Marriage, after it is complete and concluded, does not admit faskh. The option of lack of equality, option of defect, and option of puberty occur before completion (qabl al-tamam), not after. Therefore, due to these three, it is called preventing completion, not annulling. As for khul', it occurs after the contract is complete, and marriage after completion does not admit faskh. Therefore, khul' cannot be considered an annulment. However, marriage after completion can admit immediate severance (qat' fi al-hal). Therefore, we maintain that from khul' the meaning of removal of restraint and cutting of marriage is intended, and removal of restraint and cutting of marriage is called talaq. So it is established that khul' is a divorce, not an annulment. As for Imam al-Shafi'i's claim that if khul' is considered a divorce, then divorces become four, the response is: Allah mentioned that after the third divorce, whether with compensation or without, irrevocable prohibition becomes established. Divorce with compensation is mentioned with 'Fala junaha...' and divorce without compensation with 'Then if he divorces her...' The gist is that if one thing is described in two ways, it remains one thing, not two. For example, if you say to your friend, 'Take this pen with price' or 'Take it for a price,' the pen remains one. Describing it in two ways does not make two. So it is established that in the verse 'Fala junaha...' and the verse 'Then if he divorces her...' one same divorce is mentioned, not two. Therefore, based on this reasoning, the divorces are three, not four.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a full inter-madhhab dispute. The text first states the Hanafi ruling that khul' results in one bain talaq. Then it introduces Imam al-Shafi'i's dissenting view that khul' is an annulment (faskh) of the marriage, not a divorce. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is highlighted: if a man who has already given two divorces subsequently performs khul', the Hanafi school holds that the third divorce is now effective, resulting in irrevocable prohibition (hurmat ghalizah, meaning the wife becomes completely forbidden unless she marries another and is divorced). The Shafi'i school, considering khul' an annulment, would not count it as a third divorce, so prohibition does not occur. The text then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's two proofs: (1) The Quranic order of verses—'Divorce is twice' (2:229), then the khul' verse, then 'Then if he divorces her...' (2:230). If khul' were a divorce, it would be a fourth mention, contradicting the limit of three. (2) Marriage is a contract that can be annulled due to defects, so khul' being mutual consent is essentially faskh. The Hanafi response is two-fold: (a) The Prophet's hadith explicitly calls khul' a 'bain talaq,' which is a direct textual proof overriding qiyas. (b) Regarding the Shafi'i rational proof: marriage, after it is fully concluded, does not admit faskh; the options mentioned (kufu', defect, puberty) operate before the contract is complete, not after—they prevent completion, not annul a completed contract. Khul' occurs after marriage is complete, so it cannot be faskh. However, marriage after completion admits 'qat' fi al-hal' (immediate severance), which is the essence of talaq. Therefore, khul' is talaq. To the objection that this would create four divorces, the Hanafi response is that the Quranic verses are describing the same third divorce in two ways—with compensation (khul') and without compensation (regular talaq)—so the count remains three. The author illustrates with an analogy: saying 'take this pen with a price' or 'take this pen by price' does not create two pens.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract due to a defect or mutual agreement, without counting as a divorce.
بائن (ba'in): A divorce that is final and cannot be revoked (without a new marriage contract).
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in return for compensation (fidyah) paid to the husband.
حرمت غلیظہ (hurmat ghalizah): Irrevocable prohibition that occurs after three divorces, making the wife unlawful until she marries another and is divorced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute on whether khul' is talaq or faskh?
A) Validity of marriage after khul'
B) Count of divorces: if two divorces precede khul', Hanafi says third divorce occurs; Shafi'i says it does not
C) Amount of compensation due
D) Whether khul' requires witnesses

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a bain talaq in the Hanafi school based on the explicit hadith, and this classification has significant practical consequences for counting divorces and subsequent remarriage.

Two Hanafi Proofs that Khul' is Bain Talaq
Proofs that khul' is bain talaq from al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi proofs that khul' results in bain talaq and explain why intention is not required when compensation is mentioned.

Core Idea
Khul' is bain talaq because the word is kinayah and compensation specifies intent; full surrender requires irrevocable divorce.

The passage from Al-Hidayah presents two additional proofs for the Hanafi position that khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation) results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce. The first proof relies on the classification of 'khul'' as a kinayah (allusive) word, combined with the mention of compensation, which removes any ambiguity. The second proof argues that the wife's assumption of liability for compensation requires her complete release from the marriage, which only a bain talaq can provide. These proofs fortify the Hanafi stance against objections, particularly from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
Read the passage and identify the two distinct proofs offered by the author of Hidayah. The first involves linguistic analysis (kinayah and specification via mal). The second involves a logical inference about the wife's surrender.
2
Analyze the first proof
Why is khul' considered a kinayah word? What does the word 'khul'' literally mean? How does the mention of compensation (mal) remove the need for separate intention? Trace the reasoning.
The text explains that 'khul'' can mean removing clothes, removing goodness, or emerging from marriage. Mentioning mal specifies the marital meaning.
3
Analyze the second proof
What is the premise that the wife assumes liability for compensation only when her 'self' is fully surrendered? Why can this surrender only happen through bain talaq, not raj'i?
Raj'i talaq leaves the wife in a revocable state; the husband can take her back without a new contract. This partial surrender is insufficient for the full transfer of liability.
4
Synthesize the ruling
Combine both proofs to state the final Hanafi ruling: Khul' results in one bain talaq. Explain how the proofs respond to potential objections (e.g., that kinayah requires intention).
The first proof answers the intention objection; the second proof confirms the irrevocable nature of the divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے خلع کے ذریعہ طلاق بائن واقع ہونے کی دو دلیلیں اور ذکر فرمائی ہیں ایک یہ کہ لفظ ضلع طلاق کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا خالعتک یا خلعتک اور طلاق کی نیت کی تو ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ لفظ خلع کنایات طلاق میں سے ہے اور الفاظ کنایہ کے ساتھ طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے سوائے تین کلمات کئے انت واحد ة، اعتدى، استبرئی رحمک“۔
لا ان ذكر المال سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جب لفظ ضلع الفاظ کنایہ میں سے ہے تو اس میں نیت شرط ہونی چاہیے حالانکہ ضلع میں نیت شرط نہیں ہے جو اب لفظ ضلع چند معنی کا احتمال رکھتا ہے (۱) کپڑوں سے نکلنا (۲) بھلائیوں سے نکلنا (۳) نکاح سے
نکلنا۔ پس جب مال یعنی بدل خلع ذکر کر دیا گیا تو نکاح سے نکلنے کے معنی متعین ہو گئے اس وجہ سے نیت کی ضرورت باقی نہیں رہی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت مال کی ذمہ داری اس وقت قبول کرے گی جب اس کا نفس بالکلیہ اس کے سپرد کر دیا جائے اور عمارت کے واسطے اس کے نفس کی سپردگی صرف طلاق بائن سے ہو سکتی ہے نہ کہ طلاق رجعی سے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ خلع طلاق بائن ہے نہ کہ
طلاق رجعی ۔
The author of Hidayah mentioned two proofs for the occurrence of bain talaq through khul'. One is that the word khul' has the probability of divorce. For example, if a man said to his wife 'khal'atuk' or 'khala'tuk' and intended divorce, then one bain talaq will occur. The summary is that the word khul' is among the kinayah (allusive) words of divorce, and with kinayah words, bain talaq occurs, except for three words: 'i'taddi', 'asta'brid rahimak'. The phrase 'illa bi dhikr al-mal' is an answer to a question. The question is: When the word khul' is among kinayah words, then intention should be a condition, yet in khul' intention is not a condition. This is because the word khul' has several meanings: (1) to remove clothes, (2) to remove goodness, (3) to emerge from marriage. So when the property (i.e., the compensation for khul') is mentioned, the meaning of emerging from marriage becomes specified. Therefore, the need for intention is removed. The second proof is that the woman assumes liability for the property only when her self is completely surrendered to him, and the complete surrender of her self can only occur through bain talaq, not raj'i talaq. Therefore, we say that khul' is bain talaq, not raj'i talaq.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage presents two additional Hanafi proofs that khul' results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce, not a raj'i (revocable) one. The first proof: The word 'khul'' is a kinayah (allusive) word for divorce. In Hanafi law, when a kinayah word is used with the intention of divorce, it effects one bain talaq. However, since khul' is commonly used for separation, and the compensation (mal) is explicitly mentioned, the intention is automatically fulfilled—no separate intent is needed because the context specifies that the couple intends separation. The author explains that the word 'khul'' literally means 'to take off' (like removing a garment), but it can also mean 'to emerge from marriage' (nikah). When the compensation is mentioned, the marital meaning is determined. The second proof: The wife agrees to pay compensation only when she is fully freed from the marriage bond. That full freedom is achieved only through a bain talaq, which completely severs the marriage. A raj'i talaq leaves the woman in a waiting period during which the husband can take her back without a new contract; that does not constitute full surrender of her self. Therefore, khul' must be bain. These proofs solidify the Hanafi position and respond to potential objections about the need for intention in kinayah words.

Key Terms
کنایہ (kinayah): Allusive expression; a word that is not explicit for divorce but implies it. In Hanafi law, using kinayah with intention effects a bain talaq.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot take the wife back without a new contract and mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because khul' is explicit for divorce
B) Because the compensation specifies the marital meaning
C) Because the wife's consent replaces intention
D) Because the Prophet (SAW) said so

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that khul' results in a bain talaq because the word 'khul'' is kinayah for divorce and the mention of compensation removes any ambiguity, and because only a bain talaq provides the full surrender needed for the wife's liability.

When the Husband is at Fault: Taking Compensation in Khul'
States the ruling and proof for husband's nushuz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when nushuz is from the husband and explain the Quranic proof for it being makruh.

Core Idea
Taking compensation in khul' when the husband is at fault is makruh, not haram.

You already know that when a wife initiates khul' due to nushuz from her side, the husband may take compensation. But what if the husband is the one at fault? This lesson addresses that scenario: the husband cannot take compensation without it being disliked (makruh). Let's examine the Quranic basis and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the husband taking compensation (badal khul') when the discord (nushuz) originates from him. The ruling is makruh (disliked). Identify which type of makruh: here it is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), not tahrimi.
The term 'makruh' in Hanafi fiqh is distinct from haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 4:20-21, which forbids taking back anything from the wife when the husband wishes to exchange her without fault. The verse is quoted: '...do not take anything from it.'
Dalil is qat'i al-thubut (Quran) but zanni al-dalala (interpretation).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse explicitly prohibits taking back mahr when the husband is at fault. By analogy (qiyas), in khul' when the husband is the cause of discord, taking compensation is similarly discouraged. The additional principle: the husband has already alienated the wife by seeking to replace her; taking wealth would increase that alienation.
The reasoning is based on avoiding further harm (la yazid fi wahshatiha bil-mal).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (outside Hanafi) consider it haram to take compensation when the husband is at fault. The Hanafi school distinguishes between haram and makruh, holding it as makruh tanzihi.
This difference affects the sinfulness but not the validity of the khul'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that it is makruh for the husband to take compensation. The khul' itself is valid and the talaq takes effect, but the husband's act of taking money is disliked.
This ruling encourages justice: the wrongdoer should not profit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سرکشی شوہر کی جانب سے ہو تو اس کیلئے بدل خلع لینا مکروہ ہے
وان كان النشوز من قبله يكره له ان ياخذمنها عوضا لقوله تعالى وان اردتم استبدال زوج مكان زوج الى ان قال فلانا خذوامنه شيئا ولانه اوحشها بالاستبدال فلايزيدفي وحشتها باخذ المال
ترجمہ اور اگر سرکشی شوہر کی جانب سے ہو تو شوہر کے لئے مکروہ ہے کہ بیوی سے عوض لے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ہے اگر تم ایک بیوی کی جگہ دوسری بدلنا چاہو ، یہاں تک کہ فرمایا تو اس میں سے کچھ مت لو اور اس لئے کہ شوہر نے بیوی بدلنے کے ساتھ اس کو وحشت میں ڈال دیا تو مال لے کر اس کی وحشت میں اضافہ نہ کرے۔
If the nushuz (disobedience/discord) is from the husband's side, then for him it is makruh to take compensation from her. Because Allah Most High said: 'If you wish to exchange a wife in place of another... up to His saying: do not take anything from it.' And because he has alienated her by exchanging, so he should not increase her alienation by taking wealth.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage states a distinct ruling: when the discord (nushuz) originates from the husband—meaning he is the one at fault—it is makruh (disliked) for him to accept any compensation from the wife in a khul' divorce. The proof is from the Quranic verse (4:20-21): 'If you wish to exchange a wife in place of another, and you have given one of them a great amount, do not take anything from it. Would you take it by falsehood and manifest sin?' The verse forbids taking back any portion of the mahr when the husband wants to replace a wife without fault. By analogy, in khul' when the husband is the wrongdoer, taking compensation is makruh because it increases the wife's hardship. The author adds that since the husband has already alienated (awhasha) his wife by seeking to replace her, taking money adds to that alienation, which is not commendable. This ruling is consistent with the spirit of the Quranic prohibition on taking back gifts in divorce, but note: the khul' is still valid and the talaq occurs, but the husband's act is makruh.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Discord or rebellion between spouses, whether from husband or wife. Here it refers to the husband being the cause of the marital breakdown.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not haram but is discouraged. The Hanafi school distinguishes between makruh tahrimi (close to haram) and makruh tanzihi (lighter disliked). Here it is likely tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Mandatory (wajib)
C) Disliked (makruh)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
When nushuz is from the husband, it is makruh (disliked) for him to take compensation in a khul' divorce, based on Quran 4:20-21 and the principle of avoiding increased alienation.

Khula' Is Talaq, Not Faskh: Refutation of Shafi'i
Explaining that khula' is talaq and not faskh, refuting Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that khula' is talaq ba'in and refute the Shafi'i argument that it increases the count of talaqs to four using Quranic and usul evidence.

Core Idea
Khula' is talaq ba'in, not faskh, and it does not increase the count of three talaqs.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani tackles a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of khula'. The Shafi'is argue that if khula' were talaq, it would add a fourth permissible divorce, contradicting the Quranic limit. The Hanafi response demonstrates that the same talaq is expressed in two ways in the Quran, preserving the count of three. We will walk through the Hanafi proofs and see how they establish that khula' is an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds khula' to be talaq ba'in, not faskh. Understand that khula' occurs after marriage completion and does not admit annulment (naskh).
The passage begins by asserting that khula' is talaq because marriage after completion cannot be annulled.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if khula' is talaq, then the total number of permissible divorces would become four (three regular plus one khula'), exceeding the Quranic limit.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opponent's proof
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the verses about talaq with compensation (fala junaha) and without compensation (fa in tallaqaha) refer to the same single talaq expressed in two ways. The analogy of a pen mentioned with or without its price illustrates this point.
The key usul point: expressing one thing in two ways does not create two separate things.
4
Examine the two proofs that khula' results in talaq ba'in
Understand the first proof: the word 'khula' is kinayah for talaq, and mentioning the compensation (badal) specifies the meaning of divorce, eliminating the need for intention (niyyah). The second proof: the wife accepts liability only when her self is fully entrusted to the husband, which only talaq ba'in achieves.
The passage notes that tiga kinayah words (anti wahidah, i'taddi, istabri'i rahimik) are exceptions where talaq ba'in does not occur.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: in the Hanafi school, khula' counts as one of the three talaqs and is irrevocable (ba'in). In the Shafi'i school, khula' is annulment and does not count towards the three talaqs.

Source Text
